Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
10 min
Jihad as a Collective Obligation and Offensive Fighting
Opening of Kitab al-Siyar stating jihad's legal status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jihad as fard kifayah and explain the evidence for offensive fighting against disbelievers.

Core Idea
Jihad is a communal duty; failing it by all brings sin. Fighting disbelievers is wajib even without attack.

This opening of Kitab al-Siyar in Al-Quduri establishes two foundational rulings: jihad is a collective obligation (fard kifayah), and combatting disbelievers is obligatory (wajib) even if they do not initiate aggression. The author provides multiple proofs from the Quran and Sunnah to ground these rulings. In this lesson, we will unpack the legal classification, the evidence, and the practical consequences for the Muslim community.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage states two distinct but related rules: (1) Jihad is fard kifayah. (2) Fighting the disbelievers is wajib upon us even if they do not start hostilities. Note the different legal categories: fard kifayah vs. wajib.
Fard kifayah is a communal obligation; wajib here is a personal obligation that may become fard ayn under certain conditions.
2
Understand fard kifayah and its consequence
Fard kifayah means if a sufficient number of Muslims perform it, the rest are absolved. If no one performs it, the entire community sins. This is derived from the verse and hadith that indicate not all believers need to go forth, but a group should.
The sin is collective when the obligation is completely neglected.
3
Analyze the evidence for each ruling
For jihad as fard kifayah: Quran 9:122 (not all go forth), hadith of Jabir (a group always fights), hadith of Ibn Abbas (respond when summoned). For offensive fighting: Quran 4:89 (seize and kill those who turn away), Quran 9:36 (fight polytheists all together), hadith of Abu Hurairah (attack on Jews without prior aggression).
The hadith of the Prophet's attack on the Jews of Medina without their initiation is key: it establishes an offensive obligation.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a peaceful Muslim community with no external threat. According to the Hanafi ruling, they are still obligated to maintain a military capacity (fard kifayah) and the ruler must initiate campaigns periodically (wajib) unless there is a valid reason to delay (e.g., treaty).
The obligation is not suspended simply because there is peace; it is ongoing due to the command to fight until disbelief is no longer dominant (as inferred from other texts).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

لثبوت الْجِهَادُ فَرْضٌ عَلَى الْكِفَايَةِ أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ جَابِرَ بْنَ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ يَقُولُ: سمعت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول تَزَالُ طَائِفَةٌ مِنْ أُمَّتِي يُقَاتِلُونَ عَلَى الحَقِّ ظَاهِرِينَ إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ، (مسلم شریف، باب نزول عيسى بن مَرْيَمَ حَاكِمًا بِشَرِيعَةِ نَبِيِّنَا مُحَمَّدٍ ، نمبر 156/سنن ابوداود . بَابٌ في دَوَامِ الْجَهَادِ، نمبر 2484) وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت الْجِهَادُ فَرْضٌ عَلَى الْكِفَايَةِ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ الله : « لَا هِجْرَةَ بَعْدَ الْفَتْح وَلَكِنْ جِهَادٌ وَنِيَّةٌ وَإِذَا اسْتَنْفِرْتُمْ فَانْفِرُوا (بخاري شريف كِتَابُ الْجِهَادِ وَالسَّيَرِ، غير 2784 / مسلم شريف بَاب الْمُبَايَعَةِ بَعْدَ فَتْح مَكَّةَ، غير 1864) لوجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَقِتَالُ الْكُفَّارِ وَاجِبٌ عَلَيْنَا وَإِنْ لَمْ يَبْدَءُونَا ﴿فَإِن تَوَلَّوْا فَخُذُوهُمْ وَاقْتُلُوهُمْ حَيْثُ وَجَدتُّمُوهُمْ وَلَا تَتَّخِذُواْ مِنْهُمْ وَلِيًّا وَلَا نَصِيرًا﴾ (سورة النساء، 4 أيت، نمبر 89) وجه:(۲) الآية لثبوت وَقِتَالُ الْكُفَّارِ وَاجِبٌ عَلَيْنَا وَإِنْ لَمْ يَبْدَءُونَا ﴿وَقَتِلُواْ الْمُشْرِكِينَ كَافَّةً كَمَا يُقَتِلُونَكُمْ كَافَّةً وَاعْلَمُوا أَنَّ اللَّهَ مَعَ الْمُتَّقِينَ (سورة التوبة، 9 أيت، نمبر 36) وجه:(۳) الحديث لثبوت وَقِتَالُ الْكُفَّارِ وَاجِبٌ عَلَيْنَا وَإِنْ لَمْ يَبْدَءُونَا عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، أَنَّهُ قَالَ: بَيْنَا نَحْنُ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ إِذْ خَرَجَ إِلَيْنَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ، فَقَالَ: «انْطَلِقُوا إِلَى يَهُودَ» فَخَرَجْنَا مَعَهُ حَتَّى جِئْنَاهُمْ، فَقَامَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَنَادَاهُمْ، فَقَالَ: «يَا مَعْشَرَ يَهُودَ، أَسْلِمُوا تَسْلَمُوا... وَإِنِّي أُرِيدُ أَنْ أُجْلِيَكُمْ مِنْ هَذِهِ الْأَرْضِ ، سنن ابوداود، بَابُ كَيْفَ كَانَ إِخْرَاجُ الْيَهُودِ مِنَ الْمَدِينَةِ، نمبر 3003) اصول شریعت میں سیر کہتے ہیں کہ نبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی جہاد میں کیا عادت شریفہ تھی۔
Book of Siyar (Military Expeditions). He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him - Jihad is a collective obligation (fard kifayah); when a group of people undertakes it, it is lifted from the rest. If no one undertakes it, all people sin by leaving it. Fighting the disbelievers is obligatory upon us even if they do not start (fighting) against us. Evidence (1) The verse for establishing that jihad is a collective obligation: [Quran 9:122] 'And it is not for the believers to go forth all together. So why does not a party from every section go forth to gain understanding in religion and to warn their people when they return, that they may beware?' Evidence (2) The hadith for establishing that jihad is a collective obligation: Jabir ibn Abdullah heard the Prophet (peace be upon him) say: 'A group of my ummah will continue to fight for the truth, dominant until the Day of Judgment.' (Muslim, Bab Nuzul Isa; Abu Dawud, Bab Dawam al-Jihad) Evidence (3) The hadith from Ibn Abbas: The Prophet said: 'There is no hijra after the conquest, but jihad and intention. And when you are summoned (to fight), go forth.' (Bukhari, Kitab al-Jihad; Muslim, Bab al-Mubaya'a) Evidence for the obligation of fighting disbelievers even if they do not start: (1) The verse: [Quran 4:89] 'So if they turn away, then seize them and kill them wherever you find them, and take not from among them any ally or helper.' (2) The verse: [Quran 9:36] 'And fight the polytheists all together as they fight you all together.' (3) The hadith from Abu Hurairah: The Prophet said: 'Go to the Jews' and then called them: 'O Jews, embrace Islam and you will be safe... Indeed I intend to expel you from this land.' (Abu Dawud, Bab Kayfa Kana Ikhraj al-Yahud) In the principles of Shariah, 'Siyar' refers to the noble practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in jihad.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This is the opening of Kitab al-Siyar from Al-Quduri. The author begins by defining the legal status of jihad: it is fard kifayah (a collective obligation). If a sufficient number of Muslims undertake it, the obligation is lifted from the rest. If no one undertakes it, the entire community is sinful. The commentator provides three proofs: Quran 9:122 (which implies not all need to go), the hadith of Jabir about a group always fighting for the truth, and the hadith of Ibn Abbas about responding to the call. The passage then addresses fighting the disbelievers: it is wajib (obligatory) even if they do not initiate aggression. The proofs: Quran 4:89 (seize and kill those who turn away), Quran 9:36 (fight them all together), and the hadith of Abu Hurairah where the Prophet ordered attack on the Jews of Medina without prior aggression. The passage ends with a definition of 'Siyar' as the prophetic practice in jihad.

Key Terms
الجهاد (al-jihad): Struggle in the path of Allah, primarily military effort against disbelievers.
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): A communal obligation; if a sufficient number perform it, the rest are absolved; if none, all sin.
السير (al-siyar): The prophetic practice and rulings regarding military expeditions and conduct in jihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for the Muslim community if no one undertakes jihad?
A) The obligation is lifted entirely.
B) The entire community becomes sinful.
C) Only the ruler sins.
D) It is permissible to leave it if there is peace.

Key Takeaway
Jihad is a communal obligation; fighting disbelievers is wajib even without provocation, supported by explicit Quranic and Prophetic evidence.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
beginner
6 min
Jihad is a Communal Obligation (Fard Kifayah)
Ruling with three proofs from Quran and Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that jihad is fard kifayah and identify its three proofs from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Jihad is fard kifayah: if some do it, all are absolved; if none, all sin.

In this passage, Al-Quduri delivers a concise ruling that jihad is a communal obligation, not an individual one. He then backs it with three clear proofs from the Quran and Hadith. Understanding this classification is key to grasping the collective responsibility of the Muslim community in defending and upholding Islam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its definition
Read the first line: 'al-jihādu farḍun ʿalā al-kifāyah'. Recognize that fard kifayah means if a sufficient number perform it, the obligation drops from the rest; otherwise all are sinful.
Contrast with fard 'ayn which is mandatory on every individual.
2
Understand the consequence
If a group undertakes jihad, the duty lifts from others. If no one does it, the entire community commits a sin by abandoning it.
This differentiates fard kifayah from other types of obligations.
3
Analyze the first proof: Quran 9:122
The verse says not all believers should go forth; a party from each section should go to gain religious knowledge and warn others. This implies that a group suffices, so the duty is collective, not individual.
The indication (dalala) is zanni but strong.
4
Analyze the second proof: Hadith of Jabir
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said a group of his community will continue to fight for the truth until the Day of Judgment. This shows that jihad will always be performed by some, thus it is a collective obligation.
The existence of a continuous group proves that it is not required of every individual.
5
Analyze the third proof: Hadith of Ibn Abbas
The Prophet said: 'There is no emigration after the conquest, but there is jihad and intention. When you are called to arms, go forth.' The command 'when called' implies a collective call, so it is a communal duty to respond.
This hadith also emphasizes that jihad remains after the conquest of Mecca.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - الْجِهَادُ فَرْضٌ عَلَى الْكِفَايَةِ إِذَا قَامَ بِهِ فَرِيقٌ مِنْ النَّاسِ سَقَطَ عَنْ الْبَاقِينَ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَقُمْ بِهِ أَحَدٌ أَثِمَ جَمِيعُ النَّاسِ بِتَرْكِهِ . وَقِتَالُ الْكُفَّارِ وَاجِبٌ عَلَيْنَا وَإِنْ لَمْ يَبْدَءُونَا ل وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت الْجِهَادُ فَرْضٌ عَلَى الْكِفَايَةِ \ ﴿وَمَا كَانَ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ لِيَنفِرُوا كَافَّةً فَلَوْلَا نَفَرَ مِن كُلِّ فِرْقَةٍ مِّنْهُمْ طَائِفَةٌ لِيَتَفَقَّهُوا فِي الدِّينِ وَلِيُنذِرُوا قَوْمَهُمْ إِذَا رَجَعُواْ إِلَيْهِمْ لَعَلَّهُمْ يَحْذَرُونَ﴾ (سورة التوبة، 9آيت نمبر 122) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت الْجِهَادُ فَرْضٌ عَلَى الْكِفَايَةِ \ أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ جَابِرَ بْنَ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ يَقُولُ: سمعت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول تَزَالُ طَائِفَةٌ مِنْ أُمَّتِي يُقَاتِلُونَ عَلَى الحَقِّ ظَاهِرِينَ إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ، (مسلم شریف، باب نزول عيسى بن مَرْيَمَ حَاكِمًا بِشَرِيعَةِ نَبِيِّنَا مُحَمَّدٍ ، نمبر 156/سنن ابوداود . بَابٌ في دَوَامِ الْجَهَادِ، نمبر 2484) وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت الْجِهَادُ فَرْضٌ عَلَى الْكِفَايَةِ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ الله : « لَا هِجْرَةَ بَعْدَ الْفَتْح وَلَكِنْ جِهَادٌ وَنِيَّةٌ وَإِذَا اسْتَنْفِرْتُمْ فَانْفِرُوا (بخاري شريف كِتَابُ الْجِهَادِ وَالسَّيَرِ، غير 2784 / مسلم شريف بَاب الْمُبَايَعَةِ بَعْدَ فَتْح مَكَّةَ، غير 1864)
He (Al-Quduri) said - may Allah have mercy on him - Jihad is a communal obligation (fard kifayah). If a group of people undertakes it, it falls from the rest. If no one undertakes it, all the people sin by abandoning it. Fighting the disbelievers is obligatory upon us even if they do not initiate. (1) The verse proving that jihad is fard kifayah: {And the believers should not go forth all together; why then does not a party from every section of them go forth to become learned in religion and warn their people when they return to them so that they may beware?} (Surah at-Tawbah, 9:122). (2) The hadith proving that jihad is fard kifayah: He heard Jabir ibn Abdullah say: I heard the Prophet (peace be upon him) say: 'A group of my community will continue to fight for the truth, dominant until the Day of Judgment.' (Muslim, Chapter of the Descent of Jesus son of Mary as a judge by the law of our Prophet Muhammad, no. 156 / Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter on the Permanence of Jihad, no. 2484). (3) The hadith proving that jihad is fard kifayah: From Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no emigration after the conquest, but there is jihad and intention. When you are called to arms, go forth.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Book of Jihad and Siyar, no. 2784 / Muslim, Chapter of the Pledge after the Conquest of Mecca, no. 1864).
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn (Al-Quduri) that jihad is a communal obligation (fard kifayah), meaning if a sufficient number of Muslims engage in it, the obligation is lifted from the rest. However, if no one performs it, the entire community bears sin. The author then provides three pieces of evidence (wujuh) from the Quran and Sunnah to substantiate this ruling. The first evidence is the Quranic verse (9:122) which indicates that it is not required for all believers to go forth; rather, a group should go to gain religious knowledge and warn others, implying that jihad (and by extension, learning) is a collective duty. The second evidence is the hadith of Jabir about a group continuously fighting for truth, showing that jihad will always be performed by some, thus it is a collective obligation. The third evidence is the hadith of Ibn Abbas about no emigration after the conquest but jihad and intention, emphasizing that jihad remains obligatory, and when called, one must respond. Note: The initial part of the passage also includes a second ruling ('fighting disbelievers is obligatory even if they do not initiate'), but the proofs that follow are specifically for the first ruling. The author later provides separate proofs for the second ruling. This lesson focuses on the first ruling and its proofs.

Key Terms
الْجِهَادُ (al-jihād): Striving in the path of Allah, primarily through armed combat against disbelievers to elevate the word of Allah.
فَرْضٌ عَلَى الْكِفَايَةِ (farḍun ʿalā al-kifāyah): A collective obligation; if a sufficient number of Muslims perform it, the obligation is discharged for all; but if none perform it, all sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the source text, what is the consequence if no one in the community performs jihad?
A) The obligation is lifted because it is too difficult.
B) Only the ruler sins.
C) All the people sin.
D) It is acceptable because jihad is not obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Jihad is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) in the Hanafi school, supported by Quran and Sunnah proofs that indicate a group suffices to carry it out.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
8 min
Fighting Disbelievers is Obligatory Even Without Initiation
Ruling with three scriptural proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fighting disbelievers and cite the three proofs from the Quran and Sunnah that establish this obligation.

Core Idea
Fighting disbelievers is wajib even without their initiation, based on clear Quranic commands and the Prophet's practice.

The Hanafi school holds that jihad against disbelievers is an obligation upon the Muslim community even if the disbelievers have not initiated hostilities. This lesson examines the ruling as stated in Al-Quduri's matn and the three proofs provided from the Quran and hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The matn states 'wa qitālu al-kuffār wājib ʿalaynā wa in lam yabda'ūnā' (fighting disbelievers is obligatory upon us even if they do not start). Note that 'wājib' here indicates a binding collective duty (fard kifayah) when conditions are met.
This is not a personal obligation on every individual; it falls on the community under a just Imam.
2
Examine the first proof: Quran 4:89
The verse commands: 'Fa in tawallaw fakhudhūhum waqtulūhum...' (Then if they turn away, seize them and kill them wherever you find them). The phrase 'in tawallaw' (if they turn away) refers to those who reject Islam or break covenants. The imperative indicates obligation.
The proof (wajh al-dalālah) is the general command to kill those who turn away, which includes disbelievers who are not initiating combat.
3
Examine the second proof: Quran 9:36
The verse says: 'Wa qātilū al-mushrikīna kāffatan kamā yuqātilūnakum kāffatan' (And fight the polytheists all together as they fight you all together). This commands proactive fighting without requiring their initiation, since the phrase 'as they fight you' indicates a collective state, not a conditional trigger.
The command is symmetrical: Muslims are to fight polytheists in all circumstances, just as polytheists (in principle) fight Muslims.
4
Examine the third proof: Hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud
The Prophet (peace be upon him) proactively went to the Jews of Madinah, gave them the choice to accept Islam or leave, and said 'Innī urīdu an ujliyakum min hādhihi al-arḍ' (I intend to expel you from this land). This shows the Prophet initiating action against non-believers who had not attacked him.
The hadith illustrates proactive jihad: the Prophet did not wait for Jewish aggression but acted based on the community's safety and the need to remove hostility.
5
Understand the Hanafi position in context
The Hanafi school classifies this as wājib (obligatory) under the category of fard kifayah (collective duty). It requires a just Imam, prior invitation to Islam or jizyah, and reasonable chance of success. The obligation is not unconditional in all circumstances but is triggered when the community has the means and leadership.
Some later Hanafis (like al-Kāsānī) discuss conditions for offensive jihad, but the core ruling remains that initiation is permitted and even obligatory when conditions are met.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لوجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَقِتَالُ الْكُفَّارِ وَاجِبٌ عَلَيْنَا وَإِنْ لَمْ يَبْدَءُونَا ﴿فَإِن تَوَلَّوْا فَخُذُوهُمْ وَاقْتُلُوهُمْ حَيْثُ وَجَدتُّمُوهُمْ وَلَا تَتَّخِذُواْ مِنْهُمْ وَلِيًّا وَلَا نَصِيرًا﴾ (سورة النساء، 4 أيت، نمبر (89) وجه:(۲) الآية لثبوت وَقِتَالُ الْكُفَّارِ وَاجِبٌ عَلَيْنَا وَإِنْ لَمْ يَبْدَءُونَا \ ﴿وَقَتِلُواْ الْمُشْرِكِينَ كَافَّةً كَمَا يُقَتِلُونَكُمْ كَافَّةً وَاعْلَمُوا أَنَّ اللَّهَ مَعَ الْمُتَّقِينَ﴾ (سورة التوبة، 9 أيت، نمبر 36) وجه:(۳) الحديث لثبوت وَقِتَالُ الْكُفَّارِ وَاجِبٌ عَلَيْنَا وَإِنْ لَمْ يَبْدَءُونَا عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، أَنَّهُ قَالَ: بَيْنَا نَحْنُ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ إِذْ خَرَجَ إِلَيْنَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ، فَقَالَ: «انْطَلِقُوا إِلَى يَهُودَ» فَخَرَجْنَا مَعَهُ حَتَّى جِئْنَاهُمْ، فَقَامَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَنَادَاهُمْ، فَقَالَ: «يَا مَعْشَرَ يَهُودَ، أَسْلِمُوا تَسْلَمُوا... وَإِنِّي أُرِيدُ أَنْ أُجْلِيَكُمْ مِنْ هَذِهِ الْأَرْضِ ، سنن ابوداود، بَابُ كَيْفَ كَانَ إِخْرَاجُ الْيَهُودِ مِنَ الْمَدِينَةِ، نمبر 3003)
(1) The verse proving the ruling 'and fighting the disbelievers is obligatory upon us even if they do not initiate': {Then if they turn away, seize them and kill them wherever you find them and take not from them any ally or helper} (Surah an-Nisa, 4:89). (2) The verse proving the ruling: {And fight the polytheists all together as they fight you all together. And know that Allah is with the righteous} (Surah at-Tawbah, 9:36). (3) The hadith proving the ruling: From Abu Hurayrah that he said: While we were in the mosque, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) came out to us and said, 'Proceed to the Jews.' So we went out with him until we came to them. The Messenger of Allah stood and called them, saying, 'O congregation of Jews, accept Islam and you will be safe... and I intend to expel you from this land.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter on How the Jews were Expelled from Madinah, no. 3003).
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This lesson covers the second ruling from the matn: fighting disbelievers is obligatory upon Muslims even if the disbelievers do not initiate hostilities. The author provides three evidences: First, Quran 4:89 commands to seize and kill those who turn away (from faith), which applies to disbelievers in general. Second, Quran 9:36 commands to fight the polytheists collectively. Third, the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) took the initiative to go to the Jews of Madinah and give them the choice to accept Islam or leave, indicating proactive jihad. This establishes that jihad is not merely defensive but can be initiated to spread Islam, though with conditions (e.g., prior invitation to Islam). The Hanafi school holds that the obligation to fight disbelievers is wajib upon the community when the Imam calls for it, even if the disbelievers have not attacked first.

Key Terms
قِتَالُ الْكُفَّارِ (qitālu al-kuffār): Fighting the disbelievers as part of jihad, obligatory upon the community when conditions are met.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is fighting disbelievers obligatory?
A) Only if they attack first
B) Only if they persecute Muslims
C) Even if they do not initiate hostilities
D) Only when the Imam declares it, but not as a general rule

Key Takeaway
Fighting disbelievers is wajib even if they do not start, as proven by clear Quranic commands and the Prophet's proactive actions.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
beginner
10 min
Exemptions from Jihad: Who is Not Obligated
Ruling listing categories exempt from obligatory jihad with multiple hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven categories exempt from obligatory jihad and state the primary evidence for each exemption according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Jihad is not wajib on minors, insane, slaves, women, or those with severe disabilities except in general mobilization.

This lesson presents a key ruling from Al-Quduri's matn on who is exempt from the obligation of jihad. The exemption covers seven categories, each supported by strong prophetic evidence. While the general rule applies in normal times, a crucial exception arises when the enemy attacks the entire community, making jihad fard 'ayn on all capable persons, including those normally exempt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
Jihad is wajib al-kifayah on capable free adult males. The passage lists exemptions from this obligation.
Remember that wajib al-kifayah becomes wajib 'ayn when the community is directly threatened.
2
List the seven exempt categories
From the matn: child (صَبِيّ), insane person (مَجْنُون), slave (عَبْد), woman (امْرَأَة), blind person (أَعْمَى), cripple (مُقْعَد), and amputee (أَقْطَع).
These are based on lack of legal capacity or physical ability.
3
Match each exemption to its primary evidence
The passage provides hadiths: (1) 'Pen lifted' for child and insane (Abu Dawud). (2) Age limit from Ibn Umar. (3-4) Slave needs master's permission. (5) A'ishah: women's jihad is Hajj. (6) Women's supportive role in battle.
Each hadith directly addresses the exemption.
4
Understand the exception of general mobilization (nafir 'amm)
When the enemy attacks the entire community, jihad becomes fard 'ayn on every capable person. In that case, even those normally exempt may be obligated to participate.
The Urdu note in the lesson explicitly states this principle.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Consider a blind man in a situation where the enemy has surrounded the city. Is jihad obligatory on him? Normally no, but under nafir 'amm, if he can contribute (e.g., financially), it may be required.
Physical capability remains a condition, but the obligation expands.

تَجَنُونِ \ عَنْ عَلِي عليه السلام، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: " رُفِعَ الْقَلَمُ عَنْ ثَلَاثَةٍ : عَنِ النَّائِمِ حَتَّى يَسْتَيْقِظُ، وَعَنِ الصَّبِيِّ حَتَّى يَحْتَلِمَ، وَعَنِ (بخاري شريف بَابُ غَزْوَةِ الْخَنْدَقِ وَهِيَ الْأَحْزَابُ ،نمبر 4097) وجه:(۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجِبُ الْجِهَادُ عَلَى صَبِيّ وَلَا تَجَنُونِ \ عَنِ الْحَارِثِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أَبِي رَبِيعَةَ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ فِي بَعْضِ مَغَازِيهِ، فَمَرَّ بِأَنَاسٍ مِنْ مُزَيْنَةَ فَاتَّبَعَهُ عَبْدٌ لِامْرَأَةٍ مِنْهُمْ فَلَمَّا كَانَ فِي بَعْضِ الطَّرِيقِ سَلَّمَ عَلَيْهِ فَقَالَ: «فَلَانْ؟» قَالَ: نَعَمْ، قَالَ: «مَا شَأْنُكَ؟» قَالَ: أُجَاهِدُ مَعَكَ قَالَ: «أَذِنَتْ لَكَ سَيِّدَتُكَ؟» قَالَ: لَا. قَالَ: «ارْجِعْ إِلَيْهَا فَأَخْبِرْهَا فَإِنَّ مَثَلَكَ مَثَلُ عَبْدِ لَا يُصَلِّي إِنْ مُتَّ قَبْلَ أَنْ تَرْجِعَ إِلَيْهَا الخ، مستدرك للحاكم، وَأَمَّا حَدِيثُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ يَزِيدَ الْأَنْصَارِي، غبر 2553 سنن بيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ لا يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ الْجِهَادُ، نمبر 17812) وجه:(۴) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجِبُ الْجِهَادُ عَلَى صَيَ وَلَا مَجْنُونٍ \ عَنْ جَابِرٍ، قَالَ: «جَاءَ عَبْدٌ، فَبَايَعَ النَّبِيَّ اللهِ عَلَى الهِجْرَةِ ، وَلَا يَشْعُرُ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَّهُ عَبْدٌ ، فَجَاءَ سَيِّدُهُ يُرِيدُهُ، فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ : بِعْنِيهِ فَاشْتَرَاهُ بِعَبْدَيْنِ أَسْوَدَيْنِ، ثُمَّ لَمْ يُبَايِعْ أَحَدًا حَتَّى يَسْأَلَهُ: أَعَبْدُ هُوَ؟، (سنن نسائي، بَيْعَةً الْمَمَالِيكِ ، نمبر 4184 سنن ابن ماجه، بَابُ الْبَيْعَةِ، نمبر 2869) وجه:(۵)الحديث لثبوت وَلا يَجِبُ الْجِهَادُ عَلَى صَبِيّ وَلَا تَجُنُونِ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ أُمَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ قَالَتِ: «اسْتَأْذَنْتُ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي الْجِهَادِ فَقَالَ: جِهَادُكُنَّ الْحَجُ)، (بخاري بَابُ جِهَادِ النِّسَاءِ غبر 2875) وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَحِبُ الْجِهَادُ عَلَى صَبِيَّ وَلَا تَجُنُونٍ \ عَنِ الرُّبَيْعِ بِنْتِ مُعَوِدٍ قَالَتْ: كُنَّا مَعَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَسْقِي وَنُدَاوِي الْجُرْحَى وَنَرُدُ الْقَتْلَى إِلَى الْمَدِينَةِ،(بخاري شريف، بَابُ مُدَاوَاةِ النِّسَاءِ الجُرْحَى فِي الْغَزْو، نمبر 2882) اصول: عام حالات میں بچوں ، غلاموں اور عورتوں پر جہاد واجب نہیں ہے البتہ نفیر عام ہو جائے تو جہاد سبھی پر فرض ہو گا اور یہ لوگ بھی جہاد میں شرکت کر سکتے ہیں۔
And jihad is not obligatory upon a child, nor an insane person, nor a slave, nor a woman, nor a blind person, nor a cripple, nor an amputee. (1) The hadith proving that jihad is not obligatory upon a child or an insane: From Ali (peace be upon him) from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The pen is lifted from three: from the sleeper until he wakes, from the child until he reaches puberty, and from the insane until he becomes sane.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter on the Insane who Steals or Commits a Hadd Offense, no. 4403). (2) The hadith proving that jihad is not obligatory upon a child or an insane: From Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them): 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) presented him on the day of Uhud when he was fourteen years old, and did not permit him; and presented him on the day of Khandaq when he was fifteen, and permitted him.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter of the Battle of the Trench (al-Ahzab), no. 4097). (3) The hadith proving that jihad is not obligatory upon a child or an insane: From al-Harith ibn Abdullah ibn Abi Rabi'ah that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was on one of his campaigns, when he passed by some people from Muzaynah and a slave of a woman among them followed him. When he was partway on the road, he greeted him and asked: 'So-and-so?' He said: 'Yes.' He asked: 'What is your matter?' He said: 'I will fight with you.' He said: 'Did your mistress give you permission?' He said: 'No.' He said: 'Return to her and inform her, for your example is like a slave who does not pray; if you die before returning to her...' (Mustadrak al-Hakim, Hadith of Abdullah ibn Yazid al-Ansari? no. 2553, Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on Those upon whom Jihad is not Obligatory, no. 17812). (4) The hadith proving that jihad is not obligatory upon a child or an insane: From Jabir who said: 'A slave came and pledged allegiance to the Prophet (peace be upon him) for emigration, and the Prophet did not know he was a slave. Then his master came wanting him. The Prophet said: Sell him to me, and he bought him for two black slaves. Thereafter he did not accept allegiance from anyone until he asked: Is he a slave?' (Sunan al-Nasa'i, Pledge of Slaves, no. 4184; Sunan Ibn Majah, Chapter of Allegiance, no. 2869). (5) The hadith proving that jihad is not obligatory upon a child or an insane: From A'ishah, Mother of the Believers, who said: 'I asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) for permission to go for jihad, and he said: Your jihad is Hajj.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter of Women's Jihad, no. 2875). (6) The hadith proving that jihad is not obligatory upon a child or an insane: From ar-Rubayyi' bint Mu'awwidh who said: 'We were with the Prophet (peace be upon him) giving water and treating the wounded and carrying the slain back to Madinah.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter of Women Treating the Wounded in Battle, no. 2882). Principle: Under normal circumstances, jihad is not obligatory upon children, slaves, and women. However, if a general mobilization (nafir 'amm) occurs, then jihad becomes obligatory upon everyone, and these individuals may also participate.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This lesson presents the third ruling from the matn listing those on whom jihad is not obligatory: children (pre-puberty), insane persons, slaves, women, the blind, the crippled, and amputees. The author then provides six hadith evidences supporting various exemptions. The first hadith (from Ali) establishes the general principle that the pen is lifted from three categories, including the child and the insane, meaning they are not accountable for obligations. The second hadith (Ibn Umar) shows the age limit for jihad: the Prophet did not permit those under fifteen. The third hadith (al-Harith) indicates that a slave needs his master's permission, and without it, he cannot participate. The fourth hadith (Jabir) further shows that the Prophet would not accept a slave's pledge without the master's consent. The fifth hadith (A'ishah) exempts women from jihad, assigning them Hajj instead. The sixth hadith (ar-Rubayyi') shows that women could assist in non-combat roles but were not obligated to fight. The Urdu summary explains that under normal circumstances these categories are exempt, but in a general mobilization (nafir 'amm), jihad becomes fard 'ayn on all, including these individuals, and they may then participate voluntarily.

Key Terms
صَبِيّ (ṣabiyy): A minor who has not reached puberty; jihad is not obligatory upon him.
مَجْنُون (majnūn): An insane person lacking legal capacity; exempt from all religious obligations, including jihad.
نَفِير عَام (nafīr ʿāmm): General mobilization when the enemy attacks the entire Muslim community; jihad becomes fard 'ayn on every capable person, including those normally exempted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when may a slave be obligated to participate in jihad?
A) Never, because he is exempt permanently
B) Only if his master gives permission
C) In a general mobilization (nafir 'amm)
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
Jihad is not wajib on children, insane, slaves, women, blind, crippled, or amputees, but in general mobilization (nafir 'amm) the obligation expands to all capable persons, overriding normal exemptions.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
beginner
6 min
Exemptions from Obligatory Jihad and the Defense Exception
Ruling on exemptions and defense exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven categories exempt from general jihad and explain the exception for defensive jihad.

Core Idea
General jihad is not required of the incapable; but when attacked, everyone must defend.

This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar lists who is exempt from the obligation of jihad and then introduces a critical exception: when the enemy attacks, even those normally exempt must defend. Understanding this distinction between general and defensive jihad is essential for applying Hanafi rulings correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Clearly state what act is being ruled upon (jihad) and whether the ruling is general or specific.
General jihad is farḍ kifāyah; defensive jihad is farḍ ʿayn.
2
List the exempt categories
Read the text and enumerate the seven types of people who are not obligated in general jihad.
Child, insane, slave, woman, blind, bedridden, amputee.
3
Locate the dalil
Identify the proofs supporting the exemption, such as the hadith of the lifted pen.
Hadith: 'The pen is lifted from three...' (child, sleeping, insane).
4
Analyze the defense exception
Understand why the exemption is overridden when the enemy attacks and what conditions apply.
Necessity makes jihad personal; women and slaves may go without permission.
5
Note cross-madhhab differences
Recognize that other schools may classify jihad differently, but the Hanafi position on exemptions in general jihad is widely accepted.
The Hanafi position is farḍ kifāyah; some may argue farḍ ʿayn, but not for the exempt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجِبُ الْجِهَادُ عَلَى صَبِيٍّ وَلَا مَجْنُونٍ وَلَا عَبْدٍ وَلَا امْرَأَةٍ وَلَا أَعْمَى وَلَا مُقْعَدٍ وَلَا أَقْطَعَ. فَإِنْ هَجَمَ الْعَدُوُّ عَلَى بَلَدٍ وَجَبَ عَلَى جَمِيعِ النَّاسِ الدَّفْعُ تَخْرُجُ الْمَرْأَةُ بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِ زَوْجِهَا وَالْعَبْدُ بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِ سَيِّدِهِ.
And jihad is not obligatory upon a child, nor a madman, nor a slave, nor a woman, nor a blind person, nor a bedridden person, nor an amputee. If the enemy attacks a city, defense becomes obligatory upon all people; the woman goes out without her husband's permission, and the slave without his master's permission.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is a ruling statement (ḥukm) on the obligation of jihad. The author lists seven categories of people upon whom jihad is not obligatory in the general offensive jihad (jihād al-ṭalab). These are: a child (ṣabī) who has not reached puberty, an insane person (majnūn), a slave (ʿabd), a woman (imraʾa), a blind person (aʿmā), a bedridden/crippled person (muqʿad), and an amputee (aqṭaʿ). The exemption is based on lack of capacity or legal responsibility. However, if the enemy suddenly attacks a Muslim city (hajama al-ʿaduwwu ʿalā balad), then jihad becomes a personal obligation (farḍ ʿayn) on every capable resident, including women and slaves, without needing permission from husband or master. This is the defensive jihad (jihād al-dafʿ). The text provides multiple proofs: Hadiths about the pen being lifted from three (child, sleeping, insane), the Prophet not allowing a fourteen-year-old at Uhud but allowing a fifteen-year-old at the Trench, the story of a slave seeking permission, and the Prophet saying women's jihad is Hajj. Also Quranic verses (9:91, 4:95, 9:38-41, 9:120) indicate that those with valid excuses are exempt, but able believers must go forth. The exception for defense is based on necessity and the principle of repelling harm. In the Hanafi madhhab, the general offensive jihad is a communal obligation (farḍ kifāyah), but defensive jihad becomes an individual obligation (farḍ ʿayn) on all present, including those otherwise exempt, because the duty to protect Muslim lives and property overrides normal exemptions.

Key Terms
جهاد (jihād): Struggle or fighting in the path of Allah; in this context, military combat against non-Muslims to defend or spread Islam.
صبي (ṣabī): A male child who has not reached puberty; exempt from obligations requiring legal capacity.
مقعد (muqʿad): A person permanently bedridden or unable to walk due to chronic illness or disability; exempt from jihad.
فرض كفاية (farḍ kifāyah): A communal obligation; if sufficient members perform it, the rest are absolved.
فرض عين (farḍ ʿayn): An individual obligation; every capable person must perform it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT exempt from general jihad?
A) A blind man
B) A slave
C) A wealthy merchant
D) A bedridden person

Key Takeaway
General jihad is a communal obligation from which the incapable are exempt, but defensive jihad is a personal duty that overrides all exemptions.

Procedure for Calling Enemies: Islam, Jizya, or War
Ruling on the sequence of inviting enemy to Islam or jizya before fighting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three-step sequence for dealing with enemy non-Muslims in dar al-harb according to Hanafi fiqh and identify the hadith evidence supporting each step.

Core Idea
Before fighting, you must call to Islam, then offer jizya — war is the last resort.

This passage from Al-Quduri outlines the obligatory procedure when Muslim forces besiege a city in enemy territory. The ruling establishes a clear sequence: invitation to Islam first, then proposal of jizya (tribute), and only if both are refused does fighting become permissible. The text also provides three hadith proofs to support this sequence. Let's examine the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequential ruling
Read the matn: when Muslims enter dar al-harb and besiege, they call to Islam; if accepted, desist; if refused, call to jizya; if accepted, desist; if refused, they may fight. Understand this as a three-step wajib sequence.
The sequence is obligatory, not merely recommended.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the hadith of Buraidah which contains the explicit command: 'When you meet your enemy... call them to three...' This is the main evidence for the ruling.
The hadith is narrated by Muslim and Abu Dawud.
3
Examine the supporting hadith
Note the hadith of Ibn Abbas ('the Prophet never fought without calling') and of Anas ('I was commanded to fight people until they say la ilaha illa Allah') which reinforce the principle.
These hadith are from Mustadrak al-Hakim, Musnad Ahmad, Bukhari, and Muslim.
4
Understand the jizya offer
The jizya is offered only after the call to Islam is refused. Acceptance of jizya grants protection and rights similar to Muslims.
Hanafi school accepts jizya from all non-Muslims, not just People of the Book.
5
Apply the ruling
This procedure governs Muslim conduct in jihad. It must be followed before initiating combat; failure to call is a sin, even if the ultimate permission to fight exists.
The ruling is mufta bihi and agreed upon by the majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الْمُسْلِمُونَ دَارَ الْحَرْبِ فَحَاصَرُوا مَدِينَةً أَوْ حِصْنًا دَعَوْهُمْ إِلَى الْإِسْلَامِ فَإِنْ أَجَابُوهُمْ كَفُّوا عَنْ قِتَالِهِمْ وَإِنِ امْتَنَعُوا دَعَوْهُمْ إِلَى أَدَاءِ الْجِزْيَةِ فَإِنْ بَذَلُوهَا فَلَهُمْ مَا لِلْمُسْلِمِينَ وَعَلَيْهِمْ مَا عَلَيْهِمْ
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الْمُسْلِمُونَ دَارَ الْحَرْبِ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: «مَا قَاتَلَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَوْمًا حَتَّى دَعَاهُمْ» (مستدرك للحاكم، ومسند أحمد)
وجه: (2) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الْمُسْلِمُونَ دَارَ الْحَرْبِ عَنْ سليمان ابْنِ بُرَيْدَةَ عَنْ أَبِيهِ قَالَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: إِذَا أَمَّرَ أَمِيرٌ عَلَى جَيْشٍ... وَإِذَا لَقِيتَ عَدُوَّكَ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ فَادْعُهُمْ إِلَى ثَلَاثِ خِصَالٍ أَوْ خِلَالٍ، فَأَيَّتُهُنَّ مَا أَجَابُوكَ فَاقْبَلْ مِنْهُمْ وَكُفَّ عَنْهُمْ... فَإِنْ هُمْ أَبَوْا فَسَلْهُمُ الْجِزْيَةَ، فَإِنْ هُمْ أَجَابُوكَ فَاقْبَلْ مِنْهُمْ وَكُفَّ عَنْهُمْ. فَإِنْ هُمْ أَبَوْا فَاسْتَعِنْ بِاللَّهِ وَقَاتِلْهُمْ. (مسلم، باب تأمير الإمام الأمراء على البعوث... حديث 1731; أبو داود، باب في دعاء المشركين، حديث 2612)
وجه: (3) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الْمُسْلِمُونَ دَارَ الْحَرْبِ عَنْ أَنَسِ بْنِ مَالِكٍ قَالَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «أُمِرْتُ أَنْ أُقَاتِلَ النَّاسَ حَتَّى يَقُولُوا لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ، فَإِذَا قَالُوهَا، وَصَلَّوْا صَلَاتَنَا، وَاسْتَقْبَلُوا قِبْلَتَنَا، وَذَبَحُوا ذَبِيحَتَنَا، فَقَدْ حَرُمَتْ عَلَيْنَا دِمَاؤُهُمْ وَأَمْوَالُهُمْ إِلَّا بِحَقِّهَا، وَحِسَابُهُمْ عَلَى اللهِ» (بخاري، باب فضل استقبال القبلة، حديث 392; مسلم، باب الأمر بقتال الناس حتى يقولوا لا إله إلا الله، حديث 20)
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ امْتَنَعُوا دَعَوْهُمْ إِلَى أَدَاءِ الْجُزْيَةِ عَنْ سليمان ابْنِ بُرَيْدَةَ... (مثل السابق)
اصول : کفار سے قتال کا طریقہ: اولا دعوت اسلام، ثانیا نہ مانے تو جزیہ کی پیشکش، ثالثا جنگ، نیز اگر اسلام قبول کرلے تو قتال سے رک جائے۔
When the Muslims enter the abode of war (dar al-harb) and besiege a city or fort, they call them to Islam. If they respond, they desist from fighting them. And if they refuse, they call them to pay the jizya (tribute). If they pay it, then they have what the Muslims have and they owe what the Muslims owe. Evidence (1) The hadith to establish: When the Muslims enter dar al-harb: from Ibn Abbas who said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did not fight a people until he called them.' (Mustadrak al-Hakim, Musnad Ahmad) Evidence (2) The hadith to establish: from Sulaiman ibn Buraidah on the authority of his father who said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: When an amir is appointed over an army... and when you meet your enemy from among the polytheists, call them to three things (or alternatives). Whichever they respond to, accept from them and desist from them... If they refuse, then ask them for the jizya. If they respond, accept from them and desist from them. If they refuse, then seek help from Allah and fight them.' (Muslim, Abu Dawud) Evidence (3) The hadith to establish: from Anas ibn Malik who said: 'I have been commanded to fight the people until they say 'There is no god but Allah'. When they say it, pray our prayer, face our qibla, and slaughter as we slaughter, then their blood and wealth become forbidden for us except by its due, and their reckoning is with Allah.' (Bukhari, Muslim) Evidence (1) for the part about jizya: from Sulaiman ibn Buraidah as above. Principle: The method of fighting the disbelievers: first, call to Islam; second, if they refuse, offer jizya; third, war. Also, if they accept Islam, we desist from fighting.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of siyar, specifying the procedure when Muslims invade enemy territory. The ruling establishes a sequence: first invite to Islam, then to jizya, then fight. The hadith evidence from Ibn Abbas and Buraidah supports this. This is a key ruling in Hanafi fiqh regarding the conduct of war. The Urdu summary (asool) restates the three-step method.

Key Terms
دَارُ الْحَرْبِ (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim rule where Islamic law is not applied, considered abode of war.
الْجِزْيَةُ (al-jizyah): Tribute paid by non-Muslims (typically People of the Book or others) in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.
الدَّعْوَةُ (al-da'wah): Invitation to embrace Islam before initiating hostilities, a recommended and obligatory step in jihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must Muslims do first when besieging a city in dar al-harb according to this passage?
A) Immediately attack.
B) Call them to pay jizya.
C) Call them to Islam.
D) Demand surrender.

Key Takeaway
Before engaging in combat, Muslim forces must first call the enemy to Islam, then offer jizya; only after both refusals is war permitted.

The Three-Stage Invitation Before Jihad
States the three-stage invitation process before fighting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three-stage invitation process before fighting non-Muslims and identify when invitation is obligatory versus recommended.

Core Idea
Fight only after inviting: first to Islam, then jizyah, then combat.

Before the sword, there is a word. The Hanafi school, based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ, prescribes a clear sequence of invitations before engaging non-Muslims in war. This lesson unpacks the three stages and the critical condition that distinguishes obligatory from recommended invitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The passage addresses the procedure when Muslims enter dar al-harb and besiege a city or fortress. What is the act being ruled upon? The invitation process before fighting.
Dar al-harb is the territory where non-Muslim law prevails.
2
Trace the three stages
List the three sequential invitations: (1) call to Islam, (2) if refused, call to jizyah, (3) if both refused, then fight. Each stage has a different outcome.
3
Identify the condition for obligatory invitation
The text states it is not permissible to fight those who have not received the call of Islam except after inviting them. This makes invitation a condition (shart) for the permissibility of fighting.
For those who have already heard, invitation is mustahabb, not wajib.
4
Locate the dalil and its wajh al-dalalah
The ruling is based on the hadith of Buraydah where the Prophet ﷺ instructed commanders to call enemies to three things. The imperative 'فَادْعُهُمْ' indicates obligation, and the sequence 'ثَلَاثِ خِصَالٍ' establishes the order.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qat'i al-dalala).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الْمُسْلِمُونَ دَارَ الْحَرْبِ فَحَاصَرُوا مَدِينَةً أَوْ حِصْنًا دَعَوْهُمْ إِلَى الْإِسْلَامِ فَإِنْ أَجَابُوهُمْ كَفُّوا عَنْ قِتَالِهِمْ وَإِنْ امْتَنَعُوا دَعَوْهُمْ إِلَى أَدَاءِ الْجِزْيَةِ فَإِنْ بَذَلُوهَا فَلَهُمْ مَا لِلْمُسْلِمِينَ وَعَلَيْهِمْ مَا عَلَيْهِمْ وَإِنْ امْتَنَعُوا قَاتَلُوهُمْ وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يُقَاتِلَ مَنْ لَمْ تَبْلُغْهُ دَعْوَةُ الْإِسْلَامِ إِلَّا بَعْدَ أَنْ يَدْعُوَهُمْ وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أَنْ يَدْعُوَ مَنْ بَلَغَتْهُ الدَّعْوَةُ إِلَى الْإِسْلَامِ وَلَا يَجِبُ ذَلِكَ
And when Muslims enter the abode of war and besiege a city or fortress, they invite them to Islam. If they respond, they refrain from fighting them. And if they refuse, they invite them to pay the jizyah. If they give it, then for them is what is for the Muslims and upon them is what is upon the Muslims. And if they refuse, they fight them. And it is not permissible to fight those who have not received the call of Islam except after inviting them. And it is recommended to invite those who have received the call to Islam, and that is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's matn outlines the Hanafi ruling on the procedure before engaging non-Muslims in war. It prescribes a three-stage invitation: first, invite to Islam; if accepted, fighting is suspended. Second, if they refuse, invite to accepting jizyah; if accepted, they enjoy the same rights and bear the same duties as Muslims. Third, if they refuse both, then combat is permitted. The passage also establishes a critical condition: it is not permissible to fight any person who has not yet received the message of Islam; they must first be called. For those who have already heard the call, renewing the invitation is recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory. This ruling is based on the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ) and the rightly-guided caliphs, as evidenced by multiple hadith, including the famous instruction of the Prophet to commanders (hadith of Buraydah in Muslim 1731) and the practice of Ibn Abbas (reported in Mustadrak and Musnad Ahmad).

Key Terms
دَارَ الْحَرْب (dar al-harb): The territory where non-Muslims are dominant and Muslim law is not enforced, making it permissible to fight them under certain conditions.
الْجِزْيَة (al-jizyah): A tax levied on non-Muslims living under Muslim protection (dhimma) in lieu of military service and as a symbol of their acceptance of Muslim rule.
الدَّعْوَة (al-da'wah): The call or invitation to embrace Islam, which must be issued to non-Muslims before military action is initiated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on inviting to Islam a person who has already received the call but refuses?
A) It is obligatory (wajib) to invite them again.
B) It is recommended (mustahabb) but not obligatory.
C) It is prohibited (haram) to invite them again.
D) It is permissible (mubah) without any preference.

Key Takeaway
Before fighting, Muslims must invite non-Muslims to Islam, then to jizyah; only after both refusals is combat permitted, and those who have not heard must be invited first.

Permissible Destructive Measures in Jihad
Lists permissible destructive measures after the enemy refuses both Islam and jizyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permissible destructive measures in jihad according to the Hanafi school and explain the basis for their permissibility.

Core Idea
War permits destruction of property and life when necessary to break enemy resistance.

The previous lesson covered the three options offered to non-Muslims: Islam, jizyah, or war. When they choose war, the Muslim commander is permitted to use all necessary force to subdue the enemy. This passage from al-Quduri details specific measures—such as catapults, burning, flooding, and destroying crops—that are permissible as part of siege warfare, based on prophetic practice and military necessity.

Guided Path
1
Contextualize the Ruling
Understand that this passage applies only after the enemy has explicitly refused both Islam and jizyah, thus entering a state of active hostilities. The ruling assumes a legitimate defensive or offensive jihad.
The ruling does not apply to non-hostile situations or to combatants who surrender.
2
Extract the List of Actions
Read the passage carefully and identify each permissible action: setting up mangonels (catapults), burning, flooding, cutting down trees, and spoiling crops. Note that the phrase 'seek Allah's help' precedes the list, emphasizing reliance on divine support while employing earthly means.
The list is not exhaustive; it illustrates general permissibility for destructive methods that serve military ends.
3
Classify the Hukm
The ruling level is mubah (permissible), as stated in the Hanafi school. Though general Islamic teachings prohibit waste, torture, and burning with fire, these are overridden by the necessity of war. The key condition is military necessity—actions must be intended to weaken the enemy and hasten victory.
Wanton destruction without military purpose would be makruh or haram.
4
Connect to Evidence
These measures are validated by the Prophet's own practice, such as cutting down the palm trees of Banu Nadir (Quran 59:5) and using mangonels at the siege of Ta'if. The Hanafi school uses these precedents to establish permissibility despite general prohibitions.
The hadith forbidding burning with fire is understood as applying to individuals not engaged in war, not to siege warfare.
5
Apply to Modern Context
The classical measures map to modern equivalents: catapults to artillery, burning to incendiary weapons, flooding to dam destruction, and tree-cutting to deforestation for tactical advantage. The underlying principle of necessary force remains unchanged.
However, weapons causing disproportionate harm (e.g., chemical or biological) may be evaluated separately based on the principle of unnecessary suffering.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ أَبَوْا اسْتَعَانُوا عَلَيْهِمْ بِاللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَنَصَبُوا عَلَيْهِمْ الْمَجَانِيقَ وَحَرَّقُوهُمْ وَأَرْسَلُوا عَلَيْهِمْ الْمَاءَ وَقَطَعُوا شَجَرَهُمْ وَأَفْسَدُوا زَرْعَهُمْ
And if they refuse, they seek Allah's help against them, and set up mangonels against them, and burn them, and send water against them, and cut down their trees, and spoil their crops.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This ruling details the permissible actions after the enemy has rejected both Islam and the jizyah offer. The Muslims are allowed to employ full-scale warfare using all necessary means. The mention of 'seeking Allah's help' reminds that reliance remains on divine support. The use of mangonels (catapults) indicates that besieging with heavy artillery is permitted. Burning the enemy, flooding them, cutting down trees, and destroying crops were all practiced in early Islamic campaigns, such as the siege of Banu Nadir (where palm trees were cut). These actions are permissible as military necessity, even if they cause collateral damage. The Hanafi school permits such destruction because it weakens the enemy's resistance and hastens victory. However, wanton destruction without military benefit would be disliked (makruh).

Key Terms
الْمَجَانِيق (al-manajīq): Siege engines such as catapults used to hurl stones or fireballs at enemy fortifications.
حَرَّقُوهُمْ (hārraqūhum): Burning the enemy, often by setting fire to their fortifications or using flaming projectiles.
أَرْسَلُوا عَلَيْهِمْ الْمَاءَ (arsalū ʻalayhim al-māʼa): Flooding the enemy, such as diverting rivers or opening dams to cause destruction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Setting up mangonels (catapults).
B) Burning the enemy.
C) Using poison gas.
D) Cutting down trees.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, destruction of enemy property and life is permissible (mubah) when the enemy refuses peace and such measures are necessary for victory.

The Obligation of Invitation Before Fighting and Permissible Siege Tactics
Ruling on calling to Islam before fighting and siege tactics after refusal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the necessity of da'wah before combat and identify the permissible means of warfare after refusal.

Core Idea
Fighting those uninvited is haram; invitation is wajib for the uncalled, sunnah for the called.

This passage from the Book of Siyar establishes the fundamental principle that offensive jihad requires a prior call to Islam. It distinguishes between two categories of non-Muslims: those who have never heard the call (obligatory to invite) and those who have (recommended but not obligatory). After refusal, the Muslims are permitted to use various siege tactics, including catapults, burning, flooding, and destroying resources. The ruling is supported by multiple proofs including a Quranic verse, directives from the Prophet, and the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of non-Muslims
The text distinguishes between those who have not received the call of Islam (lam tablughhu da'wat al-Islam) and those who have (man balaghat-hu al-da'wah).
This distinction is crucial: the ruling differs for each category.
2
Determine the ruling for each category
For those uninvited, fighting is impermissible until they are called (wajib). For those already called, calling is recommended (sunnah) but not obligatory.
The Arabic uses 'la yajuz' (not permissible) and 'yustahab' (recommended).
3
Examine the proofs cited
The author lists a Quranic verse (9:29), a hadith from Sulayman ibn Burayda, a hadith from Ibn Abbas, and a saying of Ali. Each supports the obligation of da'wah.
The Quranic verse commands fighting until jizya is paid, implying the offer of jizya after da'wah.
4
Understand permissible actions after refusal
If the enemy refuses, Muslims may seek Allah's help, use catapults, burn, flood, cut trees, and destroy crops. These are severe but permissible measures.
These tactics are allowed only after the invitation has been extended and rejected.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school holds da'wah as wajib for the uninvited, while some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider it sunnah even for them.
This ikhtilaf has practical implications for the obligation of the commander.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ السّير
وَإِنْ امْتَنَعُوا قَاتَلُوهُمْ وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يُقَاتِلَ مَنْ لَمْ تَبْلُغْهُ دَعْوَةُ الْإِسْلَامِ إِلَّا بَعْدَ أَنْ يَدْعُوَهُمْ وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أَنْ يَدْعُوَ مَنْ بَلَغَتْهُ الدَّعْوَةُ إلَى الْإِسْلَامِ وَلَا يَجِبُ ذَلِكَ فَإِنْ أَبَوْا اسْتَعَانُوا عَلَيْهِمْ بِاللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَنَصَبُوا عَلَيْهِمْ الْمَجَانِيقَ وَحَرَّقُوهُمْ وَأَرْسَلُوا عَلَيْهِمْ الْمَاءَ وَقَطَعُوا شَجَرَهُمْ وَأَفْسَدُوا زَرْعَهُمْ
وجه:(۲) الآية لثبوت وَإِنْ امْتَنَعُوا دَعَوْهُمْ إِلَى أَدَاءِ الْجُزْيَةِ \ ﴿قَتِلُوا الَّذِينَ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ بِاللَّهِ وَلَا بِالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ وَلَا يُحَرِّمُونَ مَا حَرَّمَ اللَّهُ وَرَسُولُهُ وَلَا يَدِينُونَ دِينَ الْحَقِّ مِنَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتَابَ حَتَّى يُعْطُواْ الْجِزْيَةَ عَن يَدٍ وَهُمْ صَغِرُونَ ﴾ (سورة التوبة، 9 أيت، نمبر 29) وجه : (۳) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَإِنْ امْتَنَعُوا دَعَوْهُمْ إِلَى أَدَاءِ الْجُزْيَةِ \ قَالَ عَلِيٌّ الله: «مَنْ كَانَتْ لَهُ ذِمَّتُنَا فَدَمُهُ كِدَمَائِنَا، سنن ،قطني كِتَابُ الْحُدُودِ وَالدِّيَاتِ وَغَيْرُهُ، نمبر 3296) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ امْتَنَعُوا قَاتَلُوهُمْ \ عَنْ سليمان ابْنِ بُرَيْدَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ... وَإِذَا لَقِيتَ عَدُوَّكَ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ فَادْعُهُمْ إِلَى ثَلَاثِ خِصَالٍ أَوْ خِلَالٍ). فَأَيَّتُهُنَّ مَا أَجَابُوكَ فَاقْبَلْ مِنْهُمْ وَكُفَّ عَنْهُمْ ثُمَّ ادْعُهُمْ إِلَى الإِسْلَامِ فَإِنْ أَجَابُوكَ فَاقْبَلْ مِنْهُمْ وَكُفَّ عَنْهُمْ،، (مسلم شريف، باب تأمير الإمام الأمراء على البعوث ووصية إِيَّاهُمْ بِآدَابِ الْغَزْوِ وَغَيْرِهَا. نمبر 1731) وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ امْتَنَعُوا قَاتَلُوهُمْ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: «مَا قَاتَلَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَوْمًا حَتَّى دَعَاهُمْ، (مستدرك للحاكم، وَأَمَّا حَدِيثُ مَعْمَرٍ ، نمبر 37/مسند احمد، مسند عبد الله بن العباس بن عبد الطلب عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، نمبر 2106) وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أَنْ يَدْعُوَ مَنْ بَلَغَتْهُ \ كَتَبْتُ إِلَى نَافِعٍ، فَكَتَبَ إِلَيَّ: «إِنَّ التي لا أَغَارَ عَلَى بَنِي الْمُصْطَلِقِ وَهُمْ غَارُونَ، وَأَنْعَامُهُمْ تُسْقَى عَلَى الْمَاءِ، فَقَتَلَ مُقَاتِلَتَهُمْ، وَسَيَ ذَرَارِيَّهُمْ، وَأَصَابَ يَوْمَئِذٍ جُوَيْرِيَةَ ، بخاري شريف ، بَابُ مَنْ مَلَكَ مِنَ الْعَرَبِ رَقِيقًا فَوَهَبَ وَبَاع، غير (2541) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ أَبَوْا اسْتَعَانُوا عَلَيْهِمْ بِاللَّهِ \ عَنْ سليمان ابْنِ بُرَيْدَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ.
اصول : جن کفار کو دعوتِ اسلام نہ پہنچی ہو ان سے اولا قتال کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
Book of Siyar. And if they refuse, fight them. It is not permissible to fight those who have not received the call of Islam except after calling them. It is recommended (not obligatory) to call those who have received the call. If they refuse, seek help from Allah, set up catapults, burn them, release water on them, cut their trees, and spoil their crops. Evidence: (2) Verse: 'Fight those who do not believe in Allah... until they pay jizya willingly and are humbled' (Tawbah 9:29). (3) Saying of Ali: 'Whoever has our covenant, his blood is like our blood.' (1) Hadith of Sulayman ibn Burayda from his father: 'When you meet your enemy, call them to three things... then call them to Islam...' (Muslim). (2) Hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'The Prophet never fought a people until he called them.' (1) Hadith: 'Write to Nafi: the attack on Bani al-Mustaliq...' (Bukhari). (1) Hadith from Sulayman ibn Burayda from his father. Principle: Those disbelievers who have not received the call of Islam, it is not permissible to fight them until after calling them.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Siyar presents a ruling on the obligation of inviting the enemy to Islam before engaging in warfare. The matn states that if the enemy refuses, fighting is permissible, but those who have not received the call must be invited first. For those who have already heard the call, inviting is recommended but not obligatory. After refusal, the Muslims may use all necessary means: seeking divine aid, setting up catapults, burning, flooding, cutting trees, and destroying crops. The proofs include a Quranic verse on jizya, a saying of Ali, and several hadiths, such as the famous directive of the Prophet to call to three options (Islam, jizya, or war) and the practice of the Prophet in battles. The Urdu principle at the end emphasizes that fighting those who have not received the call is impermissible without prior invitation. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi position that da'wah is a prerequisite for offensive jihad.

Key Terms
دَعْوَةُ الْإِسْلَامِ (da'wat al-Islam): The invitation to embrace Islam given to non-Muslims before combat.
الْجِزْيَةَ (al-jizyah): Poll tax paid by non-Muslims under Muslim rule in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.
الْمَجَانِيقَ (al-majanīq): Catapults; siege engines used to breach fortifications.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is the obligation regarding calling disbelievers to Islam before fighting?
A) It is obligatory to call those who have not received the call, and recommended for those who have.
B) It is obligatory for all disbelievers without exception.
C) It is recommended but not obligatory for anyone.
D) Calling is only required for People of the Book.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school makes the invitation to Islam a binding condition (wajib) before fighting those who have never heard it, and recommends it for those who have.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate

Ruling on Shooting the Enemy When Muslims Are Present
Permissibility of targeting the enemy even if Muslim captives or traders are present

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on attacking the enemy when Muslims are used as human shields, identify the key proof (hadith of as-Sa'b ibn Jaththama), and explain the condition of aiming at the disbelievers.

Core Idea
Shooting is permitted even if Muslims are harmed, provided they aim at the disbelievers.

This passage from Al-Quduri addresses a difficult scenario in jihad: the enemy uses Muslim captives or children as human shields. The Hanafi school permits continued attack, based on the principle that the necessity of defeating the enemy overrides the risk of collateral harm to Muslims, but with the important condition that the attackers must intend to hit the disbelievers.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify what the text says: 'There is no harm in shooting them even if there is a Muslim captive or trader.' The ruling is that shooting is mubah (permissible).
The ruling is not obligatory; it is a permission based on necessity.
2
Recognize the exceptional condition
The passage then mentions the scenario where the enemy shields with Muslim children or captives: the Muslims still shoot but aim at the disbelievers.
This is a case of darurah (necessity) where the greater evil of enemy success outweighs the risk to Muslim lives.
3
Identify the primary proof
The hadith of as-Sa'b ibn Jaththama: the Prophet allowed night attacks even if it caused casualties among women and children, saying 'هم منهم' (they are from them).
This hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalala).
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'they are from them' integrates non-combatants into the enemy camp, making incidental killing permissible when necessary.
This is a key linguistic argument that expands the scope of permissible targets.
5
Consider the cross-madhhab dispute
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) prohibit targeting when Muslims are clearly used as shields. The Hanafi school allows it based on this hadith and the principle of overcoming the greater evil.
The practical difference: Hanafis continue the attack; Shafi'is would cease if certain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا بَأْسَ بِرَمْيِهِمْ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِمْ مُسْلِمٌ أَسِيرٌ أَوْ تَاجِرٌ فَإِنْ تَتَرَّسُوا بِصِبْيَانِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ أَوْ بِالْأَسَارَى لَمْ يَكُفُّوا عَنْ رَمْيِهِمْ وَيَقْصِدُونَ بِالرَّمْيِ الْكُفَّارَ
قَالَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ ، إِذَا أَمَّرَ أمير على جيش... فَإِنْ هُمْ أَبَوْا فَسَلْهُمُ الْخِزْيَةَ. فَإِنْ هُمْ أَجَابُوكَ فَاقْبَلْ مِنْهُمْ وَكُفَّ عَنْهُمْ. فَإِنْ هُمْ أَبَوْا فَاسْتَعِنْ بِاللَّهِ وَقَاتِلْهُمْ ، (مسلم شريف، باب تأمير الإمام الأمراء على البعوث ووصية إِيَّاهُمْ بِآدَابِ الْغَزْوِ وَغَيْرِهَا . نمبر 1731/سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي دُعَاءِ الْمُشْرِكِينَنمبر 2612)
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ أَبَوْا اسْتَعَانُوا عَلَيْهِمْ بِاللَّهِ \ عَنْ أَبِي عُبَيْدَةَ ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ حَاصَرَ أَهْلَ الطَّائِفِ، وَنَصَبَ عَلَيْهِمُ الْمَنْجَنِيقَ سَبْعَةَ عَشَرَ يَوْمًا، (سنن بيهقي، بَابُ قَطع الشَّجَرِ وَحَرْقِ الْمَنَازِلِ،نمبر 18120/ترمذي شريف، بَابُ مَا جَاءَفِي الْأَخْذِ مِنَ اللَّحْيَةِ، نمبر 2762) وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ أَبَوْا اسْتَعَانُوا عَلَيْهِمْ بِاللَّهِ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِي الله عنهما قَالَ: «حَرَّقَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَخْلَ بَنِي النَّضِيرِ وَقَطَعَ، وَهِيَ الْبَوَيْرَةُ، فَنَزَلَتْ : {مَا قَطَعْتُمْ مِنْ لِينَةٍ أَوْ تَرَكْتُمُوهَا قَائِمَةً عَلَى أُصُولِهَا فَبِإِذْنِ اللهِ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ بَابُ حَدِيثِ بَنِي النضير، نمبر 4031/مسلم شريف ، بَاب جَوَازِ قَطع أَشْجَارِ الْكُفَّارِ وَتَحْرِيقِهَا ، نمبر 1746) 10 وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِرَمْيِهِمْ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِمْ مُسْلِمٌ أَسِيرٌ \ عَنِ الصَّعْبِ بْنِ جَنَّامَةَ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «مَرَّ فِي النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِالْأَبْوَاءِ أَوْ بِوَدَّانَ وَسُئِلَ عَنْ أَهْلِ الدَّارِ يُبَيِّتُونَ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ فَيُصَابُ مِنْ نِسَائِهِمْ وَذَرَارِيهِمْ قَالَ: هُمْ مِنْهُمْ (بخاري) ،شريف بَابُ أَهْلِ الدَّارِ يُبَيِّتُونَ فَيُصَابُ الْوِلْدَانُ وَالدَّرَارِيُّ {بَيَاتًا لَيْلًا لَيُبَيِّتَنَّهُ لَيْلًا يُبَيَّتُ لَيْلًا، نمبر 3012)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِرَمْيِهِمْ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِمْ مُسْلِمٌ أَسِيرٌ \ أنه قال: يا رسول الله أطفال المشركين نصيبهم في الغارة بالليل قال فذكره كنز العمال، في أحكام الجهاد من الأكمال،نمبر 11288)
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِرَمْيِهِمْ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِمْ مُسْلِمٌ أَسِيرٌ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: «وُجِدَتِ امْرَأَةٌ مَقْتُولَةً فِي بَعْضٍ مَغَازِي رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَنَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ قَتْلِ النِّسَاءِ وَالصَّبْيَانِ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ قَتْلِ النِّسَاءِ فِي الحَرْبِ، نمبر 3015) اصول : جو مجاہدین سامنے قتال کرنے آئے یا جوان ہونے کی وجہ سے آنا ممکن ہو تو ایسوں کو قتل کیا جائے گا۔
There is no harm in shooting them even if there is a Muslim captive or trader among them. If they shield themselves with Muslim children or captives, they do not refrain from shooting them, and they aim at the disbelievers. He said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'When an amir is appointed over an army... if they refuse, ask them for jizya; if they accept, accept from them and stop; if they refuse, seek help from Allah and fight them.' (Muslim, Sunan Abi Dawud). Evidence: (2) Hadith from Abu Ubayda: The Prophet besieged Ta'if and set up a catapult for 17 days. (3) Hadith from Ibn Umar: The Prophet burnt the date palms of Bani al-Nadir. (1) Hadith from as-Sa'b ibn Jaththama: The Prophet passed by al-Abwa and was asked about attacking the polytheists at night causing casualties among their women and children; he said: 'They are from them.' (Bukhari). (2) Hadith: Someone asked: O Messenger of Allah, do we kill children of polytheists in night raids? He mentioned it. (Kanz al-Ummal). (3) Hadith from Ibn Umar: A woman was found killed in a battle, so the Prophet forbade killing women and children. (Bukhari). Principle: Those fighters who come to fight or are likely to come due to youth should be killed.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage addresses a critical question in the laws of war: the permissibility of attacking the enemy when Muslims are present among them, either as captives, traders, or as human shields. The matn clearly states that shooting is permissible and Muslims should aim at the disbelievers, even if it risks harming the Muslims. This is based on the principle of necessity in jihad: the greater good of defeating the enemy outweighs the risk of collateral harm. The proofs include the famous hadith of the Prophet regarding the options given to the enemy (Islam, jizya, or war), and several incidents from the Prophet's life, such as the siege of Ta'if with catapults and the burning of palm trees. The hadith of as-Sa'b ibn Jaththama explicitly allows attacking at night even if it leads to accidental killing of women and children, as they are considered part of the enemy's forces. However, an exception is noted: the Prophet forbade deliberately killing women and children, indicating that while collateral damage is permitted, intentional killing of non-combatants is not. The Urdu principle at the end summarises that those who come to fight or are capable of fighting should be killed, providing a general rule for targeting.

Key Terms
لتّترس (al-tatarsus): Using human shields (here Muslim children or captives) to protect the enemy.
بَيَاتًا (bayatan): A night raid or surprise attack on the enemy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the Hanafi ruling say about firing at the enemy when they use Muslim children as human shields?
A) Firing is completely prohibited to protect the Muslims.
B) Firing is permissible but only if aiming at the disbelievers.
C) Firing is permissible only if the Muslims consent to being used as shields.
D) Firing is permissible only after negotiating for the release of the Muslims.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits attacking the enemy even when Muslims are used as shields, based on the hadith that women and children of the polytheists are considered part of the enemy, but with the condition of aiming at the disbelievers.
