Bombarding the Enemy with Muslim Human Shields
Ruling and proofs for bombarding enemy with Muslim shields

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bombarding an enemy that uses Muslim prisoners as shields and identify the key prophetic proofs.

Core Idea
Bombarding is permitted even with Muslim captives present, provided the aim is the enemy.

In war, difficult choices arise. What if the enemy shields themselves with Muslim captives? The Hanafi school, relying on prophetic practice and clear hadith, rules that bombardment may continue with the condition that the intention is to strike the enemy, not the Muslims. This lesson unpacks the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Question
The core question: Is it permissible to bombard an enemy position when Muslim prisoners, children, or traders are present as shields?
2
State the Hanafi Ruling
The text says 'لا بأس' – there is no harm in bombarding them. The Hanafi position is permissibility with the condition that the aim is the disbelievers.
The ruling is mubah (permissible).
3
Examine the Prophetic Evidence
Three key hadith are cited: (1) the hadith of Sa‘b ibn Jaththamah about night raids – the Prophet said 'They are from them' meaning women and children are considered part of the enemy camp. (2) The hadith of the Prophet using a mangonel at Ta'if, showing area bombardment is allowed. (3) The hadith of burning the palm trees of Bani Nadir, supported by a Quranic verse.
Each hadith supports the permissibility of causing collateral harm when necessary.
4
Understand the Principle of Intention
The key condition is that the Muslims intend to hit the enemy, not the Muslims. Unintentional harm to Muslim shields is overlooked in the pursuit of the greater military objective.
This is based on the principle of necessity and the lesser of two evils.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ السّير
القدوري مع احاديثه
وَلا بَأسَ بِرَميِهِم وَإِن كَانَ فِيهِم مُسلِمٌ أَسِيرٌ أَو تَاجِرٌ فَإِن تَتَرَّسُوا بِصِبيَانِ المُسلِمِينَ أَو بِالأَسَارَى لَم يَكُفُّوا عَن رَميِهِم وَيَقصِدُونَ بِالرَّميِ الكُفَّارَ
قَالَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ ، إِذَا أَمَّرَ أمير على جيش... فَإِن هُمْ أَبَوْا فَسَلْهُمُ الْخِزْيَةَ. فَإِن هُمْ أَجَابُوكَ فَاقْبَلْ مِنْهُمْ وَكُفَّ عَنْهُمْ. فَإِن هُمْ أَبَوْا فَاسْتَعِنْ بِاللَّهِ وَقَاتِلْهُمْ ، (مسلم شريف، باب تأمير الإمام الأمراء على البعوث ووصية إِيَّاهُمْ بِآدَابِ الْغَزْوِ وَغَيْرِهَا . نمبر 1731/سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي دُعَاءِ الْمُشْرِكِينَنمبر 2612)
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ أَبَوْا اسْتَعَانُوا عَلَيْهِمْ بِاللَّهِ \ عَنْ أَبِي عُبَيْدَةَ ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ حَاصَرَ أَهْلَ الطَّائِفِ، وَنَصَبَ عَلَيْهِمُ الْمَنْجَنِيقَ سَبْعَةَ عَشَرَ يَوْمًا، (سنن بيهقي، بَابُ قَطع الشَّجَرِ وَحَرْقِ الْمَنَازِلِ،نمبر 18120/ترمذي شريف، بَابُ مَا جَاءَفِي الْأَخْذِ مِنَ اللَّحْيَةِ، نمبر 2762)
وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ أَبَوْا اسْتَعَانُوا عَلَيْهِمْ بِاللَّهِ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِي الله عنهما قَالَ: «حَرَّقَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَخْلَ بَنِي النَّضِيرِ وَقَطَعَ، وَهِيَ الْبَوَيْرَةُ، فَنَزَلَتْ : {مَا قَطَعْتُمْ مِنْ لِينَةٍ أَوْ تَرَكْتُمُوهَا قَائِمَةً عَلَى أُصُولِهَا فَبِإِذْنِ اللهِ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ بَابُ حَدِيثِ بَنِي النضير، نمبر 4031/مسلم شريف ، بَاب جَوَازِ قَطع أَشْجَارِ الْكُفَّارِ وَتَحْرِيقِهَا ، نمبر 1746)
10 وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِرَمْيِهِمْ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِمْ مُسْلِمٌ أَسِيرٌ \ عَنِ الصَّعْبِ بْنِ جَنَّامَةَ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «مَرَّ فِي النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِالْأَبْوَاءِ أَوْ بِوَدَّانَ وَسُئِلَ عَنْ أَهْلِ الدَّارِ يُبَيِّتُونَ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ فَيُصَابُ مِنْ نِسَائِهِمْ وَذَرَارِيهِمْ قَالَ: هُمْ مِنْهُمْ (بخاري) ،شريف بَابُ أَهْلِ الدَّارِ يُبَيِّتُونَ فَيُصَابُ الْوِلْدَانُ وَالدَّرَارِيُّ {بَيَاتًا لَيْلًا لَيُبَيِّتَنَّهُ لَيْلًا يُبَيَّتُ لَيْلًا، نمبر 3012)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِرَمْيِهِمْ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِمْ مُسْلِمٌ أَسِيرٌ \ أنه قال: يا رسول الله أطفال المشركين نصيبهم في الغارة بالليل قال فذكره كنز العمال، في أحكام الجهاد من الأكمال،نمبر 11288)
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِرَمْيِهِمْ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِمْ مُسْلِمٌ أَسِيرٌ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: «وُجِدَتِ امْرَأَةٌ مَقْتُولَةً فِي بَعْضٍ مَغَازِي رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَنَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ قَتْلِ النِّسَاءِ وَالصَّبْيَانِ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ قَتْلِ النِّسَاءِ فِي الحَرْبِ، نمبر 3015)
اصول : جو مجاہدین سامنے قتال کرنے آئے یا جوان ہونے کی وجہ سے آنا ممکن ہو تو ایسوں کو قتل کیا جائے گا۔

كِتَابُ السّير
القدوري مع احاديثه
ل وَلَا بَأْسَ بِإِخْرَاجِ النِّسَاءِ وَالْمَصَاحِفِ مَعَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ إِذَا كَانَ عَسْكَرٌ عَظِيمٌ يُؤْمَنُ مَعَهُمْ وَيُكْرَهُ إِخْرَاجُ ذَلِكَ فِي سَرِيَّةٍ لَا يُؤْمَنُ عَلَيْهَا
وَلَا تُقَاتِلُ الْمَرْأَةُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِ زَوْجِهَا وَلَا الْعَبْدُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِ سَيِّدِهِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَهْجُمَ الْعَدُوُّ
وجه : (۴) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِرَمْيِهِمْ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِمْ مُسْلِمٌ أَسِيرٌ وَلَا تَقْتُلُوا الْوِلْدَانَ وَلَا الشُّيُوخَ وَلَا النِّسَاءَ،(سنن بيهقي، بَابُ مَنِ اخْتَارَ الْكَفَّ عَنِ الْقَطْعِ وَالتَّحْرِيقِ إِذَا كَانَ الْأَغْلَبُ أَنَّهَا سَتَصِيرُ دَارَ إِسْلَامِ أَوْ دَارَ عَهْدِ، نمبر 18125)
ال وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِإِخْرَاجِ النِّسَاءِ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما : أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم «نَهَى أَنْ يُسَافَرَ بِالْقُرْآنِ إِلَى أَرْضِ الْعَدُوّ ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ السَّفَرِ بِالْمَصَاحِفِ إِلَى أَرْضِ الْعَدُقِ، نمبر 2990 مسلم شريف، بَاب النَّهْيِ أَنْ يُسَافَرَ بِالْمُصْحَفِ إِلَى أَرْضِ الْكُفَّارِ إِذَا خِيفَ وُقُوعُهُ بِأَيْدِيهِمْ، نمبر 1869)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِإِخْرَاج النِّسَاءِ مَخَافَةَ أَنْ يَنَالَهُ العدو،(مسلم شريف،، بَاب النَّهْيِ أَنْ يُسَافَرَ بِالْمُصْحَفِ إِلَى أَرْضِ الْكُفَّارِ إِذَا خِيفَ وُقُوعُهُ بِأَيْدِيهِمْ، نمبر 1869)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا تُقَاتِلُ الْمَرْأَةُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِ زَوْجِهَا عَنِ الْحَارِثِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أَبِي ربِيعَةَ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ فِي بَعْضٍ مَغَازِيِهِ، فَمَرَّ بِأَنَاسٍ مِنْ مُزَيْنَةَ فَاتَّبَعَهُ عَبْدٌ لِامْرَأَةٍ مِنْهُمْ فَلَمَّا كَانَ فِي بَعْضِ الطَّرِيقِ سَلَّمَ عَلَيْهِ فَقَالَ: «فُلَانٌ؟» قَالَ: نَعَمْ، قَالَ: «مَا شَأْنُكَ؟» قَالَ: أُجَاهِدُ مَعَكَ قَالَ: «أَذِنَتْ لَكَ سَيِّدَتُكَ؟» قَالَ : لَا. قَالَ: «ارْجِعْ إِلَيْهَا فَأَخْبِرْهَا فَإِنَّ مَثَلَكَ مَثَلُ عَبْدِ لَا يُصَلِّي إِنْ مُتَّ قَبْلَ أَنْ تَرْجِعَ إِلَيْهَا الخ، مستدرك للحاكم ، وَأَمَّا حَدِيثُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ يَزِيدَ الْأَنْصَارِي، نمبر 2553)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا تُقَاتِلُ الْمَرْأَةُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِ زَوْجِهَا سَمِعْتُ عَبْدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ عَمْرٍو رضي الله عنهما يَقُولُ: «جَاءَ رَجُلٌ إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَاسْتَأْذَنَهُ فِي الْجِهَادِ فَقَالَ: أَحَيٌّ وَالِدَاكَ قَالَ: نَعَمْ قَالَ: فَفِيهِمَا فَجَاهِدٌ، (بخاري شريف، الجهَادِ بِإِذْنِ الْأَبَوَيْنِ ، نمبر 3004/مسلم شریف، باب بر الوالدين، وأنهما أحق به، نمبر 2549)
اصول 1 : عام حالات میں عورت کو شوہر کی اجازت کے بغیر اور غلام کو اپنے آقا کی اجازت کے بغیر قتال نہیں کرنا ہے ، ہاں البتہ دشمن چڑھ آئے تو بغیر اجازت کے بھی قتال جائز ہے۔
Book of Siyar. And there is no harm in bombarding them even if there is a Muslim prisoner or a trader among them. If they shield themselves with Muslim children or prisoners, they do not refrain from bombarding them, and they aim at the disbelievers with the bombardment. He said: The Messenger of Allah said: When an amir appoints a commander over an army... if they refuse, ask them for jizya. If they respond, accept from them and refrain from them. If they refuse, seek help from Allah and fight them. (Muslim, no. 1731/Abu Dawud, no. 2612) Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing: 'if they refuse, they seek help from Allah against them' from Abu Ubaydah that the Messenger of Allah besieged the people of Ta'if and set up a mangonel against them for seventeen days. (Bayhaqi, no. 18120/Tirmidhi, no. 2762) Evidence (3): The hadith for establishing: 'if they refuse, they seek help from Allah against them' from Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah burned and cut the palm trees of Bani Nadir, which is al-Buwayrah, and the verse was revealed: 'Whatever palm trees you cut down or left standing on their roots, it was by Allah's permission.' (Bukhari, no. 4031/Muslim, no. 1746) Evidence (1): The hadith for establishing: 'there is no harm in bombarding them even if there is a Muslim prisoner' from al-Sa'b ibn Jaththamah that the Prophet passed by al-Abwa' or Waddan and was asked about the people of a house who are attacked at night from the polytheists, and their women and children are hit. He said: 'They are from them.' (Bukhari, no. 3012) Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing: 'there is no harm in bombarding them even if there is a Muslim prisoner' that he said: O Messenger of Allah, do we hit the children of the polytheists in a night raid? He said... (Kanz al-Ummal, no. 11288) Evidence (3): The hadith for establishing: 'there is no harm in bombarding them even if there is a Muslim prisoner' from Ibn Umar that a woman was found killed in some of the military expeditions of the Messenger of Allah, and he forbade killing women and children. (Bukhari, no. 3015) Principle: Those fighters who come forward to fight or who may come because of their youth are to be killed. And there is no harm in taking out women and copies of the Quran with the Muslims when it is a large army with which they are secure, and it is disliked to take that out in a small detachment in which it is not secure. And a woman does not fight except with the permission of her husband, nor a slave except with the permission of his master, unless the enemy attacks. Evidence (4): The hadith for establishing: 'there is no harm in bombarding them even if there is a Muslim prisoner' and 'do not kill children, old men, or women.' (Bayhaqi, no. 18125) Evidence (1): The hadith for establishing: 'there is no harm in taking out women' from Abdullah ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah forbade traveling with the Quran to enemy territory. (Bukhari, no. 2990/Muslim, no. 1869) Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing: 'there is no harm in taking out women' for fear that the enemy might get it. (Muslim, no. 1869) Evidence (1): The hadith for establishing: 'a woman does not fight except with the permission of her husband' from al-Harith ibn Abdullah ibn Abi Rabi'ah that the Messenger of Allah was in one of his expeditions, and he passed by some people of Muzaynah, and a slave of a woman among them followed him. When he was on the road, he greeted him and said: 'So-and-so?' He said: Yes. He said: 'What is your matter?' He said: I will fight alongside you. He said: 'Did your mistress give you permission?' He said: No. He said: 'Return to her and inform her, for your example is that of a slave who does not pray; if you die before returning to her...' (Mustadrak al-Hakim, no. 2553) Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing: 'a woman does not fight except with the permission of her husband' that I heard Abdullah ibn Amr say: A man came to the Prophet and asked his permission for jihad. He said: 'Are your parents alive?' He said: Yes. He said: 'Then strive with them.' (Bukhari, no. 3004/Muslim, no. 2549) Principle 1: In normal circumstances, a woman is not to fight without her husband's permission, nor a slave without his master's permission; however, if the enemy attacks, fighting is permissible even without permission.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Siyar covers three interrelated rulings on warfare. The first ruling permits bombarding the enemy even if they shield themselves with Muslim prisoners, children, or traders, provided the Muslims aim at the enemy and not intentionally at the Muslims. The author cites multiple hadith proofs: the hadith of Sa'b ibn Jaththamah about night raids where women and children may be hit unintentionally, the hadith of the Prophet allowing such actions because they are 'from them' (i.e., considered part of the enemy camp), and the incident of the Prophet using a mangonel at Ta'if and burning the palm trees of Bani Nadir, which was permitted by Quranic verse. The second ruling addresses taking women and copies of the Quran along with the army. If the army is large and secure, it is permissible; if it is a small detachment where loss is feared, it is disliked. The proof is the prohibition of traveling with the Quran to enemy territory for fear it may fall into enemy hands. The third ruling states that a woman may not fight without her husband's permission, nor a slave without his master's permission, except in the case of a sudden enemy attack where defense is necessary. The proofs include the hadith of a slave following the Prophet without his mistress's permission and the hadith about the man whose parents were alive. The Urdu commentary at the end summarizes: fighters who can fight are to be killed; women and slaves need permission except in self-defense.

Key Terms
تَتَرَّسُوا (tatarrasū): They shield themselves (with human shields)
أَسِير (asīr): Prisoner of war captured by enemy
مَنْجَنِيق (manjanīq): Mangonel, a type of siege engine used to hurl stones
بَوَيْرَة (buwayrah): Name of the palm grove of Bani Nadir that was burned

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, if enemy fighters shield themselves with Muslim children, what should the Muslim army do?
A) Cease bombardment to avoid harming the children.
B) Continue bombardment but aim only at the enemy fighters.
C) Retreat and negotiate for the children's release first.
D) Attack only with swords to avoid area damage.

Key Takeaway
Bombarding an enemy that uses Muslim shields is permissible in the Hanafi school as long as the intention is to hit the enemy, not the Muslims.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
beginner
5 min
Taking Women and Qur'ans on Expedition
Ruling on taking women and Qur'ans on campaign

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on taking women and copies of the Quran on a military expedition and differentiate between a large army and a small detachment based on the condition of security.

Core Idea
Women and Qur'ans may accompany a large, secure army but not a small detachment where loss is feared.

Traveling with women and sacred texts on a campaign carries risks of capture and desecration. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi distinction: when the army is large and secure, it is permissible; when it is a small detachment at risk, it is disliked. The proof comes from a hadith prohibiting traveling with the Quran to enemy lands due to such risks.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Two Scenarios
The act is taking women and copies of the Quran (masahif) with the Muslim army. Two scenarios: (1) a large army (askar 'azim) where security is assured, (2) a small detachment (sariyyah) where security is not assured.
2
State the Ruling for Each Scenario
The text says: 'لا بأس' (no harm) for a large army, and 'يُكره' (it is disliked) for a small detachment. The ruling is mubah for the first, makruh tanzihi for the second.
The underlying rationale is the risk of the women and Qur'ans falling into enemy hands.
3
Analyze the Proof
The author cites the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar that the Prophet forbade traveling with the Quran to enemy territory. This prohibition indicates that when there is a risk of desecration, it is not allowed; conversely, when the army is large and security is high, the risk is minimal, so the prohibition is lifted.
The same hadith is used with two 'wujuh' (aspects) to support the permissibility in secure conditions.
4
Understand the Principle
The ruling balances the benefit of having women and Qur'ans with the risk of them being captured or desecrated. Security is the operative condition (illah).
This is an example of the maxim 'al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir'? Actually it's about avoiding harm.

القدوري مع احاديثه
وَلا بَأسَ بِرَميِهِم وَإِن كَانَ فِيهِم مُسلِمٌ أَسِيرٌ أَو تَاجِرٌ فَإِن تَتَرَّسُوا بِصِبيَانِ المُسلِمِينَ أَو بِالأَسَارَى لَم يَكُفُّوا عَن رَميِهِم وَيَقصِدُونَ بِالرَّميِ الكُفَّارَ
قَالَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ ، إِذَا أَمَّرَ أمير على جيش... فَإِن هُمْ أَبَوْا فَسَلْهُمُ الْخِزْيَةَ. فَإِن هُمْ أَجَابُوكَ فَاقْبَلْ مِنْهُمْ وَكُفَّ عَنْهُمْ. فَإِن هُمْ أَبَوْا فَاسْتَعِنْ بِاللَّهِ وَقَاتِلْهُمْ ، (مسلم شريف، باب تأمير الإمام الأمراء على البعوث ووصية إِيَّاهُمْ بِآدَابِ الْغَزْوِ وَغَيْرِهَا . نمبر 1731/سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي دُعَاءِ الْمُشْرِكِينَنمبر 2612)
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ أَبَوْا اسْتَعَانُوا عَلَيْهِمْ بِاللَّهِ \ عَنْ أَبِي عُبَيْدَةَ ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ حَاصَرَ أَهْلَ الطَّائِفِ، وَنَصَبَ عَلَيْهِمُ الْمَنْجَنِيقَ سَبْعَةَ عَشَرَ يَوْمًا، (سنن بيهقي، بَابُ قَطع الشَّجَرِ وَحَرْقِ الْمَنَازِلِ،نمبر 18120/ترمذي شريف، بَابُ مَا جَاءَفِي الْأَخْذِ مِنَ اللَّحْيَةِ، نمبر 2762)
وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ أَبَوْا اسْتَعَانُوا عَلَيْهِمْ بِاللَّهِ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِي الله عنهما قَالَ: «حَرَّقَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَخْلَ بَنِي النَّضِيرِ وَقَطَعَ، وَهِيَ الْبَوَيْرَةُ، فَنَزَلَتْ : {مَا قَطَعْتُمْ مِنْ لِينَةٍ أَوْ تَرَكْتُمُوهَا قَائِمَةً عَلَى أُصُولِهَا فَبِإِذْنِ اللهِ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ بَابُ حَدِيثِ بَنِي النضير، نمبر 4031/مسلم شريف ، بَاب جَوَازِ قَطع أَشْجَارِ الْكُفَّارِ وَتَحْرِيقِهَا ، نمبر 1746)
10 وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِرَمْيِهِمْ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِمْ مُسْلِمٌ أَسِيرٌ \ عَنِ الصَّعْبِ بْنِ جَنَّامَةَ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «مَرَّ فِي النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِالْأَبْوَاءِ أَوْ بِوَدَّانَ وَسُئِلَ عَنْ أَهْلِ الدَّارِ يُبَيِّتُونَ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ فَيُصَابُ مِنْ نِسَائِهِمْ وَذَرَارِيهِمْ قَالَ: هُمْ مِنْهُمْ (بخاري) ،شريف بَابُ أَهْلِ الدَّارِ يُبَيِّتُونَ فَيُصَابُ الْوِلْدَانُ وَالدَّرَارِيُّ {بَيَاتًا لَيْلًا لَيُبَيِّتَنَّهُ لَيْلًا يُبَيَّتُ لَيْلًا، نمبر 3012)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِرَمْيِهِمْ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِمْ مُسْلِمٌ أَسِيرٌ \ أنه قال: يا رسول الله أطفال المشركين نصيبهم في الغارة بالليل قال فذكره كنز العمال، في أحكام الجهاد من الأكمال،نمبر 11288)
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِرَمْيِهِمْ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِمْ مُسْلِمٌ أَسِيرٌ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: «وُجِدَتِ امْرَأَةٌ مَقْتُولَةً فِي بَعْضٍ مَغَازِي رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَنَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ قَتْلِ النِّسَاءِ وَالصَّبْيَانِ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ قَتْلِ النِّسَاءِ فِي الحَرْبِ، نمبر 3015)
اصول : جو مجاہدین سامنے قتال کرنے آئے یا جوان ہونے کی وجہ سے آنا ممکن ہو تو ایسوں کو قتل کیا جائے گا۔

كِتَابُ السّير
القدوري مع احاديثه
ل وَلَا بَأْسَ بِإِخْرَاجِ النِّسَاءِ وَالْمَصَاحِفِ مَعَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ إِذَا كَانَ عَسْكَرٌ عَظِيمٌ يُؤْمَنُ مَعَهُمْ وَيُكْرَهُ إِخْرَاجُ ذَلِكَ فِي سَرِيَّةٍ لَا يُؤْمَنُ عَلَيْهَا
وَلَا تُقَاتِلُ الْمَرْأَةُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِ زَوْجِهَا وَلَا الْعَبْدُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِ سَيِّدِهِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَهْجُمَ الْعَدُوُّ
وجه : (۴) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِرَمْيِهِمْ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِمْ مُسْلِمٌ أَسِيرٌ وَلَا تَقْتُلُوا الْوِلْدَانَ وَلَا الشُّيُوخَ وَلَا النِّسَاءَ،(سنن بيهقي، بَابُ مَنِ اخْتَارَ الْكَفَّ عَنِ الْقَطْعِ وَالتَّحْرِيقِ إِذَا كَانَ الْأَغْلَبُ أَنَّهَا سَتَصِيرُ دَارَ إِسْلَامِ أَوْ دَارَ عَهْدِ، نمبر 18125)
ال وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِإِخْرَاجِ النِّسَاءِ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما : أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم «نَهَى أَنْ يُسَافَرَ بِالْقُرْآنِ إِلَى أَرْضِ الْعَدُوّ ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ السَّفَرِ بِالْمَصَاحِفِ إِلَى أَرْضِ الْعَدُقِ، نمبر 2990 مسلم شريف، بَاب النَّهْيِ أَنْ يُسَافَرَ بِالْمُصْحَفِ إِلَى أَرْضِ الْكُفَّارِ إِذَا خِيفَ وُقُوعُهُ بِأَيْدِيهِمْ، نمبر 1869)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِإِخْرَاج النِّسَاءِ مَخَافَةَ أَنْ يَنَالَهُ العدو،(مسلم شريف،، بَاب النَّهْيِ أَنْ يُسَافَرَ بِالْمُصْحَفِ إِلَى أَرْضِ الْكُفَّارِ إِذَا خِيفَ وُقُوعُهُ بِأَيْدِيهِمْ، نمبر 1869)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا تُقَاتِلُ الْمَرْأَةُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِ زَوْجِهَا عَنِ الْحَارِثِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أَبِي ربِيعَةَ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ فِي بَعْضٍ مَغَازِيِهِ، فَمَرَّ بِأَنَاسٍ مِنْ مُزَيْنَةَ فَاتَّبَعَهُ عَبْدٌ لِامْرَأَةٍ مِنْهُمْ فَلَمَّا كَانَ فِي بَعْضِ الطَّرِيقِ سَلَّمَ عَلَيْهِ فَقَالَ: «فُلَانٌ؟» قَالَ: نَعَمْ، قَالَ: «مَا شَأْنُكَ؟» قَالَ: أُجَاهِدُ مَعَكَ قَالَ: «أَذِنَتْ لَكَ سَيِّدَتُكَ؟» قَالَ : لَا. قَالَ: «ارْجِعْ إِلَيْهَا فَأَخْبِرْهَا فَإِنَّ مَثَلَكَ مَثَلُ عَبْدِ لَا يُصَلِّي إِنْ مُتَّ قَبْلَ أَنْ تَرْجِعَ إِلَيْهَا الخ، مستدرك للحاكم ، وَأَمَّا حَدِيثُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ يَزِيدَ الْأَنْصَارِي، نمبر 2553)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا تُقَاتِلُ الْمَرْأَةُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِ زَوْجِهَا سَمِعْتُ عَبْدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ عَمْرٍو رضي الله عنهما يَقُولُ: «جَاءَ رَجُلٌ إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَاسْتَأْذَنَهُ فِي الْجِهَادِ فَقَالَ: أَحَيٌّ وَالِدَاكَ قَالَ: نَعَمْ قَالَ: فَفِيهِمَا فَجَاهِدٌ، (بخاري شريف، الجهَادِ بِإِذْنِ الْأَبَوَيْنِ ، نمبر 3004/مسلم شریف، باب بر الوالدين، وأنهما أحق به، نمبر 2549)
اصول 1 : عام حالات میں عورت کو شوہر کی اجازت کے بغیر اور غلام کو اپنے آقا کی اجازت کے بغیر قتال نہیں کرنا ہے ، ہاں البتہ دشمن چڑھ آئے تو بغیر اجازت کے بھی قتال جائز ہے۔
Book of Siyar. And there is no harm in bombarding them even if there is a Muslim prisoner or a trader among them. If they shield themselves with Muslim children or prisoners, they do not refrain from bombarding them, and they aim at the disbelievers with the bombardment. He said: The Messenger of Allah said: When an amir appoints a commander over an army... if they refuse, ask them for jizya. If they respond, accept from them and refrain from them. If they refuse, seek help from Allah and fight them. (Muslim, no. 1731/Abu Dawud, no. 2612) Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing: 'if they refuse, they seek help from Allah against them' from Abu Ubaydah that the Messenger of Allah besieged the people of Ta'if and set up a mangonel against them for seventeen days. (Bayhaqi, no. 18120/Tirmidhi, no. 2762) Evidence (3): The hadith for establishing: 'if they refuse, they seek help from Allah against them' from Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah burned and cut the palm trees of Bani Nadir, which is al-Buwayrah, and the verse was revealed: 'Whatever palm trees you cut down or left standing on their roots, it was by Allah's permission.' (Bukhari, no. 4031/Muslim, no. 1746) Evidence (1): The hadith for establishing: 'there is no harm in bombarding them even if there is a Muslim prisoner' from al-Sa'b ibn Jaththamah that the Prophet passed by al-Abwa' or Waddan and was asked about the people of a house who are attacked at night from the polytheists, and their women and children are hit. He said: 'They are from them.' (Bukhari, no. 3012) Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing: 'there is no harm in bombarding them even if there is a Muslim prisoner' that he said: O Messenger of Allah, do we hit the children of the polytheists in a night raid? He said... (Kanz al-Ummal, no. 11288) Evidence (3): The hadith for establishing: 'there is no harm in bombarding them even if there is a Muslim prisoner' from Ibn Umar that a woman was found killed in some of the military expeditions of the Messenger of Allah, and he forbade killing women and children. (Bukhari, no. 3015) Principle: Those fighters who come forward to fight or who may come because of their youth are to be killed. And there is no harm in taking out women and copies of the Quran with the Muslims when it is a large army with which they are secure, and it is disliked to take that out in a small detachment in which it is not secure. And a woman does not fight except with the permission of her husband, nor a slave except with the permission of his master, unless the enemy attacks. Evidence (4): The hadith for establishing: 'there is no harm in bombarding them even if there is a Muslim prisoner' and 'do not kill children, old men, or women.' (Bayhaqi, no. 18125) Evidence (1): The hadith for establishing: 'there is no harm in taking out women' from Abdullah ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah forbade traveling with the Quran to enemy territory. (Bukhari, no. 2990/Muslim, no. 1869) Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing: 'there is no harm in taking out women' for fear that the enemy might get it. (Muslim, no. 1869) Evidence (1): The hadith for establishing: 'a woman does not fight except with the permission of her husband' from al-Harith ibn Abdullah ibn Abi Rabi'ah that the Messenger of Allah was in one of his expeditions, and he passed by some people of Muzaynah, and a slave of a woman among them followed him. When he was on the road, he greeted him and said: 'So-and-so?' He said: Yes. He said: 'What is your matter?' He said: I will fight alongside you. He said: 'Did your mistress give you permission?' He said: No. He said: 'Return to her and inform her, for your example is that of a slave who does not pray; if you die before returning to her...' (Mustadrak al-Hakim, no. 2553) Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing: 'a woman does not fight except with the permission of her husband' that I heard Abdullah ibn Amr say: A man came to the Prophet and asked his permission for jihad. He said: 'Are your parents alive?' He said: Yes. He said: 'Then strive with them.' (Bukhari, no. 3004/Muslim, no. 2549) Principle 1: In normal circumstances, a woman is not to fight without her husband's permission, nor a slave without his master's permission; however, if the enemy attacks, fighting is permissible even without permission.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Siyar covers three interrelated rulings on warfare. The first ruling permits bombarding the enemy even if they shield themselves with Muslim prisoners, children, or traders, provided the Muslims aim at the enemy and not intentionally at the Muslims. The author cites multiple hadith proofs: the hadith of Sa'b ibn Jaththamah about night raids where women and children may be hit unintentionally, the hadith of the Prophet allowing such actions because they are 'from them' (i.e., considered part of the enemy camp), and the incident of the Prophet using a mangonel at Ta'if and burning the palm trees of Bani Nadir, which was permitted by Quranic verse. The second ruling addresses taking women and copies of the Quran along with the army. If the army is large and secure, it is permissible; if it is a small detachment where loss is feared, it is disliked. The proof is the prohibition of traveling with the Quran to enemy territory for fear it may fall into enemy hands. The third ruling states that a woman may not fight without her husband's permission, nor a slave without his master's permission, except in the case of a sudden enemy attack where defense is necessary. The proofs include the hadith of a slave following the Prophet without his mistress's permission and the hadith about the man whose parents were alive. The Urdu commentary at the end summarizes: fighters who can fight are to be killed; women and slaves need permission except in self-defense.

Key Terms
سَرِيَّة (sariyyah): Small military detachment sent for raid or reconnaissance

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, when is it permissible to take women and copies of the Quran with the Muslim army?
A) Only when there is a large army where their security is assured.
B) Always, because they provide comfort and religious guidance.
C) Only when the army is small to avoid burden.
D) Never, because the Prophet forbade traveling with the Quran to enemy land.

Key Takeaway
Taking women and Qur'ans on campaign is permissible when the army is large and secure; otherwise it is disliked due to risk of capture.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
6 min
Women and Slaves Fighting: Permission and Exception
Ruling on women and slaves fighting with permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a woman needs her husband's permission and a slave his master's permission to fight, and identify the exception for a sudden enemy attack.

Core Idea
A woman or slave may not fight without permission, except in immediate self-defense.

Jihad is a collective obligation, but not everyone has the autonomy to join. This lesson covers the rule that women and slaves must obtain permission from their guardians to participate in combat, based on prophetic hadith. However, if the enemy attacks suddenly, permission is not required as defense becomes obligatory upon all.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Subjects and the General Rule
The subjects are women (al-mar'ah) and slaves (al-'abd). The general rule: They do not fight except with permission – the woman from her husband, the slave from his master.
The default is prohibition (or non-permissibility) without permission.
2
Note the Exception
The exception: 'illa an yahjuma al-'aduww' – unless the enemy attacks suddenly. In that case, they may fight without permission.
This is because defense against a sudden attack becomes a personal obligation (fard 'ayn).
3
Examine the Proofs
Two hadith are cited: (1) The hadith of a slave who followed the Prophet without his mistress's permission; the Prophet told him to go back and get permission, comparing him to a slave who does not pray – indicating that fighting without permission is akin to disobedience. (2) The hadith of a man who sought permission for jihad; the Prophet asked if his parents were alive and told him to strive with them – implying that parental permission is analogous.
The proofs establish that permission is required from those in authority over the individual.
4
Apply the Principle
In normal circumstances, the authority of the husband/master takes precedence over the general call to jihad. But when defense is urgent, the necessity overrides the permission requirement.
This is an example of the maxim 'al-darurah tubih al-mahzurat' (necessity permits the prohibited).

كِتَابُ السّير
القدوري مع احاديثه
وَلا بَأسَ بِرَميِهِم وَإِن كَانَ فِيهِم مُسلِمٌ أَسِيرٌ أَو تَاجِرٌ فَإِن تَتَرَّسُوا بِصِبيَانِ المُسلِمِينَ أَو بِالأَسَارَى لَم يَكُفُّوا عَن رَميِهِم وَيَقصِدُونَ بِالرَّميِ الكُفَّارَ
قَالَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ ، إِذَا أَمَّرَ أمير على جيش... فَإِن هُمْ أَبَوْا فَسَلْهُمُ الْخِزْيَةَ. فَإِن هُمْ أَجَابُوكَ فَاقْبَلْ مِنْهُمْ وَكُفَّ عَنْهُمْ. فَإِن هُمْ أَبَوْا فَاسْتَعِنْ بِاللَّهِ وَقَاتِلْهُمْ ، (مسلم شريف، باب تأمير الإمام الأمراء على البعوث ووصية إِيَّاهُمْ بِآدَابِ الْغَزْوِ وَغَيْرِهَا . نمبر 1731/سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي دُعَاءِ الْمُشْرِكِينَنمبر 2612)
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ أَبَوْا اسْتَعَانُوا عَلَيْهِمْ بِاللَّهِ \ عَنْ أَبِي عُبَيْدَةَ ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ حَاصَرَ أَهْلَ الطَّائِفِ، وَنَصَبَ عَلَيْهِمُ الْمَنْجَنِيقَ سَبْعَةَ عَشَرَ يَوْمًا، (سنن بيهقي، بَابُ قَطع الشَّجَرِ وَحَرْقِ الْمَنَازِلِ،نمبر 18120/ترمذي شريف، بَابُ مَا جَاءَفِي الْأَخْذِ مِنَ اللَّحْيَةِ، نمبر 2762)
وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ أَبَوْا اسْتَعَانُوا عَلَيْهِمْ بِاللَّهِ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِي الله عنهما قَالَ: «حَرَّقَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَخْلَ بَنِي النَّضِيرِ وَقَطَعَ، وَهِيَ الْبَوَيْرَةُ، فَنَزَلَتْ : {مَا قَطَعْتُمْ مِنْ لِينَةٍ أَوْ تَرَكْتُمُوهَا قَائِمَةً عَلَى أُصُولِهَا فَبِإِذْنِ اللهِ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ بَابُ حَدِيثِ بَنِي النضير، نمبر 4031/مسلم شريف ، بَاب جَوَازِ قَطع أَشْجَارِ الْكُفَّارِ وَتَحْرِيقِهَا ، نمبر 1746)
10 وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِرَمْيِهِمْ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِمْ مُسْلِمٌ أَسِيرٌ \ عَنِ الصَّعْبِ بْنِ جَنَّامَةَ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «مَرَّ فِي النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِالْأَبْوَاءِ أَوْ بِوَدَّانَ وَسُئِلَ عَنْ أَهْلِ الدَّارِ يُبَيِّتُونَ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ فَيُصَابُ مِنْ نِسَائِهِمْ وَذَرَارِيهِمْ قَالَ: هُمْ مِنْهُمْ (بخاري) ،شريف بَابُ أَهْلِ الدَّارِ يُبَيِّتُونَ فَيُصَابُ الْوِلْدَانُ وَالدَّرَارِيُّ {بَيَاتًا لَيْلًا لَيُبَيِّتَنَّهُ لَيْلًا يُبَيَّتُ لَيْلًا، نمبر 3012)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِرَمْيِهِمْ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِمْ مُسْلِمٌ أَسِيرٌ \ أنه قال: يا رسول الله أطفال المشركين نصيبهم في الغارة بالليل قال فذكره كنز العمال، في أحكام الجهاد من الأكمال،نمبر 11288)
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِرَمْيِهِمْ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِمْ مُسْلِمٌ أَسِيرٌ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: «وُجِدَتِ امْرَأَةٌ مَقْتُولَةً فِي بَعْضٍ مَغَازِي رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَنَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ قَتْلِ النِّسَاءِ وَالصَّبْيَانِ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ قَتْلِ النِّسَاءِ فِي الحَرْبِ، نمبر 3015)
اصول : جو مجاہدین سامنے قتال کرنے آئے یا جوان ہونے کی وجہ سے آنا ممکن ہو تو ایسوں کو قتل کیا جائے گا۔

كِتَابُ السّير
القدوري مع احاديثه
ل وَلَا بَأْسَ بِإِخْرَاجِ النِّسَاءِ وَالْمَصَاحِفِ مَعَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ إِذَا كَانَ عَسْكَرٌ عَظِيمٌ يُؤْمَنُ مَعَهُمْ وَيُكْرَهُ إِخْرَاجُ ذَلِكَ فِي سَرِيَّةٍ لَا يُؤْمَنُ عَلَيْهَا
وَلَا تُقَاتِلُ الْمَرْأَةُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِ زَوْجِهَا وَلَا الْعَبْدُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِ سَيِّدِهِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَهْجُمَ الْعَدُوُّ
وجه : (۴) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِرَمْيِهِمْ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِمْ مُسْلِمٌ أَسِيرٌ وَلَا تَقْتُلُوا الْوِلْدَانَ وَلَا الشُّيُوخَ وَلَا النِّسَاءَ،(سنن بيهقي، بَابُ مَنِ اخْتَارَ الْكَفَّ عَنِ الْقَطْعِ وَالتَّحْرِيقِ إِذَا كَانَ الْأَغْلَبُ أَنَّهَا سَتَصِيرُ دَارَ إِسْلَامِ أَوْ دَارَ عَهْدِ، نمبر 18125)
ال وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِإِخْرَاجِ النِّسَاءِ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما : أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم «نَهَى أَنْ يُسَافَرَ بِالْقُرْآنِ إِلَى أَرْضِ الْعَدُوّ ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ السَّفَرِ بِالْمَصَاحِفِ إِلَى أَرْضِ الْعَدُقِ، نمبر 2990 مسلم شريف، بَاب النَّهْيِ أَنْ يُسَافَرَ بِالْمُصْحَفِ إِلَى أَرْضِ الْكُفَّارِ إِذَا خِيفَ وُقُوعُهُ بِأَيْدِيهِمْ، نمبر 1869)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ بِإِخْرَاج النِّسَاءِ مَخَافَةَ أَنْ يَنَالَهُ العدو،(مسلم شريف،، بَاب النَّهْيِ أَنْ يُسَافَرَ بِالْمُصْحَفِ إِلَى أَرْضِ الْكُفَّارِ إِذَا خِيفَ وُقُوعُهُ بِأَيْدِيهِمْ، نمبر 1869)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا تُقَاتِلُ الْمَرْأَةُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِ زَوْجِهَا عَنِ الْحَارِثِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أَبِي ربِيعَةَ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ فِي بَعْضٍ مَغَازِيِهِ، فَمَرَّ بِأَنَاسٍ مِنْ مُزَيْنَةَ فَاتَّبَعَهُ عَبْدٌ لِامْرَأَةٍ مِنْهُمْ فَلَمَّا كَانَ فِي بَعْضِ الطَّرِيقِ سَلَّمَ عَلَيْهِ فَقَالَ: «فُلَانٌ؟» قَالَ: نَعَمْ، قَالَ: «مَا شَأْنُكَ؟» قَالَ: أُجَاهِدُ مَعَكَ قَالَ: «أَذِنَتْ لَكَ سَيِّدَتُكَ؟» قَالَ : لَا. قَالَ: «ارْجِعْ إِلَيْهَا فَأَخْبِرْهَا فَإِنَّ مَثَلَكَ مَثَلُ عَبْدِ لَا يُصَلِّي إِنْ مُتَّ قَبْلَ أَنْ تَرْجِعَ إِلَيْهَا الخ، مستدرك للحاكم ، وَأَمَّا حَدِيثُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ يَزِيدَ الْأَنْصَارِي، نمبر 2553)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا تُقَاتِلُ الْمَرْأَةُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِ زَوْجِهَا سَمِعْتُ عَبْدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ عَمْرٍو رضي الله عنهما يَقُولُ: «جَاءَ رَجُلٌ إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَاسْتَأْذَنَهُ فِي الْجِهَادِ فَقَالَ: أَحَيٌّ وَالِدَاكَ قَالَ: نَعَمْ قَالَ: فَفِيهِمَا فَجَاهِدٌ، (بخاري شريف، الجهَادِ بِإِذْنِ الْأَبَوَيْنِ ، نمبر 3004/مسلم شریف، باب بر الوالدين، وأنهما أحق به، نمبر 2549)
اصول 1 : عام حالات میں عورت کو شوہر کی اجازت کے بغیر اور غلام کو اپنے آقا کی اجازت کے بغیر قتال نہیں کرنا ہے ، ہاں البتہ دشمن چڑھ آئے تو بغیر اجازت کے بھی قتال جائز ہے۔
Book of Siyar. And there is no harm in bombarding them even if there is a Muslim prisoner or a trader among them. If they shield themselves with Muslim children or prisoners, they do not refrain from bombarding them, and they aim at the disbelievers with the bombardment. He said: The Messenger of Allah said: When an amir appoints a commander over an army... if they refuse, ask them for jizya. If they respond, accept from them and refrain from them. If they refuse, seek help from Allah and fight them. (Muslim, no. 1731/Abu Dawud, no. 2612) Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing: 'if they refuse, they seek help from Allah against them' from Abu Ubaydah that the Messenger of Allah besieged the people of Ta'if and set up a mangonel against them for seventeen days. (Bayhaqi, no. 18120/Tirmidhi, no. 2762) Evidence (3): The hadith for establishing: 'if they refuse, they seek help from Allah against them' from Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah burned and cut the palm trees of Bani Nadir, which is al-Buwayrah, and the verse was revealed: 'Whatever palm trees you cut down or left standing on their roots, it was by Allah's permission.' (Bukhari, no. 4031/Muslim, no. 1746) Evidence (1): The hadith for establishing: 'there is no harm in bombarding them even if there is a Muslim prisoner' from al-Sa'b ibn Jaththamah that the Prophet passed by al-Abwa' or Waddan and was asked about the people of a house who are attacked at night from the polytheists, and their women and children are hit. He said: 'They are from them.' (Bukhari, no. 3012) Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing: 'there is no harm in bombarding them even if there is a Muslim prisoner' that he said: O Messenger of Allah, do we hit the children of the polytheists in a night raid? He said... (Kanz al-Ummal, no. 11288) Evidence (3): The hadith for establishing: 'there is no harm in bombarding them even if there is a Muslim prisoner' from Ibn Umar that a woman was found killed in some of the military expeditions of the Messenger of Allah, and he forbade killing women and children. (Bukhari, no. 3015) Principle: Those fighters who come forward to fight or who may come because of their youth are to be killed. And there is no harm in taking out women and copies of the Quran with the Muslims when it is a large army with which they are secure, and it is disliked to take that out in a small detachment in which it is not secure. And a woman does not fight except with the permission of her husband, nor a slave except with the permission of his master, unless the enemy attacks. Evidence (4): The hadith for establishing: 'there is no harm in bombarding them even if there is a Muslim prisoner' and 'do not kill children, old men, or women.' (Bayhaqi, no. 18125) Evidence (1): The hadith for establishing: 'there is no harm in taking out women' from Abdullah ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah forbade traveling with the Quran to enemy territory. (Bukhari, no. 2990/Muslim, no. 1869) Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing: 'there is no harm in taking out women' for fear that the enemy might get it. (Muslim, no. 1869) Evidence (1): The hadith for establishing: 'a woman does not fight except with the permission of her husband' from al-Harith ibn Abdullah ibn Abi Rabi'ah that the Messenger of Allah was in one of his expeditions, and he passed by some people of Muzaynah, and a slave of a woman among them followed him. When he was on the road, he greeted him and said: 'So-and-so?' He said: Yes. He said: 'What is your matter?' He said: I will fight alongside you. He said: 'Did your mistress give you permission?' He said: No. He said: 'Return to her and inform her, for your example is that of a slave who does not pray; if you die before returning to her...' (Mustadrak al-Hakim, no. 2553) Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing: 'a woman does not fight except with the permission of her husband' that I heard Abdullah ibn Amr say: A man came to the Prophet and asked his permission for jihad. He said: 'Are your parents alive?' He said: Yes. He said: 'Then strive with them.' (Bukhari, no. 3004/Muslim, no. 2549) Principle 1: In normal circumstances, a woman is not to fight without her husband's permission, nor a slave without his master's permission; however, if the enemy attacks, fighting is permissible even without permission.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Siyar covers three interrelated rulings on warfare. The first ruling permits bombarding the enemy even if they shield themselves with Muslim prisoners, children, or traders, provided the Muslims aim at the enemy and not intentionally at the Muslims. The author cites multiple hadith proofs: the hadith of Sa'b ibn Jaththamah about night raids where women and children may be hit unintentionally, the hadith of the Prophet allowing such actions because they are 'from them' (i.e., considered part of the enemy camp), and the incident of the Prophet using a mangonel at Ta'if and burning the palm trees of Bani Nadir, which was permitted by Quranic verse. The second ruling addresses taking women and copies of the Quran along with the army. If the army is large and secure, it is permissible; if it is a small detachment where loss is feared, it is disliked. The proof is the prohibition of traveling with the Quran to enemy territory for fear it may fall into enemy hands. The third ruling states that a woman may not fight without her husband's permission, nor a slave without his master's permission, except in the case of a sudden enemy attack where defense is necessary. The proofs include the hadith of a slave following the Prophet without his mistress's permission and the hadith about the man whose parents were alive. The Urdu commentary at the end summarizes: fighters who can fight are to be killed; women and slaves need permission except in self-defense.

Key Terms
أَسِير (asīr): Prisoner of war captured by enemy

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, when is a woman allowed to fight without her husband's permission?
A) When she is skilled in combat.
B) When the enemy attacks suddenly.
C) When her husband is also fighting.
D) Never, permission is always required.

Key Takeaway
Women and slaves must obtain permission from their guardians to fight, except in a sudden enemy attack where defense becomes obligatory.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
6 min
Permissibility of Using War Booty Without Distribution
Ruling on immediate use of booty without formal division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on immediate use of war booty in Dar al-Harb and identify the conditions and proofs for its permissibility.

Core Idea
Soldiers may use captured provisions immediately for essential needs without formal distribution; this is a necessity-based dispensation.

This passage from Al-Quduri presents a practical ruling for Muslims on campaign: what can they do with spoils before formal division? The matn lists permitted uses—fodder, food, firewood, oil, weapons—and the commentary supplies four hadith proofs. Understanding this ruling helps distinguish between permissible temporary use and prohibited ownership without proper division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize the matn phrase 'لا بأس' indicating permissibility (jā'iz). List the four permitted categories: fodder for animals, food for consumption, firewood and oil for use, and weapons for fighting.
The ruling is a dispensation (rukhṣah) for military necessity.
2
Understand the condition of 'without distribution'
The permission is given 'بغير قسمة'—without formal division. This means immediate use is allowed, but ownership and sale require distribution. Use is temporary and for need.
Distribution (qismah) is required for permanent ownership and trade.
3
Examine the four hadith proofs
Each hadith supports a different aspect: (1) Ibn Umar: Companions consumed honey/grapes without setting aside. (2) Abu Ubaidah: using an enemy's sword in battle. (3) Ibn Abi Awfa: taking only enough food at Khaybar. (4) Prohibition of plundering (nuhbah) compared to carrion.
The fourth hadith shows that hoarding or taking more than needed is unlawful.
4
Note the limitations of the permission
The permission is only for immediate essential needs—consumption, fuel, anointment, and fighting. Hoarding, selling, or taking for permanent ownership is not allowed without distribution.
The prohibition of plundering (nuhbah) underscores the limit.
5
Distinguish permissibility from ownership
Hanafis draw a clear line: temporary use for necessity is lawful; permanent possession and trade require formal khums and division. This is a thin line—students must not conflate use with ownership.
The cross-madhhab difference: some Shafi'is require later accounting for any consumed item.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا بَأْسَ أَنْ يَعْلِفَ الْعَسْكَرُ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ وَيَأْكُلُوا مِمَّا وَجَدُوهُ مِنْ الطَّعَامِ وَيَسْتَعْمِلُوا الْحَطَبَ وَيَدْهُنُوا بِالدُّهْنِ وَيُقَاتِلُونَ بِمَا يَجِدُونَهُ مِنْ السِّلَاحِ كُلُّ ذَلِكَ بِغَيْرِ قِسْمَةٍ

وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ أَنْ يَعْلِفَ الْعَسْكَرُا عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: كُنَّا نُصِيبُ فِي مَغَازِينَا الْعَسَلَ وَالْعِنَبَ، فَنَأْكُلُهُ وَلَا نَرْفَعُهُ. (بخاري شريف، بَابُ مَا يُصِيبُ مِنَ الطَّعَامِ فِي أَرْضِ الْحَرْبِ، نمبر 3154/ مسلم شريف،باب جواز الأكل من طعام الغنيمة في دار الحرب،نمبر 1772/سنن ابوداود ، بَابٌ فِي وَطْءِ السَّبَايَا،نمبر 2701)

وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ أَنْ يَعْلِفَ الْعَسْكَرُا حَدَّثَنِي أَبُو عُبَيْدَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، قَالَ: مَرَرْتُ فَإِذَا أَبُو جَهْلٍ صَرِيعٌ قَدْ ضُرِبَتْ رِجْلُهُ فَقُلْتُ: «يَا عَدُوَّ اللَّهِ، يَا أَبَا جَهْلِ قَدْ أَخْرَى اللَّهُ الْآخِرَ». قَالَ: وَلَا أَهَابُهُ عِنْدَ ذَلِكَ فَقَالَ : أَبْعَدُ مِنْ رَجُلٍ قَتَلَهُ قَوْمُهُ، فَضَرَبْتُهُ بِسَيْفَ غَيْرِ طَائِلٍ، فَلَمْ يُغْنِ شَيْئًا حَتَّى سَقَطَ سَيْفُهُ مِنْ يَدِهِ، فَضَرَبْتُهُ بِهِ حَتَّى بَرَدَ. (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي الرُّخْصَةِ فِي السلاح يُقَاتَلُ بِهِ فِي الْمَعْرَكَةِ، غير 270)

وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأسَ أَنْ يَعْلِفَ الْعَسْكَرُا عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أَبِي أَوْفَ، قَالَ: قُلْتُ: هَلْ كُنْتُمْ تُخَمِسُونَ - يَعْنِي الطَّعَامَ - فِي عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ؟ فَقَالَ: «أَصَبْنَا طَعَامًا يَوْمَ خَيْبَرَ، فَكَانَ الرَّجُلُ يَجِيءُ فَيَأْخُذُ مِنْهُ مِقْدَارَ مَا يَكْفِيهِ، ثُمَّ يَنْصَرِفُ». (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي النَّهْيِ عَنِ النُّهْبَةِ إِذَا كَانَ فِي الطَّعَامِ قِلَّةٌ فِي أَرْضِ الْعَدُوِّ، نمبر 2704)

وجه : (۴) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ أَنْ يَعْلِفَ الْعَسْكَرُا عَنْ عَاصِمٍ يَعْنِي ابْنَ كُلَيْبٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ رَجُلٍ مِنَ الْأَنْصَارِ قَالَ: خَرَجْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي سَفَرٍ فَأَصَابَ النَّاسَ حَاجَةٌ شَدِيدَةٌ وَجَهْدٌ، وَأَصَابُوا غَنَمًا فَانْتَهَبُوهَا، فَإِنَّ قُدُورَنَا لَتَغْلِي إِذْ جَاءَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَمْشِي عَلَى قَوْسِهِ، فَأَكْفَأَ قُدُورَنَا بِقَوْسِهِ، ثُمَّ جَعَلَ يُرَمِّلُ اللَّحْمَ بِالتُّرَابِ ثُمَّ قَالَ: «إِنَّ النُّهْبَةَ لَيْسَتْ بِأَحَلَّ مِنَ الْمَيْتَةِ» أَوْ إِنَّ الْمَيْتَةَ لَيْسَتْ بِأَحَلَّ مِنَ النُّهْبَةِ» الشَّكُ مِنْ هَنَّادٍ. (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي النَّهْيِ عَنِ النُّهْبَةِ إِذَا كَانَ فِي الطَّعَامِ قِلَّةٌ في أَرْضِ الْعَدُوّ ، نمبر 2705/ بخاري شريف ، بَابُ قِسْمَةِ الغنم، غمبر 2488)
There is no harm for the army to feed (fodder) in Dar al-Harb, and to eat from what they find of food, and to use firewood, and to oil with oil, and to fight with what they find of weapons – all of that without distribution. Evidence 1: from Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) said: We would obtain honey and grapes in our expeditions, so we ate it and did not set it aside. (Bukhari ... Muslim ... Abu Dawud). Evidence 2: Abu Ubaidah narrated from his father: I passed by Abu Jahl who was struck on his leg... Evidence 3: from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa: I asked: Did you used to take khums of food in the time of the Messenger of Allah? He said: We obtained food on the day of Khaybar, so a man would come and take from it an amount sufficient for him, then leave. (Abu Dawud). Evidence 4: from Asim ibn Kulayb from his father from a man of the Ansar: We went out with the Messenger of Allah on a journey, and the people faced severe need and hardship. They got some sheep and plundered them. Our pots were boiling when the Messenger of Allah came walking on his bow, then he overturned our pots with his bow, then started to smear the meat with dust and said: 'Plunder is not more lawful than carrion' or 'Carrion is not more lawful than plunder' – the doubt is from Hannad. (Abu Dawud, Bukhari).
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling from the matn of Al-Quduri on the permissibility of using captured provisions in Dar al-Harb before formal division (qismah). The author lists four categories: fodder for animals, food for consumption, firewood for fuel, oil for anointment, and weapons for fighting. All this is allowed without waiting for distribution. The proofs are four hadith reports from the Prophet's practice. The first shows that the Companions consumed honey and grapes in expeditions without setting aside any portion. The second demonstrates the use of an enemy's sword during battle. The third indicates that at Khaybar, soldiers took only enough food for their immediate need, not for hoarding. The fourth is a cautionary hadith about plundering (nuhbah), comparing it to carrion, which is unlawful to consume. The Hanafi school interprets these ahadith to permit immediate use for necessity but not for ownership or sale before distribution. The ruling is a dispensation due to military necessity, as the army may not have time for formal division.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (Dār al-Ḥarb): Territory under non-Muslim control where hostilities may occur; the enemy's land where the army operates.
قسمة (Qismah): Formal distribution of war booty among the army as per Islamic law, requiring khums to be taken first.
غَنيمَة (Ghanīmah): Booty taken from the enemy during war; its rules are detailed in Kitab al-Siyar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, which of the following is allowed for the army in Dar al-Harb without distribution?
A) Selling captured food
B) Feeding captured fodder to their animals
C) Taking goods to own them permanently
D) Hoarding captured oil for later trade

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits immediate use of war booty for essential needs in enemy territory without formal distribution, based on Prophetic practice and the principle of military necessity.

Prohibition of Selling or Owning Booty Before Distribution
Ruling with three hadith proofs on booty disposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that selling or taking ownership of war booty before formal division is haram, identify the three hadith proofs from the text, and explain how they establish the prohibition.

Core Idea
Booty cannot be sold or owned before distribution; only immediate use is allowed.

This lesson examines a key ruling from the chapter of jihad: the prohibition of disposing of war booty before the imam divides it. The text from Al-Quduri states this plainly and supports it with three prophetic hadiths. Understanding this ruling is essential because it protects the collective rights of all soldiers and prevents ghulul (embezzlement).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the matn: 'ولا يجوز أن يبيعوا شيئا من ذلك ولا يتموّلونه'. Note that the verb 'لا يجوز' indicates absolute prohibition. The two prohibited actions are selling (بيع) and taking ownership (تمول).
The prohibition applies before formal division by the imam.
2
Analyze the First Hadith
The hadith from Abdullah ibn Amr: 'كلوا واعلفوا ولا تحملوا'. The key phrase is 'لا تحملوا' (do not carry away). This forbids taking more than immediate needs for later use or trade.
This hadith is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
3
Analyze the Second Hadith
The hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa: 'أصابنا طعاما يوم خيبر، فكان الرجل يجيء فيأخذ منه مقدار ما يكفيه، ثم ينصرف'. This shows that the Companions took only sufficient food for immediate consumption, not for hoarding or ownership.
It demonstrates the practice of isti'mal (use) not tamawwul.
4
Analyze the Third Hadith
The hadith from Umar: 'إذا وجدتم الرجل قد غل فأخفقوا متاعه واضربوه'. This establishes punishment for ghulul (embezzlement of booty before division).
This underscores the severity of taking booty before it is divided.
5
Synthesize the Evidence
Combine all three: the first explicitly prohibits carrying away; the second shows the permitted limit is immediate need; the third warns of punishment for exceeding that limit. Together they prove that tamawwul and sale are haram.
Use is allowed; ownership is not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَبِيعُوا شَيْئًا مِنْ ذَلِكَ وَلَا يَتَمَوَّلُونَهُ

وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَبِيعُوا شَيْئًا مِنْ ذَلِكَ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو رضي اللَّه عنهما، قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَوْمَ خَيْبَرَ : " كُلُوا وَاعْلِفُوا وَلَا تَحْمِلُوا" (سنن بيهقي، بَابُ مَا فَضَلَ فِي يَدِهِ مِنَ الطَّعَامِ وَالْعَلَفِ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ،نمبر 18004)

وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَبِيعُوا شَيْئًا مِنْ ذَلِكَ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أَبِي أَوْفَى، قَالَ: قُلْتُ: " هَلْ كُنْتُمْ تُخَمِسُونَ - يَعْنِي الطَّعَامَ - فِي عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ؟ فَقَالَ: «أَصَبْنَا طَعَامًا يَوْمَ خَيْبَرَ، فَكَانَ الرَّجُلُ يَجِيءُ فَيَأْخُذُ مِنْهُ مِقْدَارَ مَا يَكْفِيهِ، ثُمَّ يَنْصَرِفُ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي النَّهْيِ عَنِ النُّهْبَةِ إِذَا كَانَ فِي الطَّعَامِ قِلَّةٌ في أَرْضِ الْعَدُوّ ، نمبر 2704)

وجه:(۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَبِيعُوا شَيْئًا مِنْ ذَلِكَ عَنْ عُمَرَ بْنِ الْخَطَّابِ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إِذَا وَجَدْتُمُ الرَّجُلَ قَدْ غَلَّ فَأَخْرِقُوا مَتَاعَهُ وَاضْرِبُوهُ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي عُقُوبَةِ الْغَال، غير 2713)
And it is not permissible for them to sell any of that, nor to own it for themselves. Evidence 1: from Abdullah ibn Amr (may Allah be pleased with them both) that the Messenger of Allah said on the day of Khaybar: 'Eat, feed, and do not carry away.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). Evidence 2: from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa: I asked: 'Did you use to take khums of food in the time of the Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'We obtained food on the day of Khaybar, so a man would come and take from it an amount sufficient for him, then leave.' (Sunan Abi Dawud). Evidence 3: from Umar ibn al-Khattab from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: 'If you find a man who has stolen from the booty (ghalla), then spoil his goods and beat him.' (Sunan Abi Dawud).
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage states the second part of the ruling on war booty: it is not permissible to sell any of the captured items before formal distribution, nor to take ownership of them (tamawwul). The first hadith (from Abdullah ibn Amr) explicitly forbids carrying away (tahmil), which implies taking beyond immediate need for later sale or hoarding. The second hadith (from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa) shows that at Khaybar, soldiers took only what they needed, not for accumulation. The third hadith warns of the punishment for ghulul (embezzlement of booty before distribution). The Hanafi school uses these proofs to establish that while immediate use is allowed, any form of proprietary disposition (sale, gift, or permanent ownership) is prohibited until the booty is formally divided by the imam. This is because the property rights of all soldiers are pending. The ruling ensures fairness and prevents individuals from taking more than their share.

Key Terms
تَمَوُّل (Tamawwul): Taking possession of something as one's own property; owning it privately.
غُلُول (Ghulūl): Embezzlement or theft from the war booty before distribution; a major sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the hadith 'Kulu wa' lifu wa la tahmilu' (Eat, feed, and do not carry away) indicate regarding booty?
A) It is allowed to sell excess food
B) It is allowed to take food only for immediate consumption, not for storage or trade
C) It is allowed to hoard food for later use
D) It is allowed to take food to feed one's family permanently

Key Takeaway
Booty collected in war remains collective property until divided by the imam; selling or privately owning it before division is haram and constitutes ghulul.

Ruling on Property Becoming Fay' Upon Conquest
Ruling on fay' with multiple proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which types of enemy property become fay' upon conquest and cite the hadith evidence used by the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Upon conquest, only specific assets become fay': real estate, spouse, pregnancy, and adult children — not all property.

This passage addresses a key question in the law of war: what happens to the property of the enemy when Muslims gain mastery over their land? The Hanafi school teaches that certain categories become fay' (state property), and we will examine the textual evidence from the Prophet's Sunnah and the statements of the Salaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the items that become fay'
From the text, list the four categories: real estate ('aqar), wife, her pregnancy, and adult children.
Minor children follow their mother and are not separately listed.
2
Locate the primary hadith evidence
The first hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud (no. 3067) shows that upon embracing Islam, property is protected, implying it was unprotected before and thus subject to fay'.
The hadith is about a specific case but is used by analogy.
3
Examine the second hadith
The hadith from Bayhaqi (no. 18261) states that dhimmis retain their property upon conversion, confirming that non-Muslim combatants do not have such protection.
This reinforces the first hadith.
4
Understand the Tabi'i statement
Sufyan al-Thawri's statement about freeing a pregnant slave is cited as indirect support for the ruling on the pregnant wife becoming fay'.
This shows the continuity of reasoning from the Salaf.
5
Apply the underlying principle
The Urdu conclusion states that property taken from non-inviolable persons (like enemy combatants) is not returned, solidifying the fay' ruling.
This principle is used in later Hanafi texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ ظَهَرْنَا عَلَى الدَّارِ فَعَقَارُهُ فَيْءٌ وَزَوْجَتُهُ فَيْءٌ وَحَمْلُهَا فَيْءٌ وَأَوْلَادُهُ الْكِبَارُ فَيْءٌ، وَلَا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُبَاعَ السِّلَاحُ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْحَرْبِ.
الوجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ ظَهَرْنَا عَلَى الدَّارِ فَعَقَارُهُ فَيْءٌ: حَدَّثَنِي عُثْمَانُ بْنُ أَبِي حَازِمٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِهِ صَخْرٍ: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم غَنَّا ثَقِيفًا ... يَا صَخْرُ، إِنَّ الْقَوْمَ إِذَا أَسْلَمُوا أَحْرَزُوا أَمْوَالَهُمْ، وَدِمَاءَهُمْ، فَادْفَعْ إِلَى الْقَوْمِ مَاءَهُمْ، قَالَ: نَعَمْ يَا نَبِيَّ اللَّهِ، فَرَأَيْتُ وَجْهَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَتَغَيَّرُ عِنْدَ ذَلِكَ حُمْرَةً حَيَاءً مِنْ أَخْذِهِ الْجَارِيَةَ، وَأَخْذِهِ الْمَاءَ. (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي إِقْطَاع الْأَرَضِينَ، نمبر 3067)
الوجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ ظَهَرْنَا عَلَى الدَّارِ فَعَقَارُهُ فَيْءٌ: عَنْ سُلَيْمَانَ بْنِ بُرَيْدَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَقُولُ فِي أَهْلِ الذِمَّةِ: لَهُمْ مَا أَسْلَمُوا عَلَيْهِ مِنْ أَمْوَالِهِمْ وَعَبِيدِهِمْ وَدِيَارِهِمْ وَأَرْضِهِمْ وَمَاشِيَتِهِمْ، لَيْسَ عَلَيْهِمْ فِيهِ إِلَّا الصَّدَقَةُ. (سنن بيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ أَسْلَمَ عَلَى شَيْءٍ فَهُوَ لَهُ، غير 18261)
الوجه (۳) قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِنْ ظَهَرْنَا عَلَى الدَّارِ فَعَقَارُهُ فَيْءٌ: قَالَ سُفْيَانُ: وَنَحْنُ لَا تَأْخُذُ بِذَلِكَ تَقُولُ إِذَا اسْتَفْنَى مَا فِي بَطْنِهَا عَتَقَتْ كُلُّهَا إِنَّمَا وَلَدُهَا كَعُضْو مِنْهَا، وَإِذَا أَعْتَقَ مَا فِي بَطْنِهَا وَلَمْ يَعْتِقْهَا لَمْ يُعْتَقَ إِلَّا مَا فِي بَطْنِهَا. (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ الرَّجُلِ يُعْتِقُ أَمَتَهُ وَيَسْتَغْنِي مَا فِي بَطْنِهَا وَالرَّجُلُ يَشْتَرِي ابْنَهُ، نمبر 16800)
الوجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُبَاعَ السِّلَاحُ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْحَرْبِ: عَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْنِ حُصَيْنٍ، قَالَ: نَهَى رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ بَيْعِ السِّلَاحِ فِي الْفِتْنَةِ. (سنن بيهقي، بَابُ كَرَاهِيَةِ بَيْعِ الْعَصِيرِ مِمَّنْ يَعْصِرُ الْخَمْرَ، وَالسَّيْفِ مِمَّنْ يَعْصِي اللهَ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ بِهِ، نمبر 10780)
الوجه (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَلَا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُبَاعَ السِّلَاحُ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْحَرْبِ: عَنِ الْحَسَنِ قَالَ: لَا يُبْعَثُ إِلَى أَهْلِ الْحَرْبِ شَيْءٌ مِنَ السِّلَاحِ وَالْكَرَاعِ، وَلَا مَا يُسْتَعَانُ بِهِ عَلَى السِّلَاحِ وَالْكُرَاعِ. (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَا يُكْرَهُ أَنْ يُحْمَلَ إِلَى الْعَدُو فَيَتَقَوَّى بِهِ، غبر 33372)
اصول: اگر غیر معصوم مال پر قبضہ ہو جائے تو واپس نہیں کیا جائے گا، لہذا حربیوں کا مال واپس نہیں ہو گا۔
If we gain mastery over the land, then his real estate is fay', and his wife is fay', and her pregnancy is fay', and his adult children are fay', and it is not proper to sell weapons to the people of war. Evidence (1) hadith for establishing 'if we gain mastery over the land, then his real estate is fay'': ... Evidence (2) hadith ... Evidence (3) statement of a Tabi'i ... Evidence (1) hadith for establishing 'it is not proper to sell weapons to the people of war': ... Evidence (2) statement of a Tabi'i ... Principle: If possession is taken over non-inviolable property, it will not be returned; thus the property of the combatants will not be returned.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Kitab al-Siyar on the disposition of enemy property upon conquest. The matn states that when Muslims conquer a land, the real estate ('aqar) of the enemy becomes fay' (public treasury booty). Similarly, his wife, her pregnancy, and his adult children also become part of the fay'. This means they become the property of the Islamic state and are distributed as spoils. The phrase 'and his adult children are fay'' indicates that minor children follow their mother, but adult children are separately considered. The text then adds a prohibition: 'it is not proper to sell weapons to the people of war.' This is a ruling on the prohibition of providing war materials to the enemy. The remainder of the passage provides hadith and statements of the Salaf as evidence. The first hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud (on the incident of Thaqif) shows that property is protected upon Islam, implying that before Islam it is not protected. The second hadith from Bayhaqi explicitly states that dhimmis retain their property upon conversion. The statement of Sufyan al-Thawri discusses the ruling on freeing a pregnant slave. The two proofs for the prohibition of selling weapons are a hadith narrated by Imran ibn Husayn that the Prophet forbade selling weapons during fitnah, and the statement of Hasan al-Basri that nothing from weapons and horses should be sent to the enemy. The Urdu principle at the end summarizes that if possession is taken over non-inviolable property (like that of the enemy), it is not returned. In the Hanafi school, fay' is distributed according to the rules of ghanimah, but this text focuses on the initial acquisition.

Key Terms
فَيْء (fay'): Property taken from the enemy without active warfare, or booty that becomes the property of the Islamic state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT listed as becoming fay' upon conquest in this passage?
A) Real estate
B) Wife
C) Horse
D) Adult children

Key Takeaway
Only real estate, spouse, pregnancy, and adult children of the enemy become fay' upon conquest, not all property.

Prohibition of Selling Weapons to the Enemy
Prohibition ruling with hadith and Salaf evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling weapons to the people of war and identify the evidence from hadith and the practice of the Salaf.

Core Idea
Selling weapons to the enemy is prohibited (makruh tahrimi) because it strengthens them against Muslims.

This passage continues with a separate ruling: the prohibition of selling weapons to the people of war. The Hanafi school deems this as makruh tahrimi, close to haram, and provides hadith and statements of the Salaf as evidence. We will examine the proofs and the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The phrase 'لا ينبغي' indicates strong prohibition. In Hanafi usul, 'لا ينبغي' is used for makruh tahrimi.
This is less than haram but still sinful.
2
Examine the hadith evidence
The hadith from Imran ibn Husayn states that the Prophet forbade selling weapons during fitnah (civil strife). The wording is 'nahā' which indicates prohibition.
The hadith is general and applies to selling to enemies during war as well.
3
Examine the statement of Hasan al-Basri
Hasan al-Basri prohibits sending any weapons, horses, or items that help the enemy in war. This includes not just weapons but anything that strengthens them militarily.
This expands the prohibition beyond just weapons.
4
Understand the rationale
Selling weapons and war materials to the enemy directly harms Muslims by giving the enemy means to fight.
The prohibition is based on preventing harm (darar).
5
Apply the principle
This ruling applies to any item that can be used for war, not just weapons per se. It also covers selling to both combatants and non-combatants if the item will likely be used against Muslims.
The Hanafi position is absolute: no weapons to the people of war.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ ظَهَرْنَا عَلَى الدَّارِ فَعَقَارُهُ فَيْءٌ وَزَوْجَتُهُ فَيْءٌ وَحَمْلُهَا فَيْءٌ وَأَوْلَادُهُ الْكِبَارُ فَيْءٌ، وَلَا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُبَاعَ السِّلَاحُ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْحَرْبِ.
الوجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ ظَهَرْنَا عَلَى الدَّارِ فَعَقَارُهُ فَيْءٌ: حَدَّثَنِي عُثْمَانُ بْنُ أَبِي حَازِمٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِهِ صَخْرٍ: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم غَنَّا ثَقِيفًا ... يَا صَخْرُ، إِنَّ الْقَوْمَ إِذَا أَسْلَمُوا أَحْرَزُوا أَمْوَالَهُمْ، وَدِمَاءَهُمْ، فَادْفَعْ إِلَى الْقَوْمِ مَاءَهُمْ، قَالَ: نَعَمْ يَا نَبِيَّ اللَّهِ، فَرَأَيْتُ وَجْهَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَتَغَيَّرُ عِنْدَ ذَلِكَ حُمْرَةً حَيَاءً مِنْ أَخْذِهِ الْجَارِيَةَ، وَأَخْذِهِ الْمَاءَ. (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي إِقْطَاع الْأَرَضِينَ، نمبر 3067)
الوجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ ظَهَرْنَا عَلَى الدَّارِ فَعَقَارُهُ فَيْءٌ: عَنْ سُلَيْمَانَ بْنِ بُرَيْدَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَقُولُ فِي أَهْلِ الذِمَّةِ: لَهُمْ مَا أَسْلَمُوا عَلَيْهِ مِنْ أَمْوَالِهِمْ وَعَبِيدِهِمْ وَدِيَارِهِمْ وَأَرْضِهِمْ وَمَاشِيَتِهِمْ، لَيْسَ عَلَيْهِمْ فِيهِ إِلَّا الصَّدَقَةُ. (سنن بيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ أَسْلَمَ عَلَى شَيْءٍ فَهُوَ لَهُ، غير 18261)
الوجه (۳) قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِنْ ظَهَرْنَا عَلَى الدَّارِ فَعَقَارُهُ فَيْءٌ: قَالَ سُفْيَانُ: وَنَحْنُ لَا تَأْخُذُ بِذَلِكَ تَقُولُ إِذَا اسْتَفْنَى مَا فِي بَطْنِهَا عَتَقَتْ كُلُّهَا إِنَّمَا وَلَدُهَا كَعُضْو مِنْهَا، وَإِذَا أَعْتَقَ مَا فِي بَطْنِهَا وَلَمْ يَعْتِقْهَا لَمْ يُعْتَقَ إِلَّا مَا فِي بَطْنِهَا. (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ الرَّجُلِ يُعْتِقُ أَمَتَهُ وَيَسْتَغْنِي مَا فِي بَطْنِهَا وَالرَّجُلُ يَشْتَرِي ابْنَهُ، نمبر 16800)
الوجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُبَاعَ السِّلَاحُ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْحَرْبِ: عَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْنِ حُصَيْنٍ، قَالَ: نَهَى رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ بَيْعِ السِّلَاحِ فِي الْفِتْنَةِ. (سنن بيهقي، بَابُ كَرَاهِيَةِ بَيْعِ الْعَصِيرِ مِمَّنْ يَعْصِرُ الْخَمْرَ، وَالسَّيْفِ مِمَّنْ يَعْصِي اللهَ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ بِهِ، نمبر 10780)
الوجه (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَلَا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُبَاعَ السِّلَاحُ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْحَرْبِ: عَنِ الْحَسَنِ قَالَ: لَا يُبْعَثُ إِلَى أَهْلِ الْحَرْبِ شَيْءٌ مِنَ السِّلَاحِ وَالْكَرَاعِ، وَلَا مَا يُسْتَعَانُ بِهِ عَلَى السِّلَاحِ وَالْكُرَاعِ. Ransoming Prisoners: Abu Hanifa vs. the Two Companions
Presents the intra-Hanafi dispute on ransoming enemy prisoners

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on ransoming enemy prisoners for Muslim prisoners, and explain the scriptural evidence each side uses.

Core Idea
Intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa prohibits prisoner exchange; the Sahibayn permit it, and later fatwa follows their view.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding the treatment of prisoners of war. While Imam Abu Hanifa held that enemy captives cannot be ransomed to free Muslim prisoners, his two chief disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, permitted it. The debate hinges on interpreting different Quranic verses and hadith. Understanding this dispute not only clarifies an important jihad ruling but also demonstrates the Hanafi method of tarjih (weighing evidences).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Begin by identifying the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa: that enemy prisoners are not to be ransomed for Muslim prisoners.
2
Identify the opposing view
Recognize that the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) held that it is permissible to ransom them for Muslim prisoners.
Also the Shafi'i school agrees with the Sahibayn.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the evidence cited by the Sahibayn: Quran 47:4 (explicit permission of ransom after taking captives), the hadith where the Prophet ransomed two Muslims with one polytheist, and the Fazarah incident.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response
Understand how Abu Hanifa counters these proofs: he interprets the verse in Surah Muhammad as abrogated or specific to the early battles, and views the hadith as weak or insufficient to override the general command of severity.
Abu Hanifa relies on Quran 8:67, 2:191, 4:89.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical consequence: if Muslim prisoners are held, Abu Hanifa's ruling forbids exchange; the Sahibayn allow it. Later Hanafi fatwa (mufta bihi) adopts the view of the Sahibayn due to stronger evidence and practical necessity.
Tarjih authority: Later Hanafi jurists like Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah favored the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُفَادَوْنَ بِالْأَسَارَى عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ، وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ: لَا بَأْسَ أَنْ يُفَادَى بِهِمْ أَسَارَى الْمُسْلِمِينَ.
الوجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ ظَهَرْنَا عَلَى الدَّارِ فَعَقَارُهُ فَيْءٌ: أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ أَبَا هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: ... وَلَا وَاللَّهِ، لَا يَأْتِيكُمْ مِنَ الْيَمَامَةِ حَبَّةُ حِنْطَةٍ حَتَّى يَأْذَنَ فِيهَا النَّبِيُّ. (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ وَفْدِ بَنِي حَنِيفَةَ وَحَدِيثِ تُمَامَةَ بْنٍ، نمبر 4372)
الوجه (۱) الآية لثبوت وَلَا يُفَادَوْنَ بِالْأَسَارَى: ﴿مَا كَانَ لِنَبِيٍّ أَنْ يَكُونَ لَهُ أَسْرَى حَتَّى يُثْخِنَ فِي الْأَرْضِ﴾ [الأنفال: 67] تُرِيدُونَ عَرَضَ الدُّنْيَا وَاللَّهُ يُرِيدُ الْآخِرَةَ وَاللَّهُ عَزِيزٌ حَكِيمٌ.
الوجه (۲) الآية لثبوت وَلَا يُفَادَوْنَ بِالْأَسَارَى: ﴿وَاقْتُلُوهُمْ حَيْثُ ثَقِفْتُمُوهُمْ وَأَخْرِجُوهُمْ مِنْ حَيْثُ أَخْرَجُوكُمْ وَالْفِتْنَةُ أَشَدُّ مِنَ الْقَتْلِ﴾ [البقرة: 191].
الوجه (۳) الآية لثبوت وَلَا يُفَادَوْنَ بِالْأَسَارَى: ﴿فَإِنْ تَوَلَّوْا فَخُذُوهُمْ وَاقْتُلُوهُمْ حَيْثُ وَجَدْتُمُوهُمْ وَلَا تَتَّخِذُوا مِنْهُمْ وَلِيًّا وَلَا نَصِيرًا﴾ [النساء: 89].
الوجه (۱) دليل الصاحبين والشافعى لثبوت أَنَّهُ يُفَادَى بِالْأَسَارَى: ﴿فَإِذَا لَقِيتُمُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا فَضَرْبَ الرِّقَابِ حَتَّى إِذَا أَثْخَنْتُمُوهُمْ فَشُدُّوا الْوَثَاقَ فَإِمَّا مَنًّا بَعْدُ وَإِمَّا فِدَاءً حَتَّى تَضَعَ الْحَرْبُ أَوْزَارَهَا﴾ [محمد: 4].
الوجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت أَنَّهُ يُفَادَى بِالْأَسَارَى: عَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْنِ حُصَيْنٍ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَدَى رَجُلَيْنِ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ بِرَجُلٍ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ. (الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي قَتْلِ الْأُسَارَى وَالفِدَاءِ، 1568)
الوجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت أَنَّهُ يُفَادَى بِالْأَسَارَى: حَدَّثَنِي إِيَاسُ بْنُ سَلَمَةَ، حَدَّثَنِي أَبِي قَالَ: غَزَوْنَا فَزَارَةَ وَعَلَيْنَا أَبُو بَكْرٍ ... فَبَعَثَ بِهَا رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم إِلَى أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ، فَفَدَى بِهَا نَاسًا مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ كَانُوا أُسِرُوا بِمَكَّةَ. (مسلم، بَاب التَّنْفِيلِ وَفِدَاءِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ بِالْأَسَارَى، نمبر 1755)
اصول: جو جنگ کا مجاز نہیں وہ امان دینے کا مجاز نہیں ہو گا، لہذا اگر آقا نے غلام کو اجازتِ جنگ دی ہے اور اس غلام نے کسی حربی کو امان دیا تو اس کا لحاظ کیا جائے گا امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک۔
And they (enemy prisoners) are not to be ransomed according to Abu Hanifa. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: There is no harm in ransoming them for Muslim prisoners. Evidence (3) hadith for establishing 'if we gain mastery...' ... Evidence (1) verse for establishing 'they are not ransomed': ... Evidence (2) verse ... Evidence (3) verse ... Evidence (1) proof of the two companions and al-Shafi'i for establishing that they are ransomed: ... Evidence (2) hadith ... Evidence (3) hadith ... Principle: Whoever is not authorized for combat is not authorized to grant amnesty; so if a master gave his slave permission to fight and that slave granted amnesty to a combatant, it will be considered according to Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement on the issue of ransoming enemy prisoners of war. According to Abu Hanifa, it is not permissible to ransom (exchange) captured enemy soldiers with Muslim prisoners. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) held that it is permissible to ransom them for Muslim captives. The text then provides scriptural evidence for both positions. For Abu Hanifa's view, three Quranic verses are cited: Surah al-Anfal 8:67 (which rebukes taking prisoners before thorough fighting), Surah al-Baqarah 2:191 (command to kill them wherever found), and Surah al-Nisa' 4:89 (take them and kill them, do not take them as allies). These verses emphasize severity. For the Sahibayn and al-Shafi'i, the main proof is Surah Muhammad 47:4 which explicitly mentions the option of ransom (fida') after securing the prisoners. Additionally, they cite a hadith from Tirmidhi where the Prophet Himself ransomed two Muslims with one polytheist, and a hadith from Muslim about the incident of Fazarah where the Prophet used ransom to free Muslims. The Urdu principle at the end is a separate usul ruling: that a slave authorized to fight can grant amnesty, and it will be recognized according to Abu Hanifa. In terms of the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, later jurists gave tarjih to the view of the Sahibayn, making ransom permissible as a pragmatic measure.

Key Terms
أَسَارَى (asara): Prisoners of war, captives taken from the enemy.
فِدَاء (fida'): Ransom, exchanging prisoners for money or other prisoners.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on prisoner exchange; the mufta bihi permits it, following the Sahibayn's view.

Slave's Authority to Grant Amnesty in Jihad
Presents a Hanafi ruling on a slave's authority to grant amnesty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that a slave authorized to fight can grant amnesty, and explain the reasoning behind Abu Hanifa's position.

Core Idea
Authorization for war implies authorization for amnesty — a logical extension by Abu Hanifa.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling within the Hanafi law of jihad: whether a slave who has been permitted by his master to participate in combat has the authority to grant amnesty (aman) to enemy combatants. Imam Abu Hanifa held that he does, because the capacity to grant amnesty is inherent in the capacity to wage war. This ruling illustrates the Hanafi method of istihsan (juridical preference) and logical extension.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Recognize that Abu Hanifa rules: a slave with permission to fight can validly grant amnesty.
2
State the condition
The slave must have been explicitly authorized by his master to participate in combat.
3
Explain the principle
The principle: 'Whoever is not authorized for combat is not authorized for amnesty' implies that authorization for combat includes authorization for amnesty by logical extension.
This is an application of qiyas (analogy) and istihsan.
4
Note the evidence
No direct scriptural proof is cited; the ruling is derived from the general principle of delegation and the nature of war authority.
5
Contrast with other views
Some schools may require explicit permission for amnesty; Abu Hanifa's view is based on a broader interpretation of delegated authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُفَادَوْنَ بِالْأَسَارَى عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ، وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ: لَا بَأْسَ أَنْ يُفَادَى بِهِمْ أَسَارَى الْمُسْلِمِينَ.
الوجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ ظَهَرْنَا عَلَى الدَّارِ فَعَقَارُهُ فَيْءٌ: أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ أَبَا هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: ... وَلَا وَاللَّهِ، لَا يَأْتِيكُمْ مِنَ الْيَمَامَةِ حَبَّةُ حِنْطَةٍ حَتَّى يَأْذَنَ فِيهَا النَّبِيُّ. (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ وَفْدِ بَنِي حَنِيفَةَ وَحَدِيثِ تُمَامَةَ بْنٍ، نمبر 4372)
الوجه (۱) الآية لثبوت وَلَا يُفَادَوْنَ بِالْأَسَارَى: ﴿مَا كَانَ لِنَبِيٍّ أَنْ يَكُونَ لَهُ أَسْرَى حَتَّى يُثْخِنَ فِي الْأَرْضِ﴾ [الأنفال: 67] تُرِيدُونَ عَرَضَ الدُّنْيَا وَاللَّهُ يُرِيدُ الْآخِرَةَ وَاللَّهُ عَزِيزٌ حَكِيمٌ.
الوجه (۲) الآية لثبوت وَلَا يُفَادَوْنَ بِالْأَسَارَى: ﴿وَاقْتُلُوهُمْ حَيْثُ ثَقِفْتُمُوهُمْ وَأَخْرِجُوهُمْ مِنْ حَيْثُ أَخْرَجُوكُمْ وَالْفِتْنَةُ أَشَدُّ مِنَ الْقَتْلِ﴾ [البقرة: 191].
الوجه (۳) الآية لثبوت وَلَا يُفَادَوْنَ بِالْأَسَارَى: ﴿فَإِنْ تَوَلَّوْا فَخُذُوهُمْ وَاقْتُلُوهُمْ حَيْثُ وَجَدْتُمُوهُمْ وَلَا تَتَّخِذُوا مِنْهُمْ وَلِيًّا وَلَا نَصِيرًا﴾ [النساء: 89].
الوجه (۱) دليل الصاحبين والشافعى لثبوت أَنَّهُ يُفَادَى بِالْأَسَارَى: ﴿فَإِذَا لَقِيتُمُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا فَضَرْبَ الرِّقَابِ حَتَّى إِذَا أَثْخَنْتُمُوهُمْ فَشُدُّوا الْوَثَاقَ فَإِمَّا مَنًّا بَعْدُ وَإِمَّا فِدَاءً حَتَّى تَضَعَ الْحَرْبُ أَوْزَارَهَا﴾ [محمد: 4].
الوجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت أَنَّهُ يُفَادَى بِالْأَسَارَى: عَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْنِ حُصَيْنٍ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَدَى رَجُلَيْنِ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ بِرَجُلٍ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ. (الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي قَتْلِ الْأُسَارَى وَالفِدَاءِ، 1568)
الوجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت أَنَّهُ يُفَادَى بِالْأَسَارَى: حَدَّثَنِي إِيَاسُ بْنُ سَلَمَةَ، حَدَّثَنِي أَبِي قَالَ: غَزَوْنَا فَزَارَةَ وَعَلَيْنَا أَبُو بَكْرٍ ... فَبَعَثَ بِهَا رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم إِلَى أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ، فَفَدَى بِهَا نَاسًا مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ كَانُوا أُسِرُوا بِمَكَّةَ. اصول: جو جنگ کا مجاز نہیں وہ امان دینے کا مجاز نہیں ہو گا، لہذا اگر آقا نے غلام کو اجازتِ جنگ دی ہے اور اس غلام نے کسی حربی کو امان دیا تو اس کا لحاظ کیا جائے گا امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک۔

Additionally, they cite a hadith from Tirmidhi where the Prophet Himself ransomed two Muslims with one polytheist, and a hadith from Muslim about the incident of Fazarah where the Prophet used ransom to free Muslims. The Urdu principle at the end is a separate usul ruling: that a slave authorized to fight can grant amnesty, and it will be recognized according to Abu Hanifa.
