Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ransoming Prisoners
Intra-Hanafi dispute over prisoner exchange with Quranic and hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on ransoming prisoners, cite the proofs for each view, and explain the practical consequence of the ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa forbids exchanging polytheist prisoners for Muslim captives; the Sahibayn permit it based on explicit Quranic and prophetic evidence.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement on a critical issue of warfare: may captured polytheist prisoners be exchanged to free Muslim captives? Abu Hanifa holds it is not permissible, while his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, allow it. We will examine the proofs each side marshals, understand the reasoning behind Abu Hanifa's prohibition, and see how the dispute is resolved in later fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disputed Issue
Determine exactly what is being debated: whether it is permissible to ransom (fida') captured polytheist prisoners (asara) in exchange for Muslim prisoners. This is not about monetary ransom or unconditional release (mann), which are separate rulings.
The term 'fida' here means exchange of prisoners, not payment.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position and His Proofs
Abu Hanifa says 'la yufadawun' – they are not to be ransomed. His three Quranic proofs: (1) al-Anfal 67 rebukes seeking worldly gain by taking captives before subduing the enemy; (2) al-Baqarah 191 commands killing polytheists wherever found; (3) al-Nisa 89 commands killing them and taking no allies. These indicate that the default is execution, not exchange.
These verses emphasize severity; Abu Hanifa views them as primary.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position and Their Proofs
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say 'la ba'sa' – there is no harm. Their proofs: (1) Surah Muhammad 4 explicitly allows either showing favor (mann) or ransom (fida') after securing captives; (2) hadith of Imran ibn Husayn that the Prophet ransomed two Muslims for one polytheist; (3) hadith of Salamah ibn al-Akwa' that Abu Bakr ransomed Muslims captured in Makkah.
The Sahibayn and al-Shafi'i agree on this permissibility.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The text hints at Abu Hanifa's response: Surah Muhammad 4 is general about polytheists, not specifically about exchange; the hadiths may be abrogated or limited to specific circumstances. The underlying principle is that exchange strengthens the enemy and weakens the Muslims' deterrent power.
This response reflects a different prioritization of textual evidence.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf and Tarjih
The practical consequence: if a Muslim is captured, Abu Hanifa forbids releasing a polytheist captive to free him; the Sahibayn permit it. Later Hanafi fatwa often favors the Sahibayn due to the explicit permission in Surah Muhammad and Prophetic practice, making the mufta bihi the permissibility view.
The tarjih is based on strength of evidence and later scholarly consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ السّير
وَلَا يُفَادَوْنَ بِالْأَسَارَى عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لَا بَأْسَ أَنْ يُفَادَى بِهِمْ أَسَارَى الْمُسْلِمِينَ
وجه : (1) الآية لثبوت وَلَا يُفَادَوْنَ بِالْأَسَارَى مَا كَانَ لِنَبِي أَن يَكُونَ لَهُ أَسْرَى حَتَّى يُنْخِنَ فِي الْأَرْضِ تُرِيدُونَ عَرَضَ الدُّنْيَا وَاللَّهُ يُرِيدُ الْآخِرَةُ وَاللَّهُ عَزِيزٌ حَكِيمٌ (سورة الأنفال، 8 آيت نمبر 67)
وجه:(۲) الآية لثبوت وَلَا يُفَادَوْنَ بِالْأَسَارَى ﴿وَاقْتُلُوهُمْ حَيْثُ ثَقِفْتُمُوهُمْ وَأَخْرِجُوهُم مِنْ حَيْثُ أَخْرَجُوكُمْ وَالْفِتْنَةُ أَشَدُّ مِنَ الْقَتْلِ﴾ (سورة البقرة، 2 آيت نمبر 191)
وجه:(۳) الآية لثبوت وَلَا يُفَادَوْنَ بِالْأَسَارَى ﴿فَإِن تَوَلَّوْا فَخُذُوهُمْ وَأَقْتُلُوهُمْ حَيْثُ وَجَدتُّمُوهُمْ وَلَا تَتَّخِذُواْ مِنْهُمْ وَلِيًّا وَلَا نَصِيرًا﴾ (سورة النساء، 4 أيت، نمبر 89)
وجه (۱) دليل الصاحبين والشافعى الآية لثبوت وَلَا يُفَادَوْنَ بِالْأَسَارَى ﴿فَإِذَا لَقِيتُمُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا فَضَرْبَ الرِّقَابِ حَتَّى إِذَا أَثْخَنتُمُوهُمْ فَشُدُّوا الْوَثَاقَ فَإِمَّا مَنَّا بَعْدُ وَإِمَّا فِدَاءً حَتَّى تَضَعَ الْحَرْبُ أَوْزَارَهَا﴾ (سورة محمد، 47 آيت نمبر 4)
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُفَادَوْنَ بِالْأَسَارَى عَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْن حُصَيْنِ، «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَدَى رَجُلَيْنِ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ بِرَجُلٍ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ» (الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي قَتْلِ الْأُسَارَى وَالفِدَاءِ، 1568)
وجه:(۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُفَادَوْنَ بِالْأَسَارَى حَدَّثَنِي إِيَاسُ بْنُ سَلَمَةَ. حَدَّثَنِي أَبِي قَالَ: غَزَوْنَا فَزَارَةَ وَعَلَيْنَا أَبُو بَكْرٍ ..... فَبَعَثَ بِمَا رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم إِلَى أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ. فَفَدَى بِمَا نَاسًا مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ، كَانُوا أُسِرُوا بِمَكَّةَ (مسلم شريف، بَابُ التَّنْفِيلِ وَفِدَاءِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ بِالْأَسَارَى، غمر 1755)
The Book of Siyar. And they are not to be ransomed for prisoners according to Abu Hanifa, and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: There is no harm that Muslim prisoners be ransomed with them. Evidence (1): The verse for establishing that they are not to be ransomed for prisoners: 'It is not for a prophet to have captives until he has made slaughter in the land. You desire the goods of the world, and Allah desires the Hereafter, and Allah is Mighty, Wise.' (Surah al-Anfal, verse 67). Evidence (2): The verse for establishing that they are not to be ransomed for prisoners: 'And kill them wherever you find them and drive them out from wherever they drove you out, and fitnah is more severe than killing.' (Surah al-Baqarah, verse 191). Evidence (3): The verse for establishing that they are not to be ransomed for prisoners: 'But if they turn away, then seize them and kill them wherever you find them, and take not from among them any ally or helper.' (Surah al-Nisa, verse 89). Evidence (1): The proof of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and al-Shafi'i: the verse for establishing that they are not to be ransomed for prisoners: 'So when you meet those who disbelieve, strike their necks until, when you have inflicted slaughter upon them, then secure their bonds, then either show favor afterwards or ransom them until the war lays down its burdens.' (Surah Muhammad, verse 4). Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing that they are not to be ransomed for prisoners: from Imran ibn Husayn that the Prophet (peace be upon him) ransomed two Muslim men with one polytheist man. (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on killing prisoners and ransom, 1568). Evidence (3): The hadith for establishing that they are not to be ransomed for prisoners: narrated to me by Iyas ibn Salamah, narrated to me by my father: We raided Fazarah with Abu Bakr over us... and he sent them with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) to the people of Makkah, and he ransomed with them some Muslim men who had been captured in Makkah. (Sahih Muslim, chapter on spoils and ransoming Muslims with prisoners, 1755).
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether captured polytheist prisoners of war (asara) may be exchanged (fida') for captured Muslim prisoners. Abu Hanifa holds that it is not permissible (la yufadawun), meaning Muslim prisoners should not be ransomed by releasing polytheist prisoners in exchange. His proofs include three Quranic verses: firstly, al-Anfal 67, which rebukes the desire for worldly goods over the afterlife; secondly, al-Baqarah 191, which commands killing polytheists wherever found; thirdly, al-Nisa 89, which commands killing them without taking allies. These verses indicate the default is killing, not ransom. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and al-Shafi'i permit it, citing Surah Muhammad 4, which explicitly permits either showing favor (mann) or ransom (fida') after securing prisoners. They also rely on two authentic hadiths: the Prophet ransomed two Muslims with one polytheist, and Abu Bakr ransomed Muslims captured in Makkah. This is a well-known ikhtilaf in Hanafi fiqh; the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) varies by era and context, though many later Hanafi authorities lean towards the Sahibayn's view due to the explicit Quranic permission and prophetic practice.

Key Terms
أسارى (asārā): Prisoners of war, specifically polytheists captured in battle.
فداء (fidā’): Ransom or exchange of prisoners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the primary Quranic evidence cited by the Sahibayn to permit ransoming prisoners?
A) al-Anfal 67
B) al-Baqarah 191
C) Surah Muhammad 4
D) al-Nisa 89

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains a legitimate ikhtilaf on exchanging prisoners; the later relied-upon position follows the Sahibayn's permissibility due to explicit Quranic and hadith evidence.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
6 min
Only War-Authorized Persons May Grant Aman
States the principle that only those authorized for war may grant aman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that aman is valid only from those authorized for war, and identify the exception for a slave with master's permission.

Core Idea
Aman requires war authority; a slave can grant it only if his master permits him to fight.

This lesson establishes a key principle in the law of jihad: the capacity to grant safe conduct (aman) belongs only to those who are legally capable of waging war. We explore the rule and its application to slaves, noting a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the principle
Identify the core legal rule: only a person authorized for war can grant aman. Understand the rationale – aman is a serious commitment that affects the Muslim community's security, so only those with authority to engage the enemy can extend it.
This principle prevents unauthorized individuals from making binding promises to the enemy.
2
Identify the condition for the slave’s aman
The exception: a slave, who normally lacks war authority, may grant valid aman if his master specifically authorizes him to fight. This transforms the slave into a representative of the master’s authority.
The slave acts as an agent; the master's permission is the key.
3
Note the Hanafi ikhtilaf
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, such aman is valid. However, the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) are reported to hold that even with permission, a slave’s aman is not valid because a slave lacks full legal capacity. This is a legitimate difference within the school.
The practical consequence: if the Sahibayn's view is followed, the aman would be void and the enemy could be attacked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول: جو جنگ کا مجاز نہیں وہ امان دینے کا مجاز نہیں ہو گا، لہذا اگر آقا نے غلام کو اجازتِ جنگ دی ہے اور اس غلام نے کسی حربی کو امان دیا تو اس کا لحاظ کیا جائے گا امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک۔
Principle: Whoever is not authorized for war is not authorized to grant aman. Therefore, if a master has given permission to his slave to fight, and that slave grants aman to a harbi (enemy), then it will be considered (valid) according to Imam Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This is a usul (principle) passage clarifying the capacity to grant aman (safe conduct) to enemy combatants. The principle states that only those who are legally capable of participating in jihad (i.e., free, adult, Muslim males) can grant aman. A slave, even if permitted to fight by his master, is not originally authorized for war on his own; thus, his grant of aman is not automatically valid. According to Abu Hanifa, however, if the master specifically authorized the slave for battle, then the slave's aman is considered valid and must be honored. This is because the slave acts as a representative of the master. The Sahibayn may have different views. This principle ensures that aman is only granted by those with authority, preventing chaos in military engagements.

Key Terms
امان (amān): Safe conduct or guarantee of security given to an enemy combatant, allowing them temporary protection.
حربی (ḥarbī): An enemy combatant from a non-Muslim territory with whom Muslims are at war.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle stated, can a slave who is given permission by his master to fight grant aman to an enemy?
A) No, never
B) Yes, it is considered valid
C) Only with the Imam's approval
D) It depends on the slave's religion

Key Takeaway
Aman is valid only from those authorized for war; a slave authorized by his master is an exception according to Imam Abu Hanifa.

The Prohibition of Free Release of Prisoners (Mann)
Declares impermissibility of free release of prisoners with evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on free release of prisoners (mann) and explain the Quranic and hadith evidence that supports this ruling.

Core Idea
Freeing captured enemy prisoners without ransom is prohibited in the Hanafi school.

When Muslim forces capture enemy combatants, the commander faces a serious decision. The Hanafi school holds that unconditional release (al-mann) is not permissible; the only options are ransom (fida) or execution (for combatants). This ruling is derived from the Quran and Sunnah, though some hadith appear to contradict it. In this lesson, we will examine the evidence and understand why the Hanafi position is that mann is haram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the ruling (hukm) is. Here, the act is al-mann — freeing a prisoner without any compensation. The ruling is that it is not permissible (la yajuz), meaning it is prohibited (haram).
Compare with terms like fida (ransom) and qatl (execution).
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the main evidence cited. The Quranic verse Surah Muhammad 47:4 is presented as proof. It mentions both mann and fida, but with a condition: 'until the war lays down its burdens.'
Write the verse: فَإِمَّا مَنَّا بَعْدُ وَإِمَّا فِدَاءً حَتَّى تَضَعَ الْحَرْبُ أَوْزَارَهَا
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the verse proves the ruling. The Hanafi interpretation is that the phrase 'hatta tada'a al-harb awzaraha' restricts the options of mann and fida to the post-war period. During active warfare, neither is permitted; only killing or capture (and detention) apply. Thus, mann during war is not allowed.
The Shafi'i school reads the verse differently, allowing mann even during war.
4
Address the apparent hadith evidence
Two hadiths are cited: the Prophet freed eighty captives from Makkah, and he said he would release the Badr prisoners for Mut'im. These seem to permit mann. The Hanafi response is that these were specific exceptions due to unique circumstances (e.g., the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah, or showing gratitude). They do not override the general Quranic rule.
General rules are not abrogated by specific, context-bound incidents.
5
Note the inter-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i and Hanbali schools allow mann if the Imam deems it beneficial, based on the same verse and hadith. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa) due to the strength of their interpretation and the need for military deterrence.
Both positions are respected; the difference stems from interpretive principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲۴. وَلَا يَجُوزُ الْمَنُّ عَلَيْهِمْ
وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ الْمَنُّ عَلَيْهِمْ ﴿فَإِمَّا مَنَّا بَعْدُ وَإِمَّا فِدَاءً حَتَّى تَضَعَ الْحَرْبُ أَوْزَارَهَا﴾ (سورة محمد، 47 آيت نمبر 4)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ الْمَنُّ عَلَيْهِمْ عَنْ أَنَسٍ، أَنَّ ثَمَانِينَ رَجُلًا مِنْ أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ هَبَطُوا عَلَى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَأَصْحَابِهِ مِنْ جِبَالِ التَّنْعِيمِ عِنْدَ صَلَاةِ الْفَجْرِ لِيَقْتُلُوهُمْ، فَأَخَذَهُمْ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم سِلْمًا، فَأَعْتَقَهُمْ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَأَنْزَلَ اللهُ عز وجل {وَهُوَ الَّذِي كَفَّ أَيْدِيَهُمْ عَنْكُمْ وَأَيْدِيَكُمْ عَنْهُمْ بِبَطْنِ مَكَّةَ} [الفتح: 24] (ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ فِي الْمَنِّ عَلَى الْأَسِيرِ بِغَيْرِ فِدَاءٍ، 2688)
وجه:(۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ الْمَنُّ عَلَيْهِمْ عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ، عَنْ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ جُبَيْرِ بْنِ مُطْعِمٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ لِأُسَارَى بَدْرٍ: «لَوْ كَانَ مُطْعِمُ بْنُ عَدِيٍّ حَيًّا، ثُمَّ كَلَّمَنِي فِي هَؤُلَاءِ النَّتْنَى لَأَطْلَقْتُهُمْ لَهُ»، (ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ فِي الْمَنِّ عَلَى الْأَسِيرِ بِغَيْرِ فِدَاءٍ، 2689)
24. And it is not permissible to show favor (free release) to them. Evidence (1): The verse for establishing that it is not permissible to show favor to them: 'Then either show favor afterwards or ransom until the war lays down its burdens.' (Surah Muhammad, verse 4). Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing that it is not permissible to show favor to them: from Anas, that eighty men from Makkah descended upon the Prophet and his companions from the mountains of Tan'im at the time of Fajr prayer to kill them, so the Messenger of Allah captured them unharmed, and the Messenger of Allah freed them, and then Allah revealed: 'And it is He who withheld their hands from you and your hands from them within Makkah.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on showing favor to a prisoner without ransom, 2688). Evidence (3): The hadith for establishing that it is not permissible to show favor to them: from al-Zuhri, from Muhammad ibn Jubayr ibn Mut'im, from his father, that the Prophet said to the prisoners of Badr: 'If Mut'im ibn 'Adi were alive and spoke to me about these filthy ones, I would release them for him.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on showing favor to a prisoner without ransom, 2689).
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This ruling states that after capturing enemy combatants, it is not permissible to simply free them without any compensation (mann). The proof is Surah Muhammad 4, which gives the leader the choice between freeing (mann) and ransom (fida) but only after the war has ended; before that, neither is generally allowed. The hadiths cited appear to contradict this: the Prophet freed eighty captives from Makkah, and he said he would free the Badr prisoners for Mut'im. However, these were specific exceptions due to circumstances (the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah context for the first, and a desire to show gratitude for a past favor for the second). The general rule is that prisoners should not be released freely; they must be ransomed or exchanged. This aligns with maintaining military strength and deterrence.

Key Terms
المن (al-mann): Freeing a prisoner without any compensation or exchange.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on freeing captured enemy prisoners without ransom (mann)?
A) Permissible
B) Recommended
C) Not permissible
D) Obligatory

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, free release of prisoners (mann) is not permissible; the options are ransom or execution, based on Quran 47:4 and the Sunnah.

Imam's Option in Conquered Lands: Division or Jizya
States the Imam's choice regarding conquered land with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options available to the Imam for land conquered by force and identify the Quranic and Prophetic proofs for this ruling.

Core Idea
When land is conquered by force, the Imam may divide it among fighters or leave it with inhabitants and impose jizyah and kharaj.

This lesson from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar explains a key ruling in the fiqh of jihad: the Imam's discretionary authority over conquered land. The text presents two options based on the Prophet's practice at Khaybar and the Quranic principle from Surah al-Hashr. Understanding this ruling clarifies the Hanafi position on the disposition of fay' and spoils of war.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is conquering a town by force ('anwah). The ruling gives the Imam a choice: either divide the land among the Muslim fighters or leave the inhabitants in place and impose jizyah on them and kharaj on their lands.
The option is not obligatory; it is a discretionary authority.
2
Locate the first dalil — Quranic verse
Surah al-Hashr 59:7 is cited. It states that what Allah restores to the Messenger from the towns is for Allah, the Messenger, relatives, orphans, needy, and wayfarer, and that it should not circulate among the rich. This indicates that the leader has discretion in distribution.
The verse is about fay' (wealth taken without direct fighting), which includes conquered land.
3
Locate the second dalil — Hadith of Khaybar
The hadith from Ibn Umar recounts the Prophet's conquest of Khaybar. The Prophet made a treaty with the inhabitants allowing them to remain on their land in exchange for a share of produce, but when they violated the treaty, he punished them. This establishes the precedent of leaving land with inhabitants under jizyah.
The hadith shows both the option to impose taxes and the consequences of breach.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Quranic verse implies that the leader decides how to distribute fay', not that it must be divided equally. The hadith demonstrates the practical application of this discretion. Together, they prove the Imam's choice.
The evidence is zanni al-dalala but sufficient for establishing the ruling.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
The Hanafi school grants full discretion. Some other schools, like the Shafi'i, hold that conquered land becomes fay' for the public treasury and cannot be divided among fighters, but the text does not elaborate on this dispute.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that both options are valid, but retention with taxes is often considered more beneficial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲۵. وَإِذَا فَتَحَ الْإِمَامُ بَلَدًا عَنْوَةً فَهُوَ بِالْخِيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ قَسَّمَهَا بَيْنَ الْعَالِمِينَ وَإِنْ شَاءَ أَقَرَّ أَهْلَهَا عَلَيْهَا وَوَضَعَ عَلَيْهِمُ الْجُزْيَةَ وَعَلَى أَرَاضِيهِمُ الْخَرَاجَ
وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَإِذَا فَتَحَ الْإِمَامُ بَلَدًا عَنْوَةً ﴿مَّا أَفَاءَ اللَّهُ عَلَى رَسُولِهِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْقُرَى فَلِلَّهِ وَلِلرَّسُولِ وَلِذِي الْقُرْبَى وَالْيَتَامَى وَالْمَسَاكِينِ وَابْنِ السَّبِيلِ كَيْ لَا يَكُونَ دُولَةً بَيْنَ الْأَغْنِيَاءِ مِنكُمْ وَمَا آتَاكُمُ الرَّسُولُ فَخُذُوهُ وَمَا نَهَاكُمْ عَنْهُ فَانتَهُوا وَاتَّقُوا اللَّهَ إِنَّ اللَّهَ شَدِيدُ الْعِقَابِ﴾ (سورة الحشر، 59 أيت نمبر 7)
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا فَتَحَ الْإِمَامُ بَلَدًا عَنْوَةً عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَاتَلَ أَهْلَ خَيْبَرَ، فَغَلَبَ عَلَى النَّخْلِ وَالْأَرْضِ، وَأَخَأَهُمْ إِلَى قَصْرِهِمْ، فَصَاحَوهُ عَلَى أَنَّ لِرَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم الصَّفْرَاءَ، وَالْبَيْضَاءَ، وَالخَلْقَةَ، وَلَهُمْ مَا حَمَلَتْ رِكَابُهُمْ، عَلَى أَنْ لَا يَكْتُمُوا، وَلَا يُغَيِّبُوا شَيْئًا، فَإِنْ فَعَلُوا فَلَا ذِمَّةَ لَهُمْ، وَلَا عَهْدَ فَغَيَّبُوا مَسْكًا حِيَيَ بْنِ أَخْطَبَ... فَوَجَدُوا الْمَسْكَ، فَقَتَلَ ابْنَ أَبِي الْحَقَيْقِ وَسَبَى نِسَاءَهُمْ وَذَرَارِيَّهُمْ (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي حُكْمِ أَرْضِ خَيْبَرَ، نمبر 3006)
اصول : جب امام کسی مقام کو اپنی طاقت سے فتح کرے تو اختیار ہے چاہے تو مجاہدین میں تقسیم کرے یا ان باشندوں کو بر قرار رکھ کر جزیہ مقرر کر دے۔
25. And when the Imam conquers a town by force (anwah), he has the choice: if he wishes, he divides it among the combatants; if he wishes, he keeps its inhabitants on it and imposes jizyah on them and kharaj on their lands. Evidence (1): The verse for establishing when the Imam conquers a town by force: 'Whatever Allah restored to His Messenger from the people of the towns, it is for Allah and for the Messenger and for the near relatives and orphans and the needy and the wayfarer, so that it not be a circulation among the rich among you. And whatever the Messenger gives you, take it; and whatever he forbids you, abstain from it.' (Surah al-Hashr, verse 7). Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing when the Imam conquers a town by force: from Ibn Umar, that the Prophet fought the people of Khaybar, and conquered the palm trees and land, and drove them to their fortress, and they made peace with him on the condition that the yellow, white, and made things belong to the Messenger of Allah, and for them what their mounts carry, on condition that they hide nothing and conceal nothing; and if they do, then no covenant and no pledge. And they hid a hide of Huyayy ibn Akhtab... so they found the hide, and he killed Ibn Abi al-Haqiq and captured their women and children. (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on the ruling of Khaybar land, 3006). Principle: When the Imam conquers a place by his force, he has the choice: either to distribute among the mujahidin or to keep the inhabitants and impose jizyah.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This ruling discusses the disposition of land conquered by force ('anwah). The Imam has two options: either to distribute the land among the Muslim fighters as ghanimah (spoils), or to leave the land in the hands of the original inhabitants and impose jizyah (poll tax) on them and kharaj (land tax) on their lands. The proof from Surah al-Hashr 7 indicates that the disposal of conquered lands and wealth is at the discretion of the leader, not to be monopolized by the rich. The hadith of Khaybar shows that the Prophet made a treaty with the inhabitants, allowing them to remain on their land in exchange for taxes, but when they violated the treaty, he punished them. This establishes the precedent for the Imam's option. In Hanafi fiqh, the ruling is that conquered land (ard al-'anwah) becomes fay' for the Muslim state, and the Imam's decision is binding but should be based on public interest.

Key Terms
عنوة (‘anwah): By force; conquest through military overpowering, as opposed to sulhan (peaceful surrender).
الجزية (al-jizyah): A poll tax imposed on non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis) in return for protection and exemption from military service.
الخراج (al-kharāj): Land tax on agricultural land owned by non-Muslims or land that becomes state property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only distribute among fighters
B) Only impose jizyah and kharaj
C) Either distribute or impose jizyah and kharaj
D) Leave the land fallow

Key Takeaway
The Imam has full discretion over land conquered by force: he may either distribute it among soldiers or leave it with inhabitants and impose jizyah and kharaj, based on Quranic and Prophetic evidence.

Aman Given by a Free Muslim is Valid and Binding
Ruling on aman with four proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on aman given by a free Muslim and distinguish the conditions under which it is valid.

Core Idea
Aman from any free Muslim is binding on the entire community.

This lesson examines a foundational ruling from al-Quduri on the law of aman (safe conduct) in jihad. The text establishes that any free Muslim—man or woman—can grant aman to an enemy, and once given, it becomes sacred and binding on all Muslims. The only exception is when honoring the aman leads to public harm, in which case the imam must formally nullify it. The passage also provides four proofs (hadith and Quran) that anchor this ruling in revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is granting aman (safe conduct) to a disbeliever or group. The ruling is that the aman is valid (sahih) and it becomes impermissible (haram) for any Muslim to fight them.
The ruling applies to any free Muslim, male or female.
2
Recognize the condition for nullification
The text states an exception: if honoring the aman leads to mafsada (corruption), the imam must formally notify the enemy (an-nabd) before resuming hostilities.
Only the imam has authority to nullify, not individuals.
3
Examine the proofs
Four proofs are cited: 1) hadith of Ali on the unity of Muslim covenant, 2) hadith of Umm Hani showing the Prophet affirmed a woman's aman, 3) a Quranic verse on covenant-breakers, and 4) the verse on an-nabd (8:58).
Each proof supports the binding nature of a valid aman.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi position is that any free Muslim can grant aman, while Imam al-Shafi'i restricts it to the imam or his deputy.
The Hanafi view relies on the hadith of Umm Hani and the principle that the covenant of Muslims is one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا أَمِنَ رَجُلٌ حُرٌّ أَوِ امْرَأَةٌ حُرَّةٌ كَافِرًا أَوْ جَمَاعَةً أَوْ أَهْلَ حِصْنٍ أَوْ مَدِينَةٍ صَحَّ أَمَانُهُمْ وَلَا يَجُوزُ لِأَحَدٍ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ قِتَالَهُمْ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ فِيهِ مَفْسَدَةٌ فَيَنْبِذُ إِلَيْهِمُ الْإِمَامُ. وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ هَذَا: «الَّذِينَ عَاهَدْتَ مِنْهُمْ ثُمَّ يَنْقُضُونَ عَهْدَهُمْ فِي كُلِّ مَرَّةٍ وَهُمْ لَا يَتَّقُونَ» (سُورَةُ الْأَنْفَالِ، ٨:٥٦). وَجْهٌ: (٢) الْحَدِيثُ: قَالَ: «خَطَبَنَا عَلِيٌّ فَقَالَ: مَا عِنْدَنَا كِتَابٌ نَقْرَؤُهُ إِلَّا كِتَابَ اللهِ وَمَا فِي هَذِهِ الصَّحِيفَةِ، فَقَالَ: فِيهَا الْجِرَاحَاتُ وَأَسْنَانُ الْإِبِلِ ... وَذِمَّةُ الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَاحِدَةٌ، فَمَنْ أَخْفَرَ مُسْلِمًا فَعَلَيْهِ مِثْلُ ذَلِكَ» (صَحِيحُ الْبُخَارِيِّ، بَابُ ذِمَّةِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَجِوَارِهِمْ وَاحِدَةٌ، رَقْمُ ٣١٧٢). وَجْهٌ: (٣) الْحَدِيثُ: أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ أُمَّ هَانِئٍ بِنْتَ أَبِي طَالِبٍ تَقُولُ: فَقُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ، زَعَمَ ابْنُ أُمِّي عَلِيٌّ أَنَّهُ قَاتِلٌ رَجُلًا قَدْ أَجَرْتُهُ فُلَانَ بْنَ هُبَيْرَةَ، فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ ﷺ: «قَدْ أَجَرْنَا مَنْ أَجَرْتِ يَا أُمَّ هَانِئٍ». قَالَتْ أُمُّ هَانِئٍ: وَذَلِكَ ضُحًى. (صَحِيحُ الْبُخَارِيِّ، بَابُ أَمَانِ النِّسَاءِ وَجِوَارِهِنَّ، رَقْمُ ٣١٧١). وَجْهٌ: (٤) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ هَذَا: ﴿وَإِمَّا تَخَافَنَّ مِن قَوْمٍ خِيَانَةً فَانْبِذْ إِلَيْهِمْ عَلَى سَوَاءٍ إِنَّ اللهَ لَا يُحِبُّ الْخَائِنِينَ﴾ (سُورَةُ الْأَنْفَالِ، ٨:٥٨).
And if a free man or a free woman gives aman to a disbeliever, or a group, or the people of a fortress or a city, their aman is valid, and it is not permissible for any of the Muslims to fight them unless there is corruption, then the imam should notify them. Evidence (1): The hadith establishing this: 'Those with whom you have made a covenant, then they break their covenant every time, and they do not fear [Allah].' (Surah al-Anfal, 8:56). Evidence (2): The hadith: He said: 'Ali addressed us and said: We have no book that we recite except the Book of Allah and what is in this sheet. He said: In it are the wounds and the teeth of camels... and the covenant of the Muslims is one, so whoever breaches a Muslim's covenant, upon him is such and such.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter: The covenant of the Muslims and their protection is one, no. 3172). Evidence (3): The hadith: That he heard Umm Hani bint Abi Talib say: I said: O Messenger of Allah, my brother Ali claims that he will kill a man I have given protection to, so-and-so son of Hubayra. The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'We have given protection to whom you have given protection, O Umm Hani.' Umm Hani said: And that was at forenoon. (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter: The aman of women and their protection, no. 3171). Evidence (4): The verse establishing this: 'And if you fear from a people betrayal, then throw [their treaty] back to them with equity. Indeed, Allah does not like the treacherous.' (Surah al-Anfal, 8:58).
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is a matn ruling from al-Quduri on the law of aman (safe conduct) in jihad. The ruling states that aman given by any free Muslim—man or woman—is valid and binding on the entire Muslim community. It is therefore prohibited (haram) for any Muslim to fight those who have been given aman. The exception is if there is mafsada (corruption or public harm) in honoring the aman, in which case the imam must formally nullify it by an-nabd (throwing back the treaty) as per the Quranic verse. The four proofs provided are: (1) a Quranic verse about covenant-breakers (though this is more about the permissibility of fighting when the enemy breaks the covenant, it supports the principle that a valid covenant must be honored unless broken), (2) the hadith of 'Ali that the covenant of Muslims is one and breaching it incurs a curse, (3) the hadith of Umm Hani' where the Prophet ﷺ affirmed her grant of aman, showing that a woman's aman is also binding, and (4) the explicit Quranic command to notify before fighting if betrayal is feared. The ruling is clear that aman is a serious matter and must be respected by all Muslims.

Key Terms
أمان (amān): Safe conduct or protection granted to an enemy combatant or group, guaranteeing their safety from attack.
مفسدة (mafsadah): Corruption or public harm that would result from honoring the aman, such as betrayal or espionage.
نبذ (nabdh): Formal notification to the enemy that the treaty or aman is being terminated, done by the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must the imam do if honoring an aman would lead to public corruption?
A) Immediately attack the enemy without notice.
B) Notify the enemy by throwing back the treaty (an-nabd) before fighting.
C) Cancel the aman secretly and then attack.
D) Ignore the aman because it was given by a woman.

Key Takeaway
Aman from any free Muslim is binding; only the imam can nullify it for public harm, and only after formal notice.

Invalidity of Aman from Dhimmi, Captive, and Trader
Ruling that aman from dhimmi, captive, or trader is invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of aman granted by a dhimmi, captive, or trader and explain the dalil used.

Core Idea
Only Muslims with community authority can grant aman; others' aman is invalid.

In this lesson, we examine a clear ruling from Al-Quduri's matn: the aman granted by a dhimmi, a captive, or a trader entering enemy territory is not valid. We explore the rationale and the prophetic evidence from the hadith of Ali (RA). The ruling underscores that aman is a collective prerogative of the Muslim community.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that the aman of a dhimmi, a captive, or a trader is invalid (batil). First, confirm which act is being ruled upon: granting aman (protection) to enemy non-Muslims. Then note the hukm level: batil (void).
2
Locate the dalil
The author provides a hadith from Ali (RA) in Sahih Muslim: 'The covenant of the Muslims is one, the lowest among them can be bound by it.' This is the proof. Identify the type: hadith ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key phrase is 'the covenant of the Muslims is one' – the word 'Muslims' restricts the authority to give aman to Muslims only. Dhimmis are not Muslims, captives are not free agents, and traders lack the general authority of the community. Thus their aman is not binding.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Hanafi school holds this as the relied-upon view, but other schools may consider a dhimmi's aman valid in some contexts. Recognize that this is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
Cross-madhhab: mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on the literal reading of the hadith. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that aman from these individuals is invalid. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
Authority weight: zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَمَانُ ذِمِّيٍّ وَلَا الْأَسِيرِ وَلَا التَّاجِرِ الَّذِي يَدْخُلُ عَلَيْهِمْ. وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ هَذَا: قَالَ: خَطَبَنَا عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَالِبٍ فَقَالَ: وَذِمَّةُ الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَاحِدَةٌ، يَسْعَى بِمَا أَدْنَاهُمْ، وَمَنِ ادَّعَى إِلَى غَيْرِ أَبِيهِ أَوِ انْتَمَى إِلَى غَيْرِ مَوَالِيهِ فَعَلَيْهِ لَعْنَةُ اللهِ وَالْمَلَائِكَةِ وَالنَّاسِ أَجْمَعِينَ لَا يَقْبَلُ اللهُ مِنْهُ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ صَرْفًا وَلَا عَدْلًا. (صَحِيحُ مُسْلِمٍ، بَابُ فَضْلِ الْمَدِينَةِ، رَقْمُ ١٣٧٠).
And the aman of a dhimmi, nor the captive, nor the trader who enters upon them is valid. Evidence (1): The hadith establishing this: He said: 'Ali ibn Abi Talib addressed us and said: The covenant of the Muslims is one, the lowest among them can be bound by it, and whoever claims to be other than his father or affiliates with other than his masters, upon him is the curse of Allah, the angels, and all people; Allah will not accept from him any compensation or ransom on the Day of Judgment.' (Sahih Muslim, Chapter: The virtue of Madinah, no. 1370).
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage continues the matn rulings on aman. It states that the aman of a dhimmi (a non-Muslim subject of the Islamic state), a captive (prisoner of war), or a trader who enters enemy lands is not valid. The reason is that these individuals do not have the authority to represent the Muslim ummah in granting aman. The dhimmi is not a Muslim, the captive is under enemy control, and the trader is a private individual whose status is ambiguous. The proof is the hadith of 'Ali that 'the covenant of the Muslims is one'—meaning only Muslims who are part of the community (dhimmis are not Muslims) can issue a binding aman. Additionally, captives and traders lack the requisite standing.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmī): A non-Muslim living permanently under Muslim rule with a contract of protection (dhimma).
أسير (asīr): A prisoner of war (captive) taken by Muslims from the enemy.
تاجر يدخل عليهم (tājir yadkhulu ʿalayhim): A Muslim trader who enters enemy territory for commerce, not formally authorized to give aman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A Muslim trader enters a non-Muslim country for business and gives aman to a local. According to the Hanafi school, is this aman valid?
A) Yes, because he is a Muslim.
B) No, because he is a trader not authorized to give aman.
C) Yes, because any Muslim can give aman.
D) No, because he is in enemy territory.

Key Takeaway
Aman is a prerogative of the Muslim community; only Muslims with authority can grant it, not dhimmis, captives, or unauthorized traders.

Dispute on Aman by a Slave: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on aman by a slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the validity of a slave's aman, explain the Sahibayn's evidence, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A Muslim slave's aman is valid according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a Muslim slave can grant safe conduct (aman) to enemy combatants. Imam Abu Hanifa conditioned it on the master's permission to fight, while his two main students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), declared it unconditionally valid. The commentary presents their proofs and shows why the Sahibayn's view became the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the positions
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling (aman invalid unless master permits fighting) and the Sahibayn's ruling (aman valid unconditionally).
Both are within the Hanafi school.
2
Examine the first proof of the Sahibayn
Read the hadith 'The covenant of the Muslims is one, the lowest among them can be bound by it.' Explain how this supports the slave's aman (the slave is among the lowest).
This hadith is general; Abu Hanifa restricts it to free Muslims.
3
Examine the second proof
Read the explicit hadith from Ali: 'There is nothing for the slave from the spoils except low-quality goods, and his aman is permissible.' Note the direct statement.
This hadith addresses the slave specifically in a military context.
4
Examine the third proof: practice of 'Umar
Read the narration about 'Umar's ruling that a Muslim slave's aman is binding. Understand that this serves as a precedent.
This is a historical application of the principle.
5
Determine the tarjih
Note that the mufta bihi position is that of the Sahibayn. Explain why their evidence is considered stronger: explicit text and early caliphal practice.
The later Hanafi authorities prefer the Sahibayn's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَمَانُ الْعَبْدِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَأْذَنَ لَهُ مَوْلَاهُ فِي الْقِتَالِ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ يَصِحُ أَمَانُهُ. وَجْهٌ (١) دَلِيلُ الصَّاحِبَيْنِ الْحَدِيثُ: وَذِمَّةُ الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَاحِدَةٌ، يَسْعَى بِمَا أَدْنَاهُمْ (صَحِيحُ مُسْلِمٍ، رَقْمُ ١٣٧٠). وَجْهٌ (٢) الْحَدِيثُ عَنْ عَلِيِّ بْنِ أَبِي طَالِبٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ ﷺ: «لَيْسَ لِلْعَبْدِ مِنَ الْغَنِيمَةِ شَيْءٌ إِلَّا خُرْثَيِّ الْمَتَاعِ، وَأَمَانُهُ جَائِزٌ إِذَا هُوَ أَعْطَى الْقَوْمَ الْأَمَانَ» (السُّنَنُ الْكُبْرَى لِلْبَيْهَقِيِّ، رَقْمُ ١٨١٧٢). وَفِي رِوَايَةٍ: فَإِنْ غَلَبُوا عَلَى أَمْوَالِنَا وَأَحْرَزُوهَا بِدَرَاهِمَ مَلَكُوهَا فَقَالُوا: أَمَّنْتُمُونَا وَأَخْرَجُوا إِلَيْنَا السَّهْمَ فِيهِ كِتَابُ أَمَانِهِمْ فَقُلْنَا: هَذَا عَبْدٌ وَالْعَبْدُ لَا يَقْدِرُ عَلَى شَيْءٍ قَالُوا: لَا نَدْرِي عَبْدَكُمْ مِنْ حُرِّكُمْ، وَقَدْ خَرَجُوا بِأَمَانٍ، قُلْنَا: فَارْجِعُوا بِأَمَانٍ قَالُوا: لَا نَرْجِعُ إِلَيْهِ أَبَدًا فَكَتَبْنَا إِلَى عُمَرَ بَعْضَ قِصَّتِهِمْ، فَكَتَبَ عُمَرُ: «أَنَّ الْعَبْدَ الْمُسْلِمَ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ أَمَانُهُ أَمَانُهُمْ» قَالَ: فَفَاتَنَا مَا كُنَّا أَشْرَفْنَا عَلَيْهِ مِنْ غَنَائِمِهِمْ. (مُصَنَّفُ عَبْدِ الرَّزَّاقِ، بَابُ الْجِوَارِ، رَقْمُ ٩٤٣٦).
And the aman of a slave is not valid according to Abu Hanifa unless his master permits him to fight. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: His aman is valid. Evidence (1): The proof of the two companions (Sahibayn) is the hadith: 'The covenant of the Muslims is one, the lowest among them can be bound by it.' (Sahih Muslim, no. 1370). Evidence (2): The hadith from 'Ali ibn Abi Talib who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'There is nothing for the slave from the spoils except the low-quality goods, and his aman is permissible when he gives aman to the people.' (Sunan al-Kubra of al-Bayhaqi, no. 18172). And in a narration: 'Then if they overcome our property and take possession of it by dirhams, they own it. They said: You have given us aman and you brought out to us the arrow in which was the document of their aman. So we said: This is a slave, and a slave is not capable of anything. They said: We do not know your slave from your free; they have gone out with aman. We said: Then return with aman. They said: We will never return to it. So we wrote to 'Umar part of their story, and 'Umar wrote: 'Indeed, the Muslim slave is from the Muslims; his aman is their aman.' He said: So we lost what we had been close to of their spoils.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter of Jiwar, no. 9436).
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (dispute within the school) regarding the validity of aman given by a slave. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that a slave's aman is not valid unless his master has authorized him to fight in jihad, implying that only when the slave is in a state of jihad can his aman be considered. His reasoning is that a slave lacks full legal capacity (wilayah) to bind the community. In contrast, Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (the Sahibayn) argue that a slave's aman is valid unconditionally. Their evidence is the same hadith used for previous rulings: 'The covenant of the Muslims is one, the lowest among them can be bound by it'—the slave being among the lowest. They also cite a specific hadith where the Prophet ﷺ explicitly stated that a slave's aman is permissible. Additionally, they bring a historical precedent from the caliph 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, who ruled that a Muslim slave's aman is binding, thereby validating the practice. The commentary in the book presents both positions with their proofs. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, that the aman of a Muslim slave is valid. This is based on the strength of the hadith evidence and the practice of the early caliphs.

Key Terms
عبد (ʿabd): A Muslim male slave who is owned by a master.
إذن المولى في القتال (idhn al-mawlā fī al-qitāl): Permission from the master for the slave to participate in military combat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, is the aman of a Muslim slave valid?
A) No, never.
B) Yes, always.
C) Only if the master permits fighting.
D) Only if the slave is free.

Key Takeaway
The aman of a Muslim slave is valid according to the relied-upon Hanafi position, based on explicit hadith and the practice of 'Umar.

Spoils from a Conquered Enemy Who Had Conquered Others
Ruling on ownership of spoils taken from a third party who had seized them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on spoils when property changes hands through conquest by a third party, and cite the Quranic and hadith evidence for this ruling.

Core Idea
Spoils taken from a conquered enemy are lawful even if that enemy had taken them from another — possession through conquest transfers ownership.

This lesson examines a multi-party conflict scenario where the Turks conquer the Romans and take their property, and then Muslims conquer the Turks. The ruling clarifies that such property becomes lawful spoils for Muslims. The author supports this with verses from the Quran and a hadith, establishing that effective possession through conquest (ghalb) transfers ownership, and that Muslims may lawfully take spoils from defeated enemies regardless of the property's prior chain of ownership.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
Identify the chain of conquest: Turks overcome Romans, then Muslims overcome Turks. The property is taken from the Turks, not directly from the original non-Muslim owners.
2
State the ruling
When Muslims defeat the Turks, the property they recover is halal (lawful) as spoils. The matn states: 'فَإِنْ غَلَبْنَا عَلَى التُّرْكِ حَلَّ لَنَا مَا أَخَذْنَاهُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ.'
3
Identify the first proof
The author cites verse 8:69 from Surah al-Anfal, which commands to consume what you have taken as booty (ghanimah) as lawful and good. This establishes the general permissibility of spoils.
The verse is the primary textual evidence for the ruling.
4
Identify the second proof
The author also cites the hadith 'Whoever overcomes something, then it becomes his,' attributed to Usamah bin Zaid. This supports that ownership transfers through effective conquest.
Although the hadith lacks a known chain in this text, it reinforces the principle.
5
Note the additional rule on enemy purchase
The passage also states that if the enemy acquires Muslim property through purchase (with dirhams), they own it. This shows that valid transactions also transfer ownership; if recovered later, it becomes spoils.
Purchase (ahrazuha bi-darāhima) is equated to conquest in transferring ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا غَلَبَ التُّرْكُ عَلَى الرُّومِ فَسَبَوْهُمْ وَأَخَذُوا أَمْوَالَهُمْ مَلَكُوهَا. فَإِنْ غَلَبْنَا عَلَى التُّرْكِ حَلَّ لَنَا مَا أَخَذْنَاهُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ. فَإِنْ غَلَبُوا عَلَى أَمْوَالِنَا وَأَحْرَزُوهَا بِدَرَاهِمَ مَلَكُوهَا. وَجْهٌ: (١) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ ذَلِكَ: ﴿مَا أَفَاءَ اللهُ عَلَى رَسُولِهِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْقُرَى فَلِلَّهِ وَلِلرَّسُولِ وَلِذِي الْقُرْبَى وَالْيَتَامَى وَالْمَسَاكِينِ وَابْنِ السَّبِيلِ﴾ (سُورَةُ الْحَشْرِ، ٥٩:٧). وَوَجْهٌ: (٢) الْآيَةُ: ﴿فَكُلُوا مِمَّا غَنِمْتُمْ حَلَالًا طَيِّبًا﴾ (سُورَةُ الْأَنْفَالِ، ٨:٦٩). وَوَجْهٌ: (١) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ مَا إِذَا غَلَبُوا عَلَى أَمْوَالِنَا: ﴿مَا أَفَاءَ اللهُ عَلَى رَسُولِهِ﴾ (سُورَةُ الْحَشْرِ، ٥٩:٧). وَوَجْهٌ: (٢) الْحَدِيثُ عَنْ أُسَامَةَ بْنِ زَيْدٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ ﷺ: «مَنْ غَلَبَ عَلَى شَيْءٍ فَهُوَ لَهُ» أَوْ كَمَا قَالَ. (ذَكَرَهُ الْمُصَنِّفُ بِدُونِ إِسْنَادٍ).
And if the Turks overcome the Romans and take them captive and take their property, they own it. Then if we overcome the Turks, what we take from that becomes halal for us. And if they overcome our property and take possession of it with dirhams, they own it. Evidence (1): The verse establishing this: 'What Allah gave as booty (fay') to His Messenger from the people of the townships – it is for Allah and for the Messenger and for the near of kin and the orphans and the needy and the wayfarer.' (Surah al-Hashr, 59:7). And Evidence (2): The verse: 'So consume what you have taken of booty (ghanimah) as lawful and good.' (Surah al-Anfal, 8:69). And Evidence (1) for the case when they overcome our property: The verse: 'What Allah gave as booty (fay') to His Messenger...' (Surah al-Hashr, 59:7). And Evidence (2): The hadith from Usamah bin Zaid (may Allah be pleased with him) said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Whoever overcomes something, then it becomes his' or as he said. (Mentioned by the author without chain).
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage addresses the status of spoils (ghanimah/fay') in a multi-party conflict scenario. The ruling is that when a non-Muslim group (Turks) conquers another non-Muslim group (Romans) and takes their property, the Turks become the owners of that property. Then, if the Muslims subsequently defeat the Turks, the property taken from the Turks becomes lawful (halal) for the Muslims as spoils of war. Similarly, if the enemy (Turks) captures Muslim property and takes possession of it (e.g., by purchasing it with dirhams, i.e., a valid transaction), they own it, and if later recovered, it is treated as enemy property. The proofs cited include verses from Surah al-Hashr about fay' (booty taken without direct fighting) and Surah al-Anfal about ghanimah, indicating that such acquisitions are lawful for Muslims. The hadith from Usamah (although without a known chain in this text) supports the principle that ownership transfers through conquest (ghalb). This ruling is based on the principle that property changes hands through effective possession and conquest, and that Muslims may lawfully take as spoils property that was previously owned by enemy combatants, even if it was originally taken from another non-Muslim group.

Key Terms
غلب (ghalaba): To overcome or conquer, resulting in transfer of ownership of movable property through possession.
سبي (saby): Captives taken in war.
أحرزوها بدراهم (aḥrazūhā bi-darāhima): To take possession of property by means of purchase (paying dirhams), indicating a valid transaction that transfers ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the Turks conquer the Romans and take their property, and then Muslims conquer the Turks, what is the ruling on that property?
A) It must be returned to the Romans.
B) It is lawful for Muslims as spoils.
C) It is forbidden because it was previously owned by Romans.
D) It belongs to the Turks' families.

Key Takeaway
Property taken by an enemy through conquest or purchase becomes spoils for Muslims when they defeat that enemy, as supported by Quran and hadith.

Ruling on Recovered Property from Enemy Before and After Division
Quduri matn ruling on recovered property and merchant purchase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for property recovered from the enemy before and after booty distribution, and apply the rule for a merchant's purchase in Dar al-Harb.

Core Idea
Property recovered before booty division is returned free; after division, it may be reclaimed by paying its value.

This passage from Quduri's Mukhtasar sets out two key scenarios in which Muslims recover property that the enemy had seized from them. The ruling distinguishes between recovery before the official distribution of spoils and after, and also addresses the case where a Muslim merchant buys such property in enemy territory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time of recovery
Determine whether the property is found by Muslim forces before or after the imam divides the booty (ghanimah) among the soldiers.
The time of recovery relative to division is the key factor.
2
Apply the pre-division ruling
If recovered before division, the property is returned to its original owner without any compensation to the fighters.
The property is not considered spoils because it still belongs to the original owner.
3
Apply the post-division ruling
If recovered after division, the original owner may reclaim the property by paying its current value (qimah) to the soldier who holds it, but only if he wishes.
The owner is not compelled to pay; his choice.
4
Analyze the merchant purchase scenario
If a Muslim merchant buys such property in Dar al-Harb and brings it to Dar al-Islam, the original owner has the option to take it by paying the merchant the exact purchase price, or leave it.
This is similar to the post-division case but the compensation is the merchant's cost, not market value.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ ظَهَرَ عَلَيْهَا الْمُسْلِمُونَ فَوَجَدُوهَا قَبْلَ الْقِسْمَةِ فَهِيَ فَهُمْ بِغَيْرِ شَيْءٍ وَإِنْ وَجَدُوهَا بَعْدَ الْقِسْمَةِ أَخَذُوهَا بِالْقِيمَةِ إِنْ أَحَبُّوا وَ وَإِنْ دَخَلَ دَارَ الْحَرْبِ تَاجِرٌ فَاشْتَرَى ذَلِكَ بِثَمَنٍ وَأَخْرَجَهُ إِلَى دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ فَمَالِكُهُ الْأَوَّلُ بِالْخِيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَهُ بِالثَّمَنِ الَّذِي اشْتَرَاهُ التَّاجِرُ بِهِ وَإِنْ شَاءَ تَرَكَهُ
If Muslims overpower them and find it before division, then it is for them without anything. And if they find it after division, they take it at its value if they wish. And if a merchant enters the Abode of War and buys that with a price and brings it out to the Abode of Islam, then its original owner has the choice: if he wishes, he takes it for the price with which the merchant bought it, and if he wishes, he leaves it.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This matn from Quduri's Mukhtasar addresses the recovery of property that the enemy had previously taken from Muslims. If recovered before distribution as booty (ghanimah), it is returned to the original owner without compensation. If recovered after distribution, the owner may reclaim it by paying its value (qimah) to the possessor, but only if he wishes; he is not compelled. Additionally, if a Muslim merchant buys such property in Dar al-Harb and brings it to Dar al-Islam, the original owner has a choice: either to pay the merchant his purchase price and take the property, or to leave it. This ruling reflects the Hanafi principle that the enemy's possession of a Muslim's property is incomplete (mulk ghayr tam). The proofs cited in the sharh include hadith from Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas.

Key Terms
الْقِسْمَة (al-qismah): The official distribution of booty (ghanimah) among the warriors after bringing it to Dar al-Islam.
الْقِيمَة (al-qimah): The monetary value of the property at the time of recovery.
دَارُ الْحَرْب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim control where Islamic law is not enforced and war is permissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Muslim merchant buys property in Dar al-Harb that was originally owned by a Muslim, and brings it to Dar al-Islam, what are the original owner's options?
A) He can take it for free.
B) He can take it by paying the merchant the same price the merchant paid.
C) He can only leave it; he has no right to take it.
D) He can take it at half the price.

Key Takeaway
Pre-division recovery returns property to owner free; post-division recovery requires payment of value; merchant-purchased property gives owner option to pay the merchant's price.

Categories of Muslims the Enemy Cannot Own
Ruling that enemies do not own certain freedom-bound Muslims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four categories of Muslims that enemies cannot own and explain the reason for their exemption.

Core Idea
Enemies cannot own Muslims with an inherent right to eventual freedom.

This lesson examines a concise ruling from the Quduri matn: when the enemy captures Muslims, their ownership does not extend to certain categories who have an inchoate right to freedom. Understanding this principle is crucial for the law of jihad and the protection of vulnerable individuals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
Read the Arabic matn: وَلَا يَمْلِكُ عَلَيْنَا أَهْلُ الْحَرْبِ بِالْغَلَبَةِ ... The ruling declares that the enemy does not gain ownership of four specific categories of Muslims.
Note the double negative: 'do not own'.
2
List the four protected categories
From the matn: mudabbar, umm walad, mukatab, and free persons (ahrar). Write them down and memorise them.
These are listed in the source exactly.
3
Understand the rationale for each category
Each category has a strong connection to freedom: mudabbar is promised freedom upon the master's death; umm walad is the mother of her master's child and becomes free upon his death; mukatab has a contract for eventual freedom; free persons are already free. The enemy's ownership would violate these rights.
Ordinary slaves (raqiq) are not protected—they can be owned.
4
Note the asymmetry in the second half of the ruling
The matn adds: وَنَمْلِكُ عَلَيْهِمْ جَمِيعَ ذَلِكَ 'and we own over them all of that.' Muslims, conversely, can own these same categories if captured from the enemy. This reflects the superior status of Muslims in Islamic law.
This asymmetry is a key Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَمْلِكُ عَلَيْنَا أَهْلُ الْحَرْبِ بِالْغَلَبَةِ مُدَبَّرِينَا وَأُمَّهَاتِ أَوْلَادِنَا وَمُكَاتَبِينَا وَأَحْرَارَنَا وَنَمْلِكُ عَلَيْهِمْ جَمِيعَ ذَلِكَ
And the people of war do not own over us, by overcoming, our mudabbars, our umm walads, our mukatabs, and our free persons, and we own over them all of that.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This matn states a key Hanafi principle: when the enemy captures Muslims, they cannot gain ownership of certain categories of persons who have a strong connection to freedom. These include: mudabbars (slaves promised freedom upon the master's death), umm walads (slave concubines who have borne a child to their master), mukatabs (slaves with a contract of manumission), and all free persons (ahrar). These individuals retain their status and cannot become owned by the enemy. Conversely, Muslims can own such persons from the enemy if they capture them. The proof cited in the sharh is from the practice of the Companions, particularly the statement of Ata'. The principle is that the enemy's possession is not valid over those who have an inherent right to freedom. Ordinary slaves (raqiq) are not included in this protection and can be owned by the enemy.

Key Terms
مُدَبَّر (mudabbar): A slave whose master has declared him free upon the master's death.
أُمُّ وَلَد (umm walad): A slave concubine who has given birth to her master's child.
مُكَاتَب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of manumission with his master, paying in installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following categories does the enemy NOT own according to this ruling?
A) Ordinary slaves (raqiq)
B) Mudabbars
C) Camels
D) Movable property

Key Takeaway
Enemy combatants cannot own Muslims who have a pre-existing right to freedom: mudabbar, umm walad, mukatab, and free persons.

Runaway Slave vs. Stray Camel: Enemy Ownership Dispute
Ruling on enemy ownership of runaway slave vs. stray camel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's position on enemy ownership of a runaway slave versus a stray camel, and explain the practical consequence of the Sahibayn's disagreement.

Core Idea
A slave's potential for freedom prevents enemy ownership; a camel's property nature does not.

This short matn from Al-Quduri presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute. Abu Hanifa distinguishes between a runaway slave and a stray camel when they fall into enemy hands. While the Sahibayn agree on the camel, they differ on the slave. Understanding this ruling clarifies the unique legal status of slaves as beings with potential freedom, not mere property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The matn presents two scenarios: a runaway slave entering enemy territory, and a stray camel entering enemy territory. Identify both.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling for each
Abu Hanifa rules that the enemy does NOT own the slave, but DOES own the camel. Note the difference.
The ruling for the camel is agreed upon by all Hanafis.
3
Recognize the Sahibayn's disagreement
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the enemy DOES own the runaway slave, treating it like other captured property.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the slave is recaptured before booty division, Abu Hanifa says he returns to his owner for free; Sahibayn say he becomes part of the booty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا أَبَقَ عَبْدُ الْمُسْلِمِ فَدَخَلَ إِلَيْهِمْ فَأَخَذُوهُ لَمْ يَمْلِكُوهُ عِنْدَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ فَإِنْ نَدَّ إِلَيْهِمْ بَعِيرٌ فَأَخَذُوهُ مَلَكُوهُ
And when a Muslim's slave runs away and enters to them (the enemy) and they take him, they do not own him according to Abu Hanifa. But if a camel strays to them and they take it, they own it.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This matn presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. Abu Hanifa holds that if a Muslim's ordinary slave (not a mudabbar, umm walad, or mukatab) runs away to enemy territory and the enemy captures him, the enemy does not gain ownership. This is because the slave has the potential for freedom and is not like ordinary property. However, if a camel (or any other movable property) strays into enemy hands, the enemy does gain ownership. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree on the slave: they hold that the enemy does own the runaway slave, as it is a form of captured property. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to the matn is the view of Abu Hanifa. The proofs cited in the sharh include a statement of Umar (رضي الله عنه) for Abu Hanifa's view and a statement of Ali (رضي الله عنه) for the Sahibayn.

Key Terms
آبِق (abiq): A slave who runs away from his master.
نَادَّ (nadda): To stray or run away (used for animals).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, does the enemy own a runaway Muslim slave?
A) Yes, because it is property.
B) No, because the slave has potential for freedom.
C) Yes, but only after division.
D) No, because the slave is free.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa distinguishes between a runaway slave (not owned by enemy) and a stray camel (owned) based on the slave's potential for freedom.

Temporary Distribution of Spoils Without Transport (Qismat al-Ida')
Ruling on distributing spoils when the imam lacks transport

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule of qismat al-ida' and explain its purpose as a trust distribution.

Core Idea
When no transport, spoils are temporarily given to warriors as a trust for transport, then returned for final division.

In times of war, the imam is responsible for transporting the spoils from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam. If he lacks the means, Shariah provides a practical solution: the spoils are distributed temporarily to the warriors as a trust (qismat al-ida'). Each warrior carries his portion, and upon reaching safety, they must return the items for the actual division. This ensures the spoils are moved without causing hardship to the state.

Guided Path
1
Identify the governing authority
The imam is responsible for arranging transport. When he has none, the ruling changes.
2
Understand the temporary distribution
The spoils are given to the warriors as a trust (ida'), not as ownership. They must return them for final division.
This is called qismat al-ida'.
3
Recognize the purpose
The purpose is to enable transport of the spoils to Dar al-Islam. The trust distribution facilitates this.
The trust ends upon reaching safe territory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ لِلْإِمَامِ حَمُولَةٌ يَحْمِلُ عَلَيْهَا الْغَنِيمَةَ قَسَّمَهَا بَيْنَ الْغَانِينَ قِسْمَةَ إِيدَاعِ لِيَحْمِلُوهَا إلَى دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ ثُمَّ يَرْجِعُهَا مِنْهُمْ وَيَقْسِمُهَا وَلا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْغَنَائِمِ قَبْلَ الْقِسْمَةِ ٢٢ وَمَنْ مَاتَ مِنْ الْعَالِمِينَ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ قَبْلَ إِخْرَاجِهَا فَلَا حَقَّ لَهُ فِي الْغَنِيمَةِ وَمَنْ مَاتَ مِنْهُمْ بَعْدَ إِخْرَاجِهَا إِلَى دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ فَنَصِيبُهُ لِوَرَثَتِهِ
And if the imam does not have transport to carry the spoils, he distributes them among the warriors as a trust distribution so that they carry them to the Abode of Islam, then he takes them back from them and distributes them. And it is not permissible to sell the spoils before division. And whoever among the warriors dies in the Abode of War before its removal, then he has no right in the spoils. And whoever among them dies after its removal to the Abode of Islam, then his share goes to his heirs.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This matn covers three rules related to ghanimah. (1) If the imam lacks transport to carry the spoils from Dar al-Harb, he can distribute the spoils temporarily to the warriors as a trust (qismat al-ida'), so each warrior carries his portion. Upon reaching Dar al-Islam, they must return the items for actual division. This is a practical solution. (2) It is prohibited to sell spoils before official division, based on a hadith that the Prophet forbade buying spoils until they are divided. (3) A warrior who dies in Dar al-Harb before the spoils are removed from there loses his right to a share; but if he dies after removal to Dar al-Islam, his share passes to his heirs. This distinction is because ownership is finalized only after the spoils are brought to safety in Islamic territory.

Key Terms
قِسْمَةُ إِيدَاعِ (qismat al-ida'): A temporary distribution of spoils as a trust to the warriors for transport purposes, not a final division.
حَمُولَة (hamulah): Beasts of burden or transport available to the imam to carry the spoils.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of qismat al-ida'?
A) To give warriors immediate ownership of spoils.
B) To enable transport of spoils to Dar al-Islam when the imam lacks means.
C) To sell spoils before division.
D) To divide spoils permanently among warriors.

Key Takeaway
When transport is unavailable, spoils are temporarily entrusted to warriors for transport, not as final ownership.

Prohibition of Selling Spoils Before Division
Prohibition of selling spoils before division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibition of selling spoils before official division and explain the reason.

Core Idea
Spoils cannot be sold before division because ownership is not yet determined.

The second rule in the passage is clear: selling spoils before the final division is not permitted. This prevents disputes and ensures fairness. Until the imam divides the spoils, no warrior has a specific right to any item. Selling before division would involve uncertainty (gharar) and possible usurpation of others' shares. The rule is based on a prophetic directive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited act
Selling spoils (ghanaim) before official division (qismah) is prohibited.
2
Understand the basis
The prohibition is because ownership has not been established. The spoils are collectively owned by the soldiers until the imam divides them.
This prevents injustice and gharar.
3
Recognize the consequences
If a sale occurs before division, the contract is batil (void). The goods must be returned.
The imam may also have the seller punished as a discretionary punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ لِلْإِمَامِ حَمُولَةٌ يَحْمِلُ عَلَيْهَا الْغَنِيمَةَ قَسَّمَهَا بَيْنَ الْغَانِينَ قِسْمَةَ إِيدَاعِ لِيَحْمِلُوهَا إلَى دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ ثُمَّ يَرْجِعُهَا مِنْهُمْ وَيَقْسِمُهَا وَلا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْغَنَائِمِ قَبْلَ الْقِسْمَةِ ٢٢ وَمَنْ مَاتَ مِنْ الْعَالِمِينَ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ قَبْلَ إِخْرَاجِهَا فَلَا حَقَّ لَهُ فِي الْغَنِيمَةِ وَمَنْ مَاتَ مِنْهُمْ بَعْدَ إِخْرَاجِهَا إِلَى دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ فَنَصِيبُهُ لِوَرَثَتِهِ
And if the imam does not have transport to carry the spoils, he distributes them among the warriors as a trust distribution so that they carry them to the Abode of Islam, then he takes them back from them and distributes them. And it is not permissible to sell the spoils before division. And whoever among the warriors dies in the Abode of War before its removal, then he has no right in the spoils. And whoever among them dies after its removal to the Abode of Islam, then his share goes to his heirs.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This matn covers three rules related to ghanimah. (1) If the imam lacks transport to carry the spoils from Dar al-Harb, he can distribute the spoils temporarily to the warriors as a trust (qismat al-ida'), so each warrior carries his portion. Upon reaching Dar al-Islam, they must return the items for actual division. This is a practical solution. (2) It is prohibited to sell spoils before official division, based on a hadith that the Prophet forbade buying spoils until they are divided. (3) A warrior who dies in Dar al-Harb before the spoils are removed from there loses his right to a share; but if he dies after removal to Dar al-Islam, his share passes to his heirs. This distinction is because ownership is finalized only after the spoils are brought to safety in Islamic territory.

Key Terms
بَيْع (bay'): Sale contract: transfer of ownership of a specific item for a price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on selling spoils before the official division?
A) Permissible with imam's consent.
B) Makruh but valid.
C) Haram and the contract is batil.
D) Permissible only for necessities.

Key Takeaway
Spoils may not be sold before division because ownership is not yet established.

Effect of a Warrior's Death on His Right to Spoils
Ruling on warrior's share upon death before or after removal of spoils

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule regarding a warrior's share if he dies before or after the spoils are removed from Dar al-Harb.

Core Idea
A warrior's right to spoils is finalized only after the spoils are removed to Dar al-Islam.

The passage distinguishes between two scenarios: a warrior dies before the spoils are removed from Dar al-Harb, or after removal. In the first case, he loses all right to the spoils; in the second, his share goes to his heirs. This is because ownership of spoils is finalized only when they are brought to safety in Islamic territory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two timings
Death before removal (from Dar al-Harb) vs. death after removal (to Dar al-Islam).
2
Apply the rule for death before removal
The warrior loses his right entirely. No share passes to heirs.
3
Apply the rule for death after removal
The warrior's share is inherited by his heirs.
This indicates ownership was established upon removal.
4
Understand the rationale
Ownership of spoils is contingent on safe arrival in Dar al-Islam. Before that, it is potential, not actual.

Definition of Salab (Spoils of the Slain)
Defines salab and provides multiple hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of salab and identify the key hadith proofs that establish the killer's entitlement.

Core Idea
Salab is the killer's right—the slain's clothes, weapons, and mount are granted to him as nafal.

In the law of ghanimah, the salab (spoils taken from the slain enemy) has a specific definition and a special ruling. This lesson examines the Hanafi definition and the prophetic practice that supports it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being defined? The term 'salab' is a category of spoils taken from a slain enemy. The ruling is that the killer is entitled to it as an additional grant (nafal).
This is a definition ruling, so the focus is on the scope of the term.
2
Parse the definition
The definition states: 'السَّلَبُ مَا عَلَى الْمَقْتُولِ مِنْ ثِيَابِهِ وَسِلَاحِهِ وَمَرْكَبِهِ' meaning clothes, weapons, and mount. Understand each item and why the mount is included.
Note that the mount is considered part of the slain's immediate belongings.
3
Locate the dalil
Identify the hadith proofs cited: the story of the Bedouin (Bukhari), Ibn Mas'ud receiving Abu Jahl's sword, the extra camel in a detachment, and the Mu'tah incident with Khalid. Each supports the killer's right to the entire salab.
These are ahad hadith, but they are accepted as evidence in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Understand the legal effect
The definition and proofs establish that the salab is not part of the general ghanimah pool; it belongs exclusively to the killer. This incentivizes bravery in battle.
Some schools differ on the scope or require khums, but Hanafi school holds it as a separate entitlement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ السّير
وَالسَّلَبُ مَا عَلَى الْمَقْتُولِ مِنْ ثِيَابِهِ وَسِلَاحِهِ وَمَرْكَبِهِ
فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم : صَدَقَ فَأَعْطَاهُ. فَبِعْتُ الدِّرْعَ، فَابْتَعْتُ بِهِ مَخْرَفًا فِي بَنِي سَلِمَةَ، فَإِنَّهُ لَأَوَّلُ مَالٍ تَأَثَلْتُهُ فِي الْإِسْلَامِ.
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَالسَّلَبُ مَا عَلَى الْمَقْتُولِ مِنْ ثِيَابِهِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْن مَسْعُودٍ، قَالَ: «نَفَّلَنِي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَوْمَ بَدْرٍ سَيْفَ أَبِي جَهْلِ كَانَ قَتَلَهُ»
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَالسَّلَبُ مَا عَلَى الْمَقْتُولِ مِنْ ثِيَابِهِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، قَالَ: «بَعَثَنَا رَسُولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي سَرِيَّةٍ فَبَلَغَتْ سُهْمَانُنَا التي عَشَرَ بَعِيرًا، وَنَفَّلَنَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَعِيرًا بَعِيرًا»
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَالسَّلَبُ مَا عَلَى الْمَقْتُولِ مِنْ ثِيَابِهِ أَنَّ مَدَدِيَّا رَافَقَهُمْ فِي غَزْوَةِ مُؤْتَةَ ، وَأَنَّ رُومِيًّا كَانَ يَشُدُّ عَلَى الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَيُغْرِي بِهِمْ ، فَتَلَطَّفَ لَهُ ذَلِكَ الْمَدَدِيُّ ، فَأَقْبَل بِفَرَسِهِ ، وَسَيْفِهِ ، وَسَرْجِهِ ، وَلَجَامِهِ ، وَمِنْطَقَتِهِ ، وَسِلَاحِهِ ، كُلُّ ذَلِكَ مُذَهَبٌ بِالذَّهَبِ وَالْجُوْهَرِ ، إِلَى خَالِدِ بْنِ الْوَلِيدِ ، فَأَخَذَ مِنْهُ خَالِدٌ طَائِفَةً ، وَنَفَّلَهُ بَقِيَّتَهُ ، فَقُلْتُ: يَا خَالِدُ ، مَا هَذَا؟ أَمَا تَعْلَمُ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَفَّلَ الْقَاتِلَ السَّلَبَ كُلَّهُ ، قَالَ بَلَى ، وَلَكِنِّي اسْتَكْثَرْتُهُ
Book of Military Expeditions. And the salab is what is on the slain of his clothes, weapons, and mount. So the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'He told the truth, so give it to him.' So I sold the armor and bought a garden with it among Banu Salimah, and it was the first property I acquired in Islam. Wajh (1): The hadith proving that salab is what is on the slain of his clothes from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: 'The Messenger of Allah gave me as a nafal on the day of Badr the sword of Abu Jahl, whom he had killed.' Wajh (2): The hadith proving that salab is what is on the slain of his clothes from Abdullah: 'The Messenger of Allah sent us in a detachment, and our shares reached ten camels each, and he gave us one extra camel.' Wajh (3): The hadith proving that salab is what is on the slain of his clothes that a Muhajir accompanied them in the battle of Mu'tah, and a Roman was attacking the Muslims, so that Muhajir went to him and came back with his horse, sword, saddle, bridle, belt, and weapons, all gilded with gold and jewels, and brought them to Khalid ibn al-Walid. Khalid took some and gave him the rest. I said: O Khalid, what is this? Do you not know that the Messenger of Allah gave the killer the entire salab? He said: Yes, but I considered it too much.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Siyar defines the term 'salab' (spoils taken from a slain enemy combatant). According to the Hanafi school, salab includes the clothes, weapons, and mount of the slain. The passage then provides several hadith to support this definition. The first hadith (Bukhari) narrates the story of a Bedouin who asked the Prophet for the salab of an enemy he killed, and the Prophet granted it, illustrating that the salab is the right of the killer. The subsequent wajh points provide additional evidence: (1) Ibn Mas'ud received the sword of Abu Jahl as a nafal (extra grant), (2) a hadith about extra shares in a detachment, and (3) the incident at Mu'tah where Khalid ibn al-Walid gave the bulk of the salab to the killer despite its high value, confirming that the killer is entitled to the entire salab. This definition is foundational for the law of ghanimah in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
السَّلَب (al-salab): What is taken from a slain enemy, including clothes, weapons, and mount.
نَفَّل (naffala): To give something extra (nafal) beyond the regular share of ghanimah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Clothes, weapons, and mount of the slain
C) All property of the slain including gold and silver
D) Only the armor and sword

Key Takeaway
The salab is the killer's exclusive right, consisting of the slain's clothes, weapons, and mount, as established by Prophetic practice.
