Prohibition of Using Ghanimah Before Leaving Dar al-Harb
States the ruling and provides two proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that using ghanimah before the Imam divides it is haram, and explain the supporting evidence from the hadith of Mu'adh and the opinion of Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
Ghanimah is sacred trust until division — not even fodder may be consumed.

In this lesson, we examine a clear ruling from the matn of Al-Quduri regarding the sanctity of ghanimah (spoils of war). While in enemy territory, the mujahideen must refrain from using any part of the spoils for themselves or their animals until the Imam divides it. This ruling is based on prophetic practice and the understanding of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Recall the central prohibition: it is not permissible to eat or feed animals from ghanimah while still in Dar al-Harb.
The ruling applies to both food (طعام) and fodder (علف).
2
Identify the consequence
If someone has leftover fodder or food, they must return it to the common pool of ghanimah.
This emphasizes that no personal use is allowed without division.
3
Recall the primary proof
Learn the hadith of Mu'adh: At Khaybar, the Prophet divided a portion of the sheep and placed the rest back into the ghanimah, showing that unsanctioned use is prohibited.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud (2707).
4
Understand the secondary proof
The opinion of Ibn Abbas: He saw no harm in eating food in enemy land only after the Muslim owners enter the territory, implying that before exiting, it is not permissible.
This supports the idea that the prohibition lasts until division or exit.
5
Recognize the Hanafi strictness
Note that the Hanafi school holds the prohibition firmly, with no exception for necessity unless the Imam explicitly authorizes use.
Other schools may permit discretionary use with permission, but the Hanafi position is absolute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا خَرَجَ الْمُسْلِمُونَ مِنْ دَارِ الْحَرْبِ لَمْ يَجُزْ أَنْ يَعْلِفُوا مِنْ الْغَنِيمَةِ وَلَا يَأْكُلُوا مِنْهَا شَيْئًا وَمَنْ فَضَلَ مَعَهُ عَلَفٌ أَوْ طَعَامٌ رَدَّهُ إِلَى الْغَنِيمَةِ
د. وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا خَرَجَ الْمُسْلِمُونَ مِنْ دَارِ الْحَرْبِ فَقَالَ مُعَادٌ: «غَزَوْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم غَزْوَةَ خَيْبَرَ فَأَصَبْنَا فِيهَا غَنَمًا، فَقَسَمَ فِينَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم طَائِفَةً، وَجَعَلَ بَقِيَّتَهَا فِي الْمَغْنَمِ»
وجه : (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَإِذَا خَرَجَ الْمُسْلِمُونَ أَنَّ عَبْدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ عَبَّاسٍ لَمْ يَرَ بَأْسًا أَنْ يَأْكُلَ الطَّعَامَ فِي أَرْضِ الشِّرْكِ حَتَّى يَدْخُلَ أَهْلُهُ
And when the Muslims leave the abode of war, it is not permissible for them to feed (animals) from the spoils nor to eat anything from them. And whoever has leftover fodder or food with him, he must return it to the spoils. Proof (1): The hadith proving that when the Muslims leave the abode of war, Mu'adh said: 'We went on campaign with the Messenger of Allah in the expedition of Khaybar, and we acquired sheep there. The Messenger of Allah divided a portion among us and placed the rest in the booty.' Proof (2): The saying of the Companion proving that when the Muslims leave, that Abdullah ibn Abbas saw no harm in eating food in the land of polytheism until its owners enter (the territory).
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This ruling addresses the sanctity of ghanimah (spoils of war) while still in enemy territory. According to the Hanafi school, Muslims are not permitted to consume or use any part of the spoils for themselves or their animals until the spoils are properly divided by the Imam. Even the fodder for animals must not be used; if someone has leftover food or fodder with them, they must return it to the common pool. The proof is from the practice of Mu'adh ibn Jabal and the opinion of Ibn Abbas. The hadith from Mu'adh shows that the Prophet divided a portion of the sheep among the troops and placed the remainder in the ghanimah, indicating that nothing was consumed without permission. Ibn Abbas's opinion confirms that food taken in enemy land before distribution is permissible only after the owners (the Muslims) enter the territory, implying that before exiting, it is not permissible.

Key Terms
الْغَنِيمَة (al-ghanimah): Spoils of war taken from the enemy.
الْعَلَف (al-'alaf): Fodder for animals, which is included in the prohibition of using ghanimah before division.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It is permissible if necessary for survival
C) It is not permissible; leftover fodder must be returned to the ghanimah
D) It is permissible only for the cavalry

Key Takeaway
Using ghanimah before the Imam divides it is haram; even fodder must be returned to the common pool.

Horseman's Shares in Ghanimah: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
States Hanafi position and internal dispute on shares for horse and foot

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi internal dispute on horseman's shares in ghanimah, identify the proofs for each position, and explain why the mufta bihi follows the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A horseman's share: Abu Hanifa says 2, Sahibayn say 3 — later fatwa prefers the higher share.

After the khums is set aside, the remaining four-fifths of the spoils are divided among the warriors. But how many shares does a horseman deserve? The Hanafi school has an internal difference: Imam Abu Hanifa gives the horseman two shares (one for himself, one for his horse), while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, give three shares (one for him, two for his horse). This lesson examines the proofs of both sides, the reasoning behind the disagreement, and which view is relied upon in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and the internal dispute
Identify that all Hanafi imams agree that the khums is first set aside, then the rest is divided among the warriors. The dispute is over the exact number of shares for a horseman versus a foot soldier.
The foot soldier always receives one share according to all.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Examine the hadith of Khaybar where the Prophet (ﷺ) gave the horseman two shares and the foot soldier one. Explain how this supports Abu Hanifa's view of two shares for the horseman.
This hadith is recorded in Sunan Abi Dawud.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
Examine the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet (ﷺ) allotted three shares to a man and his horse: one for the man, two for the horse. Explain how this supports three shares for the horseman.
This hadith is also in Sunan Abi Dawud.
4
Understand the reconciliation and tarjih
Later Hanafi scholars reconcile the two hadiths by noting that the Ibn Umar hadith is more specific about the horse's share. They preferred the Sahibayn's view because it is more comprehensive and aligns with prophetic practice as recorded in multiple narrations.
The mufta bihi position is that of the Sahibayn (three shares).
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Calculate the difference: Under Abu Hanifa, a horseman receives 2/3 of a foot soldier's total share; under Sahibayn, 3/4. This affects the overall distribution of the spoils.
The greater the number of horsemen, the more significant the difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَقْسِمُ الْإِمَامُ الْغَنِيمَةَ فَيُخْرِجُ خُمُسَهَا وَيَقْسِمُ الْأَرْبَعَةَ أَخْمَاسِ بَيْنَ الْغَانِمِينَ
لِلْفَارِسِ سَهْمَانِ وَلِلرَّاجِلِ سَهْمٌ عِنْدَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لِلْفَارِسِ ثَلَاثُ أَسْهُم
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت لِلْفَارِسِ سَهْمَانِ وَلِلرَّاجِلِ سَهْمٍ قَالَ: «قُسِمَتْ خَيْبَرُ عَلَى أَهْلِ الحُدَيْبِيَّةِ، فَقَسَمَهَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَلَى ثَمَانِيَةَ عَشَرَ سَهْمًا، وَكَانَ الْخَيْسُ أَلْفًا وَخَمْسَ مِائَةٍ، فِيهِمْ ثَلَاثُ مِائَةِ فَارِسٍ، فَأَعْطَى الْفَارِسَ سَهْمَيْنِ، وَأَعْطَى الرَّاجِلَ سَهْمًا»
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت لِلْفَارِسِ سَهْمَانِ وَلِلرَّاجِلِ سَهْمٍ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، " أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَسْهَمَ لِرَجُلٍ وَلِفَرَسِهِ ثَلَاثَةَ أَسْهُمٍ: سَهْمًا لَهُ وَسَهْمَيْنِ لِفَرَسِهِ "
And the Imam divides the spoils: he extracts its khums (one-fifth) and divides the remaining four-fifths among the warriors. The horseman gets two shares and the foot soldier gets one share according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The horseman gets three shares. Proof (1): The hadith proving that the horseman gets two shares and the foot soldier one: 'Khaybar was distributed among the people of al-Hudaybiyyah, the Prophet divided it into eighteen shares. There were 1500 people, among them 300 horsemen. He gave the horseman two shares and the foot soldier one share.' Proof (2): The hadith from Ibn Umar: 'The Messenger of Allah allotted three shares to a man and his horse: one share for him and two for his horse.'
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage discusses the division of ghanimah after khums is set aside. The Hanafi school has an internal dispute regarding the number of shares for a horseman. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, a horseman receives two shares (one for himself and one for his horse) while a foot soldier receives one share. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) hold that a horseman receives three shares (one for himself and two for his horse). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in later Hanafi fatwa is that of the Sahibayn for horses that are actually used in battle. The proofs cited are the distribution of Khaybar (where the horseman got two shares) and the hadith of Ibn Umar (where the horseman got three shares). The apparent contradiction is resolved by noting that the Ibn Umar hadith specifies shares for the horse, while the Khaybar distribution might have included horses differently. The dispute affects the exact ratio: Abu Hanifa gives a horseman 2/3 of an infantryman's share, while the Sahibayn give 3/4. The majority of later Hanafi scholars prefer the Sahibayn's view.

Key Terms
سَهْم (sahm): A unit of share in the division of spoils.
الْفَارِس (al-faris): Horseman (cavalry) in the battlefield.
الرَّاجِل (al-rajil): Foot soldier (infantry) in the battle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, how many shares does a horseman receive in the division of ghanimah?
A) One share
B) Two shares
C) Three shares
D) Four shares

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the relied-upon position gives a horseman three shares (one for himself, two for his horse) due to the explicit hadith of Ibn Umar, while the foot soldier gets one share.

The Shares of Khums and Their Recipients after the Prophet
Rulings on khums distribution and proof texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the Prophet's share of khums and the relatives' share, and apply the evidence to explain why they fell or changed after his death.

Core Idea
The Prophet's share and safi fell with his death; the relatives' share is now only for the poor.

This lesson explains the distribution of khums (one-fifth of war booty) according to the Hanafi school. We focus on two key shares: the Prophet's personal share (sahm al-nabi) and the special selection (safi), both of which ended with his passing, and the share of the relatives (sahm dhawil-qurba), which now goes only to the needy among Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib. Understanding these rules is essential for correctly applying the khums system in Islamic jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shares
List the five shares of khums mentioned in Surah al-Anfal: 41, then focus on the Prophet's share, the relatives' share, and the safi. Note that the 'for Allah' portion is rhetorical.
The 'for Allah' opening is not a literal share.
2
Establish the Fall of the Prophet's Share
Analyze the hadith from Abu Hurairah (Sahih al-Bukhari no. 3096) that the Prophet's wealth is charity, not inherited. This proves that his personal share ended with his death.
The hadith is ahad but accepted by the Hanafi school.
3
Examine the Relatives' Share
Read the hadith from Jubayr ibn Mut'im showing that the Prophet allocated the relatives' share to Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib. After his death, the share becomes for the poor only, based on the practice of the caliphs.
Hanafis restrict relatives to these two clans.
4
Trace the Istidlal (Legal Reasoning)
Connect the hadith proofs to the rulings: the Prophet's share fell because his wealth is sadaqah; the relatives' share is conditioned on need after his death. The caliphs spent these two shares on jihad equipment.
This is based on ijma of the Companions.
5
Contrast with Other Schools
Briefly note that Shafi'is hold the Prophet's share continues for public welfare, and some schools include all Quraysh in the relatives' share. Hanafis rely on the specific hadith and practice of the early caliphs.
This ikhtilaf affects actual distribution.

ود وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيَدْخُلُ فُقَرَاءُ ذَوِي الْقُرْبَى فِيهِمْ \ سَمِعْتُ عَلِيًّا، يَقُولُ: «وَلَّاتِي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم خَمُسَ الْخُمُسِ»، فَوَضَعْتُهُ مَوَاضِعَهُ حَيَاةَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَحَيَاةَ أَبِي بَكْرٍ، وَحَيَاةَ عُمَرَ، فَأَتِي بِمَالٍ فَدَعَانِي فَقَالَ: خُذْهُ، فَقُلْتُ لا أريدُهُ، قَالَ: خُذْهُ فَأَنْتُمْ أَحَقُّ بِهِ، قُلْتُ: قَدِ اسْتَغْنَيْنَا عَنْهُ فَجَعَلَهُ فِي بَيْتِ الْمَالِ" (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي بَيَانِ مَوَاضِعِ قَسْمِ الْخُمُسِ، وَسَهْمِ ذِي الْقُرْبَى، غير (2983)

الوجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَسَهُمُ النَّبِيِّ - صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَنْ عَامِرِ الشَّعْبِيِّ، قَالَ: «كَانَ للنَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم سَهُمْ يُدْعَى الصَّفِيَّ، إِنْ شَاءَ عَبْدًا، وَإِنْ شَاءَ أَمَةً، وَإِنْ شَاءَ فَرَسًا يَخْتَارُهُ قَبْلَ الْخُمُسِ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي سَهْمِ الصَّفِيِّ،نمبر 2991)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَسَهْمُ ذَوِي الْقُرْبَى كَانُوا يَسْتَحِقُونَهُ فِي زَمَنِ النَّبِيَا أَخْبَرَنِي جُبَيْرُ بْنُ مُطْعِمٍ، قَالَ: لَمَّا كَانَ يَوْمُ خَيْبَرَ وَضَعَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم سَهْمَ ذِي الْقُرْبَى فِي بَنِي هَاشِمٍ، وَبَنِي الْمُطَّلِبِ، وَتَرَكَ بَنِي نَوْفَلِ، وَبَنِي عَبْدِ شَمْسٍ فَانْطَلَقْتُ أَنَا وَعُثْمَانُ بْنُ عَفَّانَ حَتَّى أَتَيْنَا النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم، فَقُلْنَا: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، هَؤُلَاءِ بَنُو هَاشِمٍ لَا تُنْكِرُ فَضْلَهُمْ لِلْمَوْضِعِ الَّذِي وَضَعَكَ اللَّهُ مِنْهُمْ، فَمَا بَالُ إخْوَانِنَا بَنِي الْمُطَّلِبِ أَعْطَيْتَهُمْ وَتَرَكْتَنَا وَقَرَابَتُنَا وَاحِدَةٌ، فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ : «إِنَّا وَبَنُو الْمُطَّلِبِ لا نَفْتَرِقُ فِي جَاهِلِيَّةِ، وَلا إِسْلَام وَإِنَّمَا نَحْنُ وَهُمْ شَيْءٌ وَاحِدٌ» وَشَبَّكَ بَيْنَ أَصَابِعِهِ (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي بَيَانِ مَوَاضِعِ قَسْمِ الْخُمُسِ، وَسَهْمِ ذِي الْقُرْبَ، نمبر 2980) وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَسَهْمُ ذَوِي الْقُرْبَى كَانُوا يَسْتَحِقُونَهُ فِي زَمَنِ النَّبِيِّ فَاجْتَمَعَ رَأْيُهُمْ عَلَى أَنْ يَجْعَلُوا هَذَيْنِ السَّهْمَيْنِ فِي الخَيْلِ وَالْعُدَّةَ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ، فَكَانَا عَلَى ذَلِكَ فِي خِلَافَةِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ وَعُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما (المستدرك علي الصحيحين للحاكم، والأصل من كتاب الله عز وجل، نمبر 2585)
Book of Military Expeditions. 59: The poor among the relatives enter among them and are given precedence, and nothing is given to their rich. 60: As for what Allah the Exalted mentioned for Himself in His Book of the khums, it is only to open the speech, seeking blessing by His name. But the share of the Prophet, peace be upon him, fell with his death just as the safi (special selection) fell. And the share of the relatives: they were entitled to it in the time of the Prophet, peace be upon him, by support, and after him by poverty. (From al-Hakim, and the original from the Book of Allah, no. 2585). Indication (2): The hadith for establishing that the khums is divided into three shares, from Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'My heirs do not share a dinar; what I leave after the maintenance of my wives and the provision of my worker is charity.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on maintenance of the Prophet's wives after his death, no. 3096). And indication (1): The hadith for establishing 'And the poor among the relatives enter among them', I heard Ali say: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, entrusted me with the khums of the khums, so I placed it in its proper places during the lifetime of the Messenger of Allah, the lifetime of Abu Bakr, and the lifetime of Umar. Then wealth was brought to me, so he called me and said: Take it. I said: I do not want it. He said: Take it, for you are more entitled to it. I said: We have no need of it. So he placed it in the treasury.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on explaining the places of dividing the khums and the share of the relatives, no. 2983). Indication (1): The hadith for establishing 'As for what Allah mentioned for Himself', I asked al-Hasan ibn Muhammad about the saying of Allah the Blessed and Exalted {And know that whatever you take as spoils, then for Allah is one-fifth and for the Messenger} [al-Anfal: 41], the verse. He said: 'This is the key to the speech of Allah the Exalted regarding this world and the Hereafter.' (al-Mustadrak of al-Hakim, and the original from the Book of Allah, no. 2585). The indication (a): The hadith for establishing 'and the share of the Prophet, peace be upon him', from 'Amir al-Sha'bi, he said: 'The Prophet, peace be upon him, had a share called the safi; if he wished, a slave, or if he wished, a slave girl, or if he wished, a horse, he would choose it before the khums.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on the share of the safi, no. 2991). Indication (1): The hadith for establishing 'and the share of the relatives used to be entitled in the time of the Prophet', Jubayr ibn Mut'im informed me: On the day of Khaybar, the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, placed the share of the relatives among Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib, and left out Banu Nawfal and Banu 'Abd Shams. So I and 'Uthman ibn 'Affan went until we came to the Prophet, peace be upon him, and said: O Messenger of Allah, these are Banu Hashim – we do not deny their virtue for the position in which Allah placed you among them, but what about our brothers Banu al-Muttalib? You gave them and left us, while our relationship is one. The Messenger of Allah said: 'We and Banu al-Muttalib do not separate in Jahiliyyah or Islam; indeed, we and they are one thing,' and he interlaced his fingers. (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on explaining the places of dividing the khums and the share of the relatives, no. 2980). Indication (2): The hadith for establishing 'and the share of the relatives used to be entitled in the time of the Prophet', then they (the Companions) collectively agreed to place these two shares (the Prophet's and the relatives') in horses and equipment for the sake of Allah, and they remained thus during the caliphate of Abu Bakr and 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them. (al-Mustadrak of al-Hakim, and the original from the Book of Allah, no. 2585).
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage clarifies the distribution of khums (one-fifth of war booty) according to the Hanafi school. It begins by stating that the poor among the Prophet's relatives (Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib) are given precedence in the share allocated to them, and the rich among them receive nothing. This is based on the principle that after the Prophet's death, the share for relatives is given only to the needy among them. The text then explains that the phrase 'for Allah' in the verse is not a literal share but an opening formula seeking blessing. The Prophet's personal share (sahm al-nabi) and the special selection (safi) fell with his death, as the Prophet's wealth is charity for the ummah, not inherited. The relatives' share (sahm dhawil-qurba) was originally given for their support of the Prophet during his lifetime; after his death, it is given only to the poor among them. The hadith proofs provided support these rules: a hadith from Abu Hurairah establishes that the Prophet's wealth is charity; a hadith from Ali shows that the khums was distributed to the relatives during the caliphates of Abu Bakr and Umar; a hadith from al-Hasan ibn Muhammad explains the 'for Allah' phrase as an opening; a hadith from al-Sha'bi describes the safi; and a hadith from Jubayr ibn Mut'im shows that the Prophet allocated the relatives' share to Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib exclusively. Finally, a narration indicates that after the Prophet, the companions agreed to spend the two shares (Prophet's and relatives') on horses and weapons for jihad, effectively suspending them for future generations, which became the practice under Abu Bakr and Umar.

Key Terms
الخمس (al-khumus): One-fifth of war booty taken from the enemy, to be distributed among the five categories mentioned in Surah al-Anfal: 41.
الصفي (al-safi): A special selection the Prophet could take from the booty before division, such as a slave, horse, or sword.
ذو القربى (dhawu al-qurba): The relatives of the Prophet, specifically Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib, who are entitled to a share of khums.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school as presented, what happened to the Prophet's share (sahm al-nabi) and the safi after his death?
A) They were distributed to the poor among the relatives.
B) They were allocated to horses and equipment for jihad.
C) They fell and are no longer distributed; the Prophet's wealth is charity.
D) They continued to be given to the caliphs.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's share of khums and the safi fell with his death; the relatives' share is now only for the poor among Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules

Khums on Unauthorized Raids: The Man'ah Distinction
Rulings on khums for unauthorized entry into Dar al-Harb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khums when Muslims enter Dar al-Harb without the Imam's permission, distinguishing between individuals and a group with defensive strength (man'ah).

Core Idea
A group with defensive strength owes khums even without permission; individuals do not.

This passage presents two rulings from the Hanafi school on the obligation of khums (the one-fifth tax) when Muslims raid enemy territory without the Imam's authorization. The key distinction is the size and strength of the raiding party. Individuals or very small groups are not subject to khums, but a group that constitutes a defensive force (man'ah) must pay khums on any booty taken. The proofs come from two hadiths: one warning against treachery and another from the Prophet's practice of granting extra shares to raiding parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage describes two cases: one or two individuals entering Dar al-Harb, and a group that has man'ah (defensive strength) entering.
Man'ah means a force capable of defending itself and engaging militarily.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
For one or two individuals: the booty is not subject to khums. For a group with man'ah: khums is wajib (obligatory) on the booty.
3
Locate the dalil for each ruling
The ruling for individuals is supported by a hadith condemning treachery (ghadr), implying sin but no fiscal obligation. The ruling for the group is supported by a hadith where the Prophet gave extra shares (nafal) to raiding parties and stated 'the khums on that is obligatory'.
The hadith for the group (Sunan Abi Dawud no. 2746) explicitly states 'wa al-khumusu fi dhalika wajib kulluhu'.
4
Understand the reasoning for the distinction
A group with man'ah resembles a formal military expedition, so the full khums rules apply. Individuals are not seen as a military force, so their gains are personal and not subject to khums.
The distinction is practical, not moral; even unauthorized groups with capacity must pay khums.
5
Recognize the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school holds that khums is wajib only for groups with man'ah. The proof is the hadith on nafal and the logic of military capacity.
This is the mufta bihi (operative ruling) as per zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
د وجه : (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا دَخَلَ وَاحِدٌ أَوْ اثْنَانِ دَارَ الْحَرْبِ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ دِينَارٍ، عَن ابْنِ عُمَرَ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: " إِنَّ الْغَادِرَ يُنْصَبُ لَهُ لِوَاءٌ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ فَيُقَالُ: هَذِهِ غَدْرَةُ فُلَانِ بْن فُلَانِ" سنن ابوداود ، بَابٌ فِي الْوَفَاءِ بِالْعَهْدِ غمبر (2756)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ دَخَلَ جَمَاعَةٌ هُمْ مَنْعَةٌ فَأَخَذُوا شَيْئًا خُمِسَ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ، «أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَدْ كَانَ يُنَفِّلُ بَعْضَ مَنْ يَبْعَثُ مِنَ السَّرَايَا لِأَنْفُسِهِمْ خَاصَّةَ النَّفَلِ سِوَى قَسْمِ عَامَّةِ الْجَيْشِ، وَالْخُمُسُ فِي ذَلِكَ وَاجِبٌ كُلُّهُ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي نَفْلِ السَّرِيَّةِ تَخْرُجُ مِنَ الْعَسْكَرِ، نمبر 2746)
Proof indication (a): The hadith for establishing 'When one or two enter Dar al-Harb...' from Abdullah ibn Dinar, from Ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'The treacherous one will have a banner set up for him on the Day of Resurrection, and it will be said: This is the treachery of so-and-so.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on fulfilling the covenant, no. 2756). Indication (1): The hadith for establishing 'And if a group who are a defense force enter and take something, it is subject to khums.' From Abdullah ibn Umar: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, used to give extra (nafal) to some of those he sent as raiding parties, to themselves exclusively, apart from the general division of the army, and the khums on that is obligatory entirely.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on the nafal of a raiding party that goes out from the army, no. 2746).
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings from the Hanafi school regarding Muslims who enter enemy territory (Dar al-Harb) without the Imam's permission. First: if one or two individuals enter as raiders (mugheerin) and take booty, that booty is not subject to khums (one-fifth tax). The proof cited is a hadith condemning treachery (ghadr), implying that such unauthorized action is sinful but not subject to the same fiscal rules as legitimate warfare. Second: if a group of Muslims constitutes a 'man'ah' (a defensive force with strength) and takes booty, even without the Imam's permission, the khums must be taken from it. The proof is a hadith about the Prophet giving additional shares (nafal) to special raiding parties, and the khums is wajib (obligatory) on all such acquisitions. The distinction is based on the group's capacity: a small number of individuals are not considered a formal military expedition, so their gains are treated as personal acquisitions without khums, while a substantial group is akin to an army, and thus the full khums rules apply. The hadith on treachery serves to warn against unauthorized actions, but the group's case is treated differently due to their collective strength and the precedent of the Prophet's practice.

Key Terms
منعة (man'a): A group of people who collectively have defensive strength; a force that can protect itself and engage in military action.
الغادر (al-ghadir): The one who betrays a covenant or trust; here referring to Muslims who enter enemy territory without permission and break the implied peace treaty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when do one or two Muslims who enter Dar al-Harb without the Imam's permission have to pay khums on the booty they take?
A) Always, because all booty is subject to khums.
B) Only if they are rich.
C) Never, because they are not a formal military expedition.
D) Only if they confess to the Imam.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between individuals and a defensive force regarding khums on booty taken without Imam's permission.

Muslim Trader Entering Dar al-Harb: Prohibited Ownership and Charity
Ruling on a Muslim trader in enemy territory who takes property by treachery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on property taken by a Muslim trader in Dar al-Harb through treachery and explain why it must be given in charity.

Core Idea
A Muslim trader who takes enemy property by treachery incurs prohibited ownership and must give it in charity.

In this lesson, we examine a specific scenario from Hanafi fiqh of siyar: a Muslim enters enemy territory as a trader and takes property by breaking the implicit covenant of safety. The ruling is nuanced: the property is acquired physically but is not lawful for him to keep. We will explore the proof from the Sunnah and understand the concept of "milk mahdhur" (prohibited ownership).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the legal classification (hukm) is. The act is a Muslim trader taking enemy property by treachery in Dar al-Harb. The ruling is that it is haram, and the property is 'milkan mahdhuran' (prohibited ownership) – he must give it in charity.
The trader enters under an implicit aman (covenant of safety), so his treachery violates that trust.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
Identify the proof cited by the Hanafi school. The evidence is the hadith from Sulaiman ibn Buraidah, with the command 'la taghduru' (do not be treacherous).
This hadith is found in Sahih Muslim (no. 1731) and Sunan Abi Dawud (no. 2613).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof yields the ruling)
Explain how the specific phrase in the dalil leads to the ruling. The prohibition of treachery ('la taghduru') includes the trader who acts treacherously by taking property, as he enjoys an implicit aman. Therefore, such taking is haraam, and the property becomes prohibited ownership.
The command is general (amm) and applies to all forms of treachery, including breach of trust.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly difference)
Acknowledge that some scholars may consider such acquisition lawful if no formal covenant exists, but the Hanafi school upholds the prohibition due to the implicit aman.
The cross-madhhab status is 'mukhtalaf fih', meaning it is a point of disagreement.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih (preferred position)
Identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position. The established view from Zahir al-Riwayah is that the trader must give the taken property in charity to the poor.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲۵وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الْمُسْلِمُ دَارَ الْحَرْبِ تَاجِرًا \ عَنْ سليمان ابْنِ بُرَيْدَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ. قَالَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ ، إِذَا أَمَّرَ أمير على جيش... قَاتِلُوا مَنْ كَفَرَ بِاللَّهِ اغْرُوا وَلَا تَغْلُوا وَلَا تَغْدِرُوا وَلَا تَقْتُلُوا وَلَا تَقْتُلُوا وَلِيدًا، مسلم شريف، باب تأمير الإمام الأمراء على البعوث، ووصية إِيَّاهُمْ بِآدَابِ الْغَزْوِ وَغَيْرِهَا ، نمبر 1731 / سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي دُعَاءِ الْمُشْرِكِينَ، نمبر 2613)
Indication (a): The hadith for establishing 'When a Muslim enters Dar al-Harb as a trader...' from Sulaiman ibn Buraidah, from his father: The Messenger of Allah said: 'When an amir appoints a commander over an army... fight those who disbelieve in Allah, incite them, and do not be excessive, do not be treacherous, do not mutilate, and do not kill children.' (Muslim, chapter on the Imam appointing commanders over expeditions and advising them on the etiquette of warfare, no. 1731 / Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on calling the polytheists, no. 2613).
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation of a Muslim who enters enemy territory (Dar al-Harb) as a trader. The Hanafi ruling is clear: it is not permissible (la yahillu) for him to target any of the enemy's property or blood. If he betrays them (ghadara), takes something, and exits with it, he acquires it as 'milkan mahdhuran' (prohibited ownership). He is then ordered to give it in charity (yatassadaqa bihi). This means the property is not legally his; he must dispose of it in charity to Allah. The proof cited is the hadith from Sulaiman ibn Buraidah, which contains the command 'la taghduru' (do not be treacherous). This prohibition applies even to a trader, as he is under an implicit covenant of safety (aman) when entering for trade. Therefore, taking anything violates that trust and incurs a moral and legal obligation to give it away in charity, rather than keeping it as lawful booty.

Key Terms
ملك محظور (milk mahdhur): Ownership that is legally prohibited; the owner has physical possession but no legal right to use the property, and must dispose of it in charity.
غدر (ghadr): Treachery, breaking a covenant or trust; here specifically violating the safety granted to a trader.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the legal status of property taken by a Muslim trader from enemies in Dar al-Harb by treachery?
A) It becomes lawful booty subject to khums.
B) It is prohibited ownership and must be given in charity.
C) It is halal if the trader fought them.
D) It becomes the trader's personal property.

Key Takeaway
A Muslim trader who violates the implicit aman in Dar al-Harb by taking enemy property must give it in charity; it is prohibited ownership, not lawful booty.

Imam's Reward for Killing a Specific Enemy
Usul principle: Imam's reward for killing a specific enemy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle of the Imam's reward (in'aam) for killing a specific enemy and identify the condition that the reward must be set with proper regulation (ba zabita).

Core Idea
The Imam may lawfully incentivize killing a specific enemy, distinct from general booty.

In the rules of jihad (siyar), the Imam has authority to motivate fighters by offering rewards for specific objectives. This short usul principle clarifies that such rewards are valid when properly established, and the killer becomes entitled to the promised reward. Understanding this principle helps distinguish between general distribution of booty and targeted incentives in Islamic military law.

Guided Path
1
State the principle
Read the usul principle: the Imam may set a reward (in'aam) for killing a specific enemy. Memorize the wording.
The principle is short but foundational for understanding state incentives in jihad.
2
Identify the condition
Note that the reward must be set 'ba zabita' – with proper regulation meaning clear rules and conditions established by the Imam.
Without proper regulation, the entitlement may not be valid.
3
Determine the entitlement
If the conditions are met (the Imam sets the reward with rules, and the killer kills that specific enemy), the killer is entitled to the reward.
Entitlement is contingent on both the Imam's declaration and the killer's action.
4
Distinguish from booty
This reward is separate from the general distribution of ghanimah (spoils). The Imam can offer extra incentives beyond the usual shares.
Booty is divided according to fixed rules; in'aam is an additional, conditional prize.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول: اگر امام با ضابطہ کسی خاص دشمن کے قتل کرنے پر انعام مقرر کرے تو ایسے مقتول پر انعام کا مستحق ہو گا
Principle: If the Imam, with rules, sets a reward for killing a specific enemy, then he (the killer) will be entitled to the reward for that killed person.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This is a separate usul (principle) written in Urdu. It states that if the Imam, with proper regulation (ba zabita), designates a reward (in'am) for killing a particular enemy, then the Muslim who kills that enemy becomes entitled to that reward. This principle is part of the rules of jihad, allowing the Imam to incentivize targeting high-value enemies. The killer must fulfill the conditions set by the Imam to claim the reward. This principle is consistent with the practice of the Prophet, who sometimes gave extra shares (nafal) for specific objectives.

Key Terms
انعام (in'aam): A reward or prize set by the Imam for achieving a specific military objective, such as killing a particular enemy.
با ضابطہ (ba zabita): With proper regulation or rules; the condition that the Imam's reward must be established through clear procedures and conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the usul principle, what condition must be fulfilled for a killer to be entitled to a reward set by the Imam?
A) The Imam must have set the reward with proper rules.
B) The killer must be a close relative of the Imam.
C) The enemy must be a high-ranking officer.
D) The killer must have prior permission.

Key Takeaway
The Imam's reward (in'aam) for killing a specific enemy is a valid incentive in jihad when properly regulated, entitling the killer to the promised reward.

Khums on Spoils from Unauthorized Raids
Ruling on khums for unauthorized raiders

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for khums on spoils taken by raiders entering Dar al-Harb without the Imam's permission, and distinguish between one/two raiders and a group with man'ah.

Core Idea
Khums is due only when the raiding party is a military force (man'ah).

This lesson addresses a key distinction in Hanafi law of spoils: whether khums (the one-fifth tax) applies to goods taken by Muslims who raid enemy territory without the caliph's authorization. The ruling turns on the size and capability of the raiding party. The matn of Al-Quduri presents a clear, memorizable rule that differentiates between a lone or duo scout and a band that constitutes a military force.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Default Ruling
The act is entering Dar al-Harb to raid (igharah) and taking property. The default ruling is that spoils are subject to khums, but here the key variable is authorization and party size.
The text assumes the raid is done without the Imam's permission – a recurring issue in frontier warfare.
2
Distinguish the Two Scenarios
The text gives two cases: (a) one or two individuals, and (b) a group that has man'ah (strength to resist). For the first, no khums; for the second, khums is wajib.
Man'ah means the group is capable of defending itself and achieving military objectives, i.e., it is a significant force.
3
Understand the Legal Basis
A small party's action is akin to individual initiative and does not represent the Muslim polity; thus, they own all they take. A group with man'ah resembles an official expedition, so the spoils are treated as ghanimah proper, requiring khums.
This ruling is specific to Hanafi fiqh; some other scholars require khums on all spoils regardless.
4
Apply the Ruling
In practice, if a handful of Muslims cross into enemy land to retrieve stolen goods, no khums. But if a dozen armed fighters launch a raid, khums is due even if the caliph did not authorize it.
The ruling applies only to movable property (spoils), not to land or captives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا دَخَلَ وَاحِدٌ أَوْ اثْنَانِ دَارَ الْحَرْبِ مُغِيرِينَ بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِ الْإِمَامِ فَأَخَذُوا شَيْئًا لَمْ يُخَمَّسْ وَإِنْ دَخَلَ جَمَاعَةٌ هُمْ مَنْعَةٌ فَأَخَذُوا شَيْئًا خَمَسَ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَأْذَنْ لَهُمُ الْإِمَامُ
And when one or two enter Dar al-Harb as raiders without the Imam's permission and take something, it is not subject to khums. And if a group enters who are a force (capable of resistance) and they take something, it is subject to khums even if the Imam did not permit them.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of Al-Quduri on the law of spoils (ghanimah). The ruling distinguishes between a small raiding party (one or two individuals) and a group that constitutes a military force (man'ah). For the small party, no khums (one-fifth) is taken from the spoils; they own it entirely. For the group, khums must be paid regardless of whether the Imam authorized the raid. The distinction is based on the likelihood of success and the potential for significant gain: a small group's action is akin to individual initiative, while a group's raid resembles an official expedition and thus requires the khums to be set aside for the public treasury and the shares of the Prophet's family.

Key Terms
خمس (khums): The one-fifth tax on spoils of war, distributed to the public treasury and the Prophet's family.
منعة (man'ah): A group that is capable of defending itself and achieving military strength.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, which of the following requires khums on spoils taken without imam's permission?
A) One Muslim raider
B) Two Muslim raiders
C) A group of raiders with man'ah
D) A group of raiders without man'ah

Key Takeaway
Khums is due on spoils taken without imam's permission only when the raiding party constitutes a military force (man'ah).

Muslim trader in dar al-harb: prohibited ownership
Ruling on a Muslim trader entering dar al-harb: cannot take enemy property; if he does, it is prohibited ownership.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a Muslim trader entering dar al-harb and explain the consequence of milk mahzur.

Core Idea
A Muslim trader under aman cannot take enemy property; taking results in prohibited ownership.

When a Muslim enters enemy territory as a trader, he enjoys an implied safe conduct (aman) that prohibits him from taking any property or harming any person. This lesson explains the ruling if he betrays that trust and takes something: he obtains it but only as prohibited ownership, and must give it in charity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its prohibition
Recognize that the trader is under aman, so taking property or harming persons is haram.
Aman is implicit for traders; they are not combatants.
2
Understand the consequence of violation
If he treacherously takes something, he owns it but as milk mahzur (prohibited ownership).
Milk mahzur means he is legally the owner but cannot use or keep it.
3
Apply the required remedy
He must give the item in charity; it does not become his lawful property.
Charity purifies the ownership but does not erase the sin of ghadr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الْمُسْلِمُ دَارَ الْحَرْبِ تَاجِرًا فَلَا يَحِلُّ لَهُ أَنْ يَتَعَرَّضَ لِشَيْءٍ مِنْ أَمْوَالِهِمْ وَلَا مِنْ دِمَائِهِمْ وَإِنْ غَدَرَ بِهِمْ وَأَخَذَ شَيْئًا وَخَرَجَ بِهِ مَلَكَهُ مِلْكًا مَحْظُورًا وَيُؤْمَرُ أَنْ يَتَصَدَّقَ اللهُ بِهِ
And when a Muslim enters Dar al-Harb as a trader, it is not permissible for him to interfere with any of their property nor their lives. And if he betrays them and takes something and exits with it, he owns it as prohibited ownership, and he is commanded to give it in charity in the way of Allah.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This ruling statement prohibits a Muslim who enters enemy territory as a trader from taking any property or harming any person, as he is under an implied aman (safe conduct) as a merchant. If he treacherously takes something, he obtains it but with a prohibited ownership (milk mahzur). The remedy is that he must give it in charity; he does not keep it. This ruling ensures the integrity of trade and trust, and distinguishes between legitimate spoils of war and betrayal.

Key Terms
ملك محظور (milk mahzur): Prohibited ownership: legally owning something but it is not permissible to use or keep; must be disposed of by charity.
غدر (ghadr): Betrayal or breach of trust; in this context, breaking the implied aman of being a trader.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a Muslim trader do if he treacherously takes property from dar al-harb?
A) Keep it as spoils
B) Give khums and keep the rest
C) Give it in charity
D) Return it to the enemy

Key Takeaway
A Muslim trader in dar al-harb is bound by an implied aman; taking property is haram and results in milk mahzur which must be given in charity.

The Harbi with Aman: Maximum One Year Stay and Becoming Dhimmi
Ruling on a harbi entering with aman: maximum stay one year

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a harbi who stays in Muslim lands with aman for one year and identify the consequence of staying beyond that period.

Core Idea
A harbi with aman cannot stay beyond one year; after that, he must become a dhimmi and pay jizya.

This lesson examines a clear-cut ruling from the matn of Al-Quduri regarding the status of a non-Muslim enemy (harbi) who enters Muslim territory under temporary safe conduct (aman). The passage sets a strict time limit — one year — after which the harbi must either leave or transition to permanent dhimmi status with the obligation of jizya. Understanding this rule clarifies the boundary between temporary protection and permanent residence in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person and the grant
Recognize that the ruling applies to a harbi (enemy alien) who has been given aman (safe conduct) to enter Muslim lands.
Aman can be granted by any adult Muslim, not only the Imam.
2
Recognize the time limit
The text states he is not allowed to reside for a full year. This means his stay is limited to less than one year.
The year is calculated from the date of entry.
3
Understand the Imam's warning
The Imam informs the harbi before the year ends that staying a complete year will trigger jizya and dhimmi status.
This serves as a clear notice so the harbi can make an informed choice.
4
Know the consequence of staying a full year
If he stays one year, jizya is collected from him, and he becomes a dhimmi (protected non-Muslim resident).
Dhimmi status is permanent; he cannot revert to being a harbi.
5
Note the prohibition on return
After becoming a dhimmi, he is not allowed to return to dar al-harb (enemy territory).
This ensures commitment to the Muslim state.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الْحَرْبِيُّ إِلَيْنَا بِأَمَانٍ لَمْ يُمَكِّنْ أَنْ يُقِيمَ فِي دَارِنَا سَنَةً وَيَقُولُ لَهُ الْإِمَامُ إِذَا أَقَمْت تَمَامَ السَّنَةِ وَضَعْت عَلَيْكَ الْجُزْيَةَ فَإِنْ أَقَامَ سَنَةً أُخِذَتْ مِنْهُ الْجُزْيَةُ وَصَارَ ذِمِّيَّا وَلَمْ يُتْرَكُ أَنْ يَرْجِعَ إِلَى دَارِ الحزب
And when a harbi enters our land with aman (safe conduct), he is not allowed to reside in our land for a year. And the Imam says to him: 'If you stay for a complete year, I will impose the jizya upon you.' And if he stays a year, the jizya is taken from him, and he becomes a dhimmi, and he is not allowed to return to the abode of war.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This ruling statement addresses the status of a harbi (enemy alien) who enters Muslim territory with aman (temporary safe conduct). He may not reside beyond one year. Before the year ends, the Imam informs him that staying a full year will subject him to jizya (poll tax) and permanent dhimmi status. If he stays, jizya is collected and he becomes a protected non-Muslim resident; he cannot return to enemy territory. This rule prevents perpetual temporary residence and ensures clarity of status.

Key Terms
حربي (harbi): A person from dar al-harb (enemy territory) who is not a Muslim or a dhimmi.
أمان (aman): Safe conduct granted to a harbi, temporary protection in Muslim lands.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim permanently residing in Muslim lands under protection, paying jizya.
جزية (jizya): Poll tax imposed on adult free male non-Muslims in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, what happens if a harbi with aman stays in Muslim territory for a full year?
A) He must leave immediately and cannot return
B) He becomes a dhimmi and pays jizya, and cannot return to dar al-harb
C) He may renew his aman for another year
D) He is given an option to convert to Islam or leave

Key Takeaway
A harbi who enters with aman cannot stay a full year; staying a year imposes jizya and dhimmi status, with no option to return to dar al-harb.

Ruling on Harbi Entering Dar al-Islam with Aman
Al-Quduri's ruling on harbi with aman and its proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a harbi with aman staying in Dar al-Islam and explain the proofs from Quran, Hadith, and Sahabi practice.

Core Idea
A harbi with aman cannot stay a full year; if he does, he becomes a dhimmi and must pay jizyah.

This lesson examines Al-Quduri's ruling on a harbi (non-Muslim from enemy territory) who enters Muslim lands with safe conduct (aman). The Hanafi school insists that such a person cannot be allowed to stay for a full year without accepting dhimmi status and paying jizyah. We will study the primary ruling and the four proofs (wujuh) that support it, including a Quranic verse, a prophetic hadith, and two practices of Caliph Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a harbi entering Dar al-Islam with aman and staying for a full year. The ruling is that the Imam must restrict the stay; if the year is completed, jizyah is taken and he becomes a dhimmi.
The obligation falls on the Imam to enforce this.
2
Locate the first proof: Quranic verse
Verse 9:28 declares polytheists as unclean and prohibits them from approaching the Sacred Mosque after that year. The Hanafi school uses qiyas to extend this restriction to the entire Dar al-Islam for extended stays.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalala for this ruling.
3
Locate the second proof: Hadith
The hadith of Ibn Abbas records the Prophet's order to expel polytheists from the Arabian Peninsula. This indicates that permanent residence of non-Muslims in Muslim lands is not permitted.
This is a specific command for the Arabian Peninsula, but Hanafis apply by analogy.
4
Locate the third and fourth proofs: Sahabi practices
Umar ibn al-Khattab limited dhimmis in Madinah to a three-day stay and imposed a tax (ushr) on harbis staying six months or a year. These show the precedent for restricting stay and imposing jizyah.
These are qawl al-sahabi, considered a proof in Hanafi usul.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The proofs collectively support the ruling that aman does not grant permanent residence. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi and is based on Zahir al-Riwayah.
Some other schools may allow indefinite stay, but the Hanafi school maintains the restriction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ السِّير
وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الْحَرْبِيُّ إِلَيْنَا بِأَمَانٍ لَمْ يُمَكِّنْ أَنْ يُقِيمَ فِي دَارِنَا سَنَةً وَيَقُولُ لَهُ الْإِمَامُ إِذَا أَقَمْتَ تَمَامَ السَّنَةِ وَضَعْتُ عَلَيْكَ الْجُزْيَةَ فَإِنْ أَقَامَ سَنَةً أُخِذَتْ مِنْهُ الْجُزْيَةُ وَصَارَ ذِمِّيًّا وَلَمْ يُتْرَكْ أَنْ يَرْجِعَ إِلَى دَارِ الْحَرْبِ
الوجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الْحَرْبِيُّ إِلَيْنَا بِأَمَانٍ يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِنَّمَا الْمُشْرِكُونَ نَجَسٌ فَلَا يَقْرَبُوا الْمَسْجِدَ الْحَرَامَ بَعْدَ عَامِهِمْ هَذَا (سورة التوبة، 9 آيت، نمبر 28)
وجه: (2) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الْحَرْبِيُّ إِلَيْنَا بِأَمَانٍ سَمِعَ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ رضي الله عنهما يَقُولُ: يَوْمُ الْخَمِيسِ وَمَا يَوْمُ الْخَمِيسِ، ثُمَّ بَكَى حَتَّى بَكَتْ دُمُوعُهُ الْحَصَى، قُلْتُ: يَا أَبَا عَبَّاسٍ: مَا يَوْمُ الْخَمِيسِ؟ ..... فَأَمَرَهُمْ بِثَلَاثٍ، قَالَ: أَخْرِجُوا الْمُشْرِكِينَ مِنْ جَزِيرَةِ الْعَرَبِ (بخاري شريف، بَابُ إِخْرَاجِ الْيَهُودِ مِنْ جَزِيرَةِ الْعَرَبِ، نمبر 3168)
وجه: (3) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الْحَرْبِيُّ إِلَيْنَا بِأَمَانٍ أَنْ عُمَرَ بْنَ الْخَطَّابِ ضَرَبَ لِلْيَهُودِ وَالنَّصَارَى وَالْمَجُوسَ بِالْمَدِينَةِ إِقَامَةَ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ يَتَسَوَّقُونَ بِمَا وَيَقْضُونَ حَوَائِجَهُمْ، وَلَا يُقِيمُ أَحَدٌ مِنْهُمْ فَوْقَ ثَلَاثِ لَيَالٍ (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ الذِّمِّي يَمُرُّ بِالْحِجَازِ مَارًّا لَا يُقِيمُ بِبَلَدٍ مِنْهَا أَكْثَرَ مِنْ ثَلَاثِ لَيَالٍ، نمبر 18762)
وجه: (4) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الْحَرْبِيُّ إِلَيْنَا بِأَمَانٍ عَنْ زِيَادِ بْنِ حُدَيْرٍ قَالَ: كَتَبْتُ إِلَى عُمَرَ فِي أُنَاسٍ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْحَرْبِ يَدْخُلُونَ أَرْضَنَا أَرْضَ الْإِسْلَامِ فَيُقِيمُونَ قَالَ: فَكَتَبَ إِلَيَّ عُمَرُ: إِنْ أَقَامُوا سِتَّةَ أَشْهُرٍ فَخُذْ مِنْهُمُ الْعُشْرَ، وَإِنْ أَقَامُوا سَنَةً فَخُذْ مِنْهُمْ نِصْفَ الْعُشْرِ (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنَ الذِّمِّي إِذَا اتَّجَرَ فِي غَيْرِ بَلَدِهِ، وَالْحَرْبِي إِذَا دَخَلَ بِلَادَ الْإِسْلَامِ بِأَمَانٍ، نمبر 18771)
اصول: حربی قلبی اعتبار سے نجس ہے، دائمی قیام خطرے سے خالی نہیں لہذا پورے سال قیام کی اجازت نہیں ہے۔
اصول: جو دارالحرب بھاگ گیا تو اس کا مال اور اس کی جان حلال ہے۔
Book of Siyar. And when a harbi enters our land with aman, he is not allowed to stay in our land for a year, and the Imam says to him: 'If you complete the year, I will impose jizyah on you.' So if he stays a year, jizyah is taken from him, he becomes a dhimmi, and he is not allowed to return to the land of war. Proofs: (1) The verse for establishing 'and when a harbi enters our land with aman': O you who believe, the polytheists are unclean, so let them not approach the Sacred Mosque after this year. (2) The hadith... (Ibn Abbas) he ordered three things, he said: Expel the polytheists from the Arabian Peninsula. (3) The saying of the Companion: Umar ibn al-Khattab set for the Jews, Christians, and Zoroastrians in Madinah a stay of three days for trade and needs, and none of them may stay more than three nights. (4) The saying of the Companion: Ziyad ibn Hudayr said: I wrote to Umar about people from the war land entering our land of Islam and staying. He wrote back: If they stay six months, take a tenth from them; if they stay a year, take half a tenth. Principles: A harbi is ritually impure in essence, permanent stay is not free from risk, therefore permission for a full year's stay is not given. Principles: Whoever flees to Dar al-Harb, his wealth and his life become permissible.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Siyar presents the Hanafi ruling regarding a harbi (non-Muslim enemy combatant) who enters Dar al-Islam with an aman (safe conduct). The matn states that such a person is not permitted to stay for a full year; if he does, the Imam imposes jizyah upon him, he becomes a dhimmi (protected non-Muslim citizen), and he loses the right to return to Dar al-Harb. The author then provides four proofs (wujuh) to support this ruling. The first proof is the Quranic verse (9:28) declaring polytheists as najas and prohibiting their approach to the Sacred Mosque after the year of Hajj, which implies that their stay in the entire Dar al-Islam is similarly restricted. The second proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered the expulsion of polytheists from the Arabian Peninsula, indicating that non-Muslims cannot permanently reside there. The third proof is the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab, who limited the stay of dhimmis in Madinah to three days, showing that the restriction is not limited to the Haram but applies elsewhere. The fourth proof is another narration from Umar through Ziyad ibn Hudayr, where he imposes a tax (ushr) on harbis who stay in Muslim lands for six months or a year, similar to jizyah. The Urdu commentary adds that a harbi is inherently impure and his permanent stay poses a security risk, and that if he escapes to Dar al-Harb, his life and property become permissible (i.e., no longer protected).

Key Terms
حربي (harbi): A non-Muslim who is not under a peace treaty and resides in Dar al-Harb (land of war).
أمان (aman): Safe conduct granted by a Muslim to a harbi, guaranteeing temporary protection.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim citizen of an Islamic state who pays jizyah in exchange for protection and religious freedom.
جزية (jizyah): A tax imposed on non-Muslims in an Islamic state in return for their protection and exemption from military service.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what happens if a harbi who entered with aman stays in Dar al-Islam for a complete year?
A) He is allowed to return to Dar al-Harb freely.
B) He becomes a dhimmi and must pay jizyah.
C) His aman is renewed for another year.
D) He is expelled immediately.

Key Takeaway
A harbi with aman cannot stay a full year; completion of the year triggers dhimmi status and jizyah, backed by Quran, Hadith, and Sahabi practice.

Ruling on Harbi Returning to Dar al-Harb and Status of His Property
Al-Quduri's ruling with proofs from hadith and tabi'i saying.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a harbi who returns to Dar al-Harb and explain how the Khaybar hadith serves as the proof through qiyas.

Core Idea
Return to Dar al-Harb breaks the aman: the harbi's life becomes permissible and his property becomes fay'.

This passage continues the discussion of a harbi who entered Dar al-Islam with aman. Al-Quduri rules that if such a person returns to Dar al-Harb, his protection is nullified and his left property is at risk. The ruling is derived from the Prophet's treatment of the Khaybar Jews who breached their pact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a harbi who had previously received aman (safe passage) and then returns to Dar al-Harb. The ruling: his blood becomes mubah (permissible to kill) and any property he left in Dar al-Islam (deposit or debt) becomes at risk; if captured or killed, the deposit becomes fay' and debts nullified.
Note that the return itself, not a formal declaration, triggers the loss of protection.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The key proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar about the Battle of Khaybar (Sunan Abi Dawud). The Jews hid a skin, breaching their pact, and the Prophet nullified their covenant, making their lives and property permissible.
This hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted for legal derivation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith establishes that violating a pact nullifies the protection. By qiyas, returning to Dar al-Harb after receiving aman is a violation of the aman contract, so the same ruling applies: protection ends and the person becomes a legitimate target.
The illa (effective cause) is the breach of trust/pact.
4
Note the cross-madhhab nuance
While Hanafis consider the act of returning itself sufficient, some other schools may require an explicit declaration of renouncing aman. The practical consequence (thamarah) is that Hanafis treat the property as fay' immediately upon capture, without further proceedings.
This nuance is noted in the hanafi_position_box.
5
Apply the ruling to subtypes of property
The matn specifies two types: wadi'ah (deposit) and dayn (debt). Both become fay' (state property) if the harbi is captured/killed. The deposit, previously a trust (amanah), loses its protected status.
The Urdu commentary adds: if a dhimmi settles in Dar al-Harb, he becomes harbi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ عَادَ إِلَى دَارِ الْحَرْبِ وَتَرَكَ وَدِيعَةً عِنْدَ مُسْلِمٍ أَوْ ذِمِّيٍّ أَوْ دَيْنًا فِي ذِمَّتِهِمْ فَقَدْ صَارَ دَمُهُ مُبَاحًا بِالْعَوْدِ ١٨ وَمَا فِي دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ مِنْ مَالِهِ عَلَى خَطَرٍ فَإِنْ أُسِرَ أَوْ ظَهَرَ عَلَى الدَّارِ فَقُتِلَ سَقَطَتْ دُيُونُهُ وَصَارَتِ الْوَدِيعَةُ فَيْئًا
وَجْهُ (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ فَإِنْ عَادَ إِلَى دَارِ الْحَرْبِ وَتَرَكَ وَدِيعَةً عِنْدَ مُسْلِمٍ عَنْ مُعَاذٍ، «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لَمَّا وَجَّهَهُ إِلَى الْيَمَنِ أَمَرَهُ أَنْ يَأْخُذَ مِنْ كُلِّ حَالِمٍ - يَعْنِي مُتَلِمًا - دِينَارًا، أَوْ عَدْلَهُ مِنَ المُعَافِرِيِّ ثِيَابٌ تَكُونُ بِالْيَمَنِ» (سُنَنُ أَبِي دَاوُدَ، بَابٌ فِي أَخْذِ الْخِزْيَةِ، نمر 3038)
وَجْهُ (2) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَاتَلَ أَهْلَ خَيْبَرَ، فَغَلَبَ عَلَى النَّخْلِ وَالْأَرْضِ، وَأَخْاَهُمْ إِلَى قَصْرِهِمْ، فَصَاخَوهُ عَلَى أَنَّ لِرَسُولِ اللهِ الصَّفْرَاءَ، وَالْبَيْضَاءَ، وَالخُلْقَةَ، وَهُمْ مَا حَمَلَتْ رِكَابُهُمْ، عَلَى أَنْ لَا يَكْتُمُوا، وَلَا يُغَيِّبُوا شَيْئًا، فَإِنْ فَعَلُوا فَلَا ذِمَّةَ لَهُمْ، وَلَا عَهْدَ فَغَيَّبُوا مَسْكًا حِيَيَ بْنِ أَخْطَبَ... فَوَجَدُوا الْمَسْكَ، فَقَتَلَ ابْنَ أَبِي الْحَقَيْقِ وَسَبَى نِسَاءَهُمْ وَذَرَارِيَّهُمْ (سُنَنُ أَبِي دَاوُدَ، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي حُكْمِ أَرْضِ خَيْبَرَ، نمر 3006)
وَجْهُ (3) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ سُئِلَ عَطَاءٌ عَنِ الرَّجُلِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الذِّمَّةِ يُؤْخَذُ فِي أَهْلِ الشِّرْكِ، وَقَدِ اشْتَرَطَ عَلَيْهِمْ أَنْ لَا يَأْتِيهِمْ، فَيَقُولُ: لَمْ أُرِدْ عَوْنَهُمْ، فَكَرِهَ قَتْلَهُ إِلَّا بِبَيِّنَةٍ فَقَالَ لَهُ بَعْضُ أَهْلِ الْعِلْمِ: «إِذَا نَقَضَ شَيْئًا وَاحِدًا مِمَّا عَلَيْهِ فَقَدْ نَقَضَ الصُّلْحَ» (مُصَنَّفُ عَبْدِ الرَّزَّاقِ، بَابُ الْمُشْرِكِ يَأْتِي الْمُسْلِمَ بِغَيْرِ عَهْدٍ، نمر 9654)
وَجْهُ (4) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ عَنْ أَبِيهَا أَسْمَرَ بْنِ قَالَ: أَتَيْتُ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَبَايَعْتُهُ، فَقَالَ: «مَنْ سَبَقَ إِلَى مَاءٍ لَمْ يَسْبِقْهُ إِلَيْهِ مُسْلِمٌ فَهُوَ لَهُ» (سُنَنُ أَبِي دَاوُدَ، بَابٌ فِي إِقْطَاعِ الْأَرَضِينَ، نمر 3071)
وَجْهُ (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَا فِي دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ مِنْ مَالِهِ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَاتَلَ أَهْلَ مُضَرِّسٍ
اصول: ذمی دار لحرب میں گھر بنالے، رہائش پزیر ہو جائے تو حربی کا حکم لگے گا ذمی نہ رہے گا۔
And if he returns to Dar al-Harb, leaving a deposit with a Muslim or a dhimmi, or a debt in their liability, then his blood becomes permissible by that return (18). And what is in Dar al-Islam of his property is at risk. So if he is captured, or (the Muslims) prevail over the land and he is killed, his debts are nullified and the deposit becomes fay'. Proofs: (1) The hadith of Mu'adh that the Prophet sent him to Yemen ordering him to take from every adult a dinar or its equivalent. (2) The hadith of Ibn Umar about the battle of Khaybar... they hid a skin of Huyayy ibn Akhtab... so the Prophet killed Ibn Abi al-Huqayq and took women and children. (3) The saying of the tabi'i: Ata was asked about a dhimmi who helps polytheists despite a pact; he said if he breaks any condition, the pact is broken. (4) The hadith of Asmar that the Prophet said: Whoever gets to water not preceded by a Muslim, it is his. (5) The hadith of Ibn Umar about the battle of Mudarris. Principle: If a dhimmi builds a house in Dar al-Harb and takes residence, he takes the ruling of a harbi and is no longer a dhimmi.
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of the harbi who had entered with aman. The matn states that if such a person returns to Dar al-Harb, his blood becomes permissible (i.e., he may be killed without liability) by virtue of his return. Any property he left behind in Dar al-Islam, such as a deposit (wadi'ah) or a debt (dayn) owed to him, becomes at risk. If he is captured or killed by Muslims, his debts are nullified and the deposit becomes fay' (spoils for the Muslim treasury). The author then provides several proofs. The first proof (from Mu'adh) establishes the principle of taking jizyah from non-Muslims, which underpins the contractual nature of aman. The second proof (from the Khaybar incident) shows that violation of a pact nullifies protection and justifies killing. The third proof (from Ata) reinforces that any breach of a pact invalidates the entire agreement. The fourth proof (about water) illustrates that prior claim creates ownership, analogically supporting that return to Dar al-Harb forfeits claims. The fifth proof (from Ibn Umar about Mudarris) is fragmentary but supports the same point. The Urdu commentary adds that if a dhimmi settles in Dar al-Harb and makes a home there, he is treated as a harbi and loses his dhimmi status.

Key Terms
وديعة (wadi'ah): A deposit left for safekeeping with a Muslim or dhimmi.
فَيْء (fay'): Spoils taken from non-Muslims without battle, or property of harbis that becomes state property.
ذمة (dhimma): The covenant of protection and responsibility between the Islamic state and its non-Muslim subjects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what happens to a deposit (wadi'ah) left by a harbi in Dar al-Islam if he returns to Dar al-Harb and is subsequently captured or killed?
A) It remains with the depositary and must be returned to his heirs.
B) It becomes fay' (state property).
C) It is given to the Muslim who holds the deposit.
D) It is destroyed.

Key Takeaway
A harbi who returns to Dar al-Harb after having aman loses his protection, and any property he left behind becomes fay' upon his capture or death.

Ruling on a Dhimmi Who Returns to Dar al-Harb
Ruling with proofs on dhimmi returning to Dar al-Harb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a dhimmi who returns to Dar al-Harb and identify the consequences for his property left in Dar al-Islam.

Core Idea
A dhimmi who returns to enemy territory loses protection: his blood becomes mubah and his property becomes fay'.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on a dhimmi who abandons his covenant by returning to Dar al-Harb. The matn of al-Quduri lays out the consequences for his property left behind, citing several proofs from the Sunnah and the practice of the Companions. The ruling underscores the principle that allegiance and residence determine legal status in jihad rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The dhimmi returns to Dar al-Harb. The ruling: his blood becomes permissible (mubah) and his property in Dar al-Islam is at risk.
The property is not immediately fay'; it becomes fay' only if he is captured or killed.
2
Locate the proofs (adillah)
The passage cites four proofs: two hadith (from Mu'adh and Ibn 'Umar), a saying of 'Ata', and a hadith on water rights. Identify which proofs directly support the ruling.
The Khaybar hadith and 'Ata''s statement are most directly relevant.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each proof connects to the ruling. The Khaybar hadith shows that violating treaty conditions nullifies protection; 'Ata' explicitly states that breaking one condition breaks the peace.
The Mu'adh hadith establishes the jizyah obligation, implying the covenant binds the dhimmi.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The ruling is mukhtalaf fih; other schools may have different conditions for nullification. The Hanafi position relies on the principle of allegiance.
This ikhtilaf is over specific conditions, not the basic rule.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The matn represents Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi position. Later Hanafi scholars uphold it.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded here.

Source Text

فَإِنْ عَادَ إِلَى دَارِ الْحَرْبِ وَتَرَكَ وَدِيعَةً عِنْدَ مُسْلِمٍ أَوْ ذِمّي أَوْ دَيْنًا فِي ذِمَّتِهِمْ فَقَدْ صَارَ دَمُهُ مُبَاحًا بِالْعَوْدِ. وَمَا فِي دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ مِنْ مَالِهِ عَلَى خَطَرٍ، فَإِنْ أُسِرَ أَوْ ظَهَرَ عَلَى الدَّارِ فَقُتِلَ سَقَطَتْ دُيُونُهُ وَصَارَتْ الْوَدِيعَةُ فَيْئًا. 
ادلته: 
- وجه (1): الحديث عن معاذ: «أن النبي ﷺ لما وجهه إلى اليمن أمره أن يأخذ من كل حالم - يعني محتلما - دينارا أو عدله من المعافري» (سنن أبي داود، باب في أخذ الجزية، 3038).
- وجه (2): الحديث عن ابن عمر: أن النبي ﷺ قاتل أهل خيبر، فصالحهم على أن لهم الصفراء والبيضاء والحلقة، على أن لا يكتموا ولا يغيبوا شيئا، فإن فعلوا فلا ذمة لهم ولا عهد، فغيبوا مسكا، فقتل ابن أبي الحقيق وسبى نساءهم (سنن أبي داود، باب ما جاء في حكم أرض خيبر، 3006).
- وجه (3): قول عطاء: سئل عن الرجل من أهل الذمة يؤخذ في أهل الشرك وقد اشترط عليهم أن لا يأتيهم، فكره قتله إلا ببينة، فقال: «إذا نقض شيئا واحدا مما عليه فقد نقض الصلح» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب المشرك يأتي المسلم بغير عهد، 9654).
- وجه (4): الحديث عن أسماء بنت [؟] أن النبي ﷺ قال: «من سبق إلى ماء لم يسبقه إليه مسلم فهو له» (سنن أبي داود، باب في إقطاع الأراضين، 3071).
- وجه (1) أخرى: الحديث عن ابن عمر أن النبي ﷺ قاتل أهل [؟] (الحديث مكرر).
اصول: ذمی دار لحرب میں گھر بنالے، رہائش پزیر ہو جائے تو حربی کا حکم لگے گا ذمی نہ رہے گا۔
If he returns to Dar al-Harb and leaves a deposit with a Muslim or a dhimmi, or a debt in their liability, then his blood becomes permissible by [his] return. And whatever property of his is in Dar al-Islam is at risk: if he is captured or [the enemy] prevails over the land and he is killed, his debts fall away and the deposit becomes fay'. Its proofs: - Proof (1): The hadith from Mu'adh: 'When the Prophet ﷺ sent him to Yemen, he ordered him to take from every adult (meaning pubescent) a dinar or its equivalent from al-Ma'afiri garments' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on taking jizya, no. 3038). - Proof (2): The hadith from Ibn 'Umar: The Prophet ﷺ fought the people of Khaybar and made peace with them on condition that they give the yellow, white, and weapons, and that they hide nothing, and if they do so, there is no covenant for them; they hid a leather bag, so he killed Ibn Abi al-Huqayq and captured their women (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on ruling of Khaybar, no. 3006). - Proof (3): The saying of 'Ata': He was asked about a dhimmi who is taken among the polytheists, and they had stipulated that he not go to them; he disliked killing him without evidence, but he said: 'If he violates one thing of what he agreed to, he has broken the peace' (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on a polytheist coming to a Muslim without treaty, no. 9654). - Proof (4): The hadith from Asma' bint [?] that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Whoever precedes to water that no Muslim has preceded him to, it is his' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on granting lands, no. 3071). - Another Proof (1): The hadith from Ibn 'Umar that the Prophet ﷺ fought the people of [؟] (repeated). Principle: If a dhimmi builds a house in dar al-harb and takes up residence, the ruling of a harbi applies; he will no longer be a dhimmi.
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school on the status of a dhimmi (a non-Muslim subject of the Islamic state) who returns to dar al-harb (the territory of war) and leaves behind property in dar al-Islam. The passage is a ruling with multiple proofs. The author begins by stating the legal consequence: such a person's blood becomes mubah (permissible to shed) because of his return to enemy territory. This means he loses the protection of his covenant and is treated as a harbi (enemy combatant). Furthermore, any property he left in dar al-Islam—whether a deposit (wadi'ah) or a debt owed to him—becomes at risk. If he is captured or killed (by the Muslims), his debts are cancelled and his deposited property becomes fay' (spoils acquired without fighting) for the Muslim treasury. The passage then provides four proofs: two hadith (from Mu'adh and Ibn 'Umar), a saying of the tabi'i 'Ata', and another hadith about water rights. The 'Ata' narration clarifies that violation of any condition of the peace treaty nullifies the covenant. The Urdu principle at the end summarizes: if a dhimmi builds a house in dar al-harb and resides there, he becomes a harbi and loses his dhimmi status. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi principle that residence and allegiance determine legal status in jihad rulings.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under the protection of the Islamic state, paying jizyah.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under the rule of non-Muslims with whom a state of war exists.
فيء (fay’): Property acquired from the enemy without fighting (e.g., through peace treaty or abandonment).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) They are returned to his heirs.
B) They become fay’ for the Muslim treasury.
C) They are divided among the Muslims who captured him.
D) They are given to the imam for distribution.

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi who returns to Dar al-Harb forfeits his covenant: his blood becomes permissible, and if captured or killed, his property in Muslim lands becomes fay' for the treasury.
