Fay’: Property Acquired without Fighting – Definition and Distribution in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling on the disposition of property acquired from the enemy without fighting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish fay' from ghanimah and explain the Hanafi ruling on its distribution, citing the Quran, hadith, and the statement of al-Thawri.

Core Idea
Fay’ is not spoils—it belongs to the whole community, wajib to spend on public welfare.

This passage from al-Quduri defines a critical fiscal category in Islamic law: wealth obtained from non-Muslims without military engagement. Understanding the difference between fay' and ghanimah is essential for grasping how the Hanafi school structures state finance. The text presents multiple proofs, including a Qur’anic verse and two hadiths, to establish that fay' must be spent on the general welfare of Muslims, exactly like kharaj (land tax).

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition of fay'
Locate in the text the statement: 'Whatever property of the people of war that Muslims acquire without fighting.' This is the core definition: peaceful acquisition.
The Arabic phrase 'bighayri qital' is key.
2
Contrast fay' with ghanimah using al-Thawri's explanation
Al-Thawri explicitly differentiates: ghanimah is taken by force and distributed (khums to imam, 4/5 to fighters); fay' comes from peace treaties and is entirely for public welfare.
This distinction determines distribution rules.
3
Analyze the primary proof: Qur'an 59:7
The verse lists categories (Allah, Messenger, relatives, orphans, needy, wayfarer). The Hanafi school interprets this as the public treasury, not private distribution.
The imperative structure indicates obligation (wujub).
4
Examine the additional proofs (hadiths)
The hadith from Abu Hurayrah divides towns: those taken by force vs. by peace. The hadith from Ibn 'Abbas about Najran shows a practical example of fay' (jizyah payment).
These reinforce the separation from ghanimah.
5
Derive the Hanafi ruling on expenditure
The text concludes: fay' is spent on the welfare of Muslims (masalih al-muslimin) like kharaj. The imam has discretion but must not distribute it as spoils.
This is the mufta bihi position in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَا أَوْجَفَ عَلَيْهِ الْمُسْلِمُونَ مِنْ أَمْوَالِ أَهْلِ الْحَرْبِ بِغَيْرِ قِتَالٍ صُرِفَ فِي مَصَالِحِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ كَمَا يُصْرَفُ الْخَرَاجُ. 
ادلته: 
- وجه (1): قول الثوري: «الفيء والغنيمة مختلفان، أما الغنيمة: فما أخذ المسلمون فصار في أيديهم من الكفار، والخمس في ذلك إلى الأمير يضعه حيث أمر الله، والأربعة الأخماس للذين غنموا الغنيمة، والفيء: ما وقع من صلح بين الإمام والكفار في أعناقهم وأرضهم وزرعهم، وفيما صوحوا عليه مما لم يأخذه المسلمون عنوة ولم يحوزوه ولم يقهمروا عليه، حتى وقع فيهم صلح» قال: «فذلك الصلح إلى الإمام يضعه حيث أمر الله» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الغنيمة والفيء مختلفان، 9778).
- وجه (2): الآية: {مَا أَفَاءَ اللَّهُ عَلَى رَسُولِهِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْقُرَى فَلِلَّهِ وَلِلرَّسُولِ وَلِذِي الْقُرْبَى وَالْيَتَامَى وَالْمَسَاكِينِ وَابْنِ السَّبِيلِ} (الحشر: 7).
- وجه (3): الحديث عن أبي هريرة: «أيما قرية افتتحها الله ورسوله فهي لله ورسوله، وأيما قرية افتتحها المسلمون عنوة فخمسها لله ورسوله وبقيتها لمن قاتل عليها» (سنن البيهقي، باب من رأى قسمة الأراضي المغنومة، 18393).
- وجه (4): الحديث عن ابن عباس: «صالح رسول الله ﷺ أهل نجران على ألفي حلة، النصف في صفر والباقي في رجب يؤدونها إلى المسلمين» (سنن أبي داود، باب في أخذ الجزية، 3041).
اصول: مال فئی جو قتال کے بغیر دشمن سے ملے وہ بیت المال میں جمع ہو کر مصلحت امت پر خرچ ہو گا۔
And whatever property of the people of war that Muslims acquire without fighting is spent on the welfare of the Muslims, just as the kharaj is spent. Its proofs: - Proof (1): The saying of al-Thawri: "Fay' and ghanimah are different. As for ghanimah: it is what Muslims take from the disbelievers and come into their hands; the khums of that goes to the imam to place where Allah commanded, and the remaining four-fifths are for those who gained the ghanimah. As for fay': it is what comes from a peace treaty between the imam and the disbelievers regarding their persons, land, and crops, and what they made peace upon without the Muslims taking it by force or conquering it, until a peace was made with them." He said: "That peace is up to the imam, to place it where Allah commanded." (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on ghanimah and fay' differ, no. 9778). - Proof (2): The verse: "Whatever Allah has restored to His Messenger from the people of the towns, it is for Allah and for the Messenger and for the near of kin and orphans and the needy and the wayfarer" (al-Hashr: 7). - Proof (3): The hadith from Abu Hurayrah: "Any town that Allah and His Messenger have taken is for Allah and His Messenger; and any town that the Muslims take by force, its khums is for Allah and His Messenger, and the rest is for those who fought for it." (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on division of conquered lands, 18393). - Proof (4): The hadith from Ibn 'Abbas: "The Messenger of Allah ﷺ made peace with the people of Najran on two thousand garments, half in Safar and the rest in Rajab, which they would pay to the Muslims." (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on taking jizyah, 3041). Principle: Property of fay', which is obtained from the enemy without fighting, will be collected in the bayt al-mal and spent on the welfare of the ummah.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage defines the category of fay’ and its distribution, contrasting it with ghanimah (spoils taken by force). It is a ruling with proofs, including the statement of al-Thawri (a tabi'i scholar), a Qur'anic verse, and two hadith. The author states that property acquired from the enemy without fighting—such as through a peace treaty or abandonment—is spent on the general welfare of Muslims, in the same manner as kharaj (land tax). Al-Thawri's explanation clarifies the distinction: ghanimah is taken by force and distributed with khums (one-fifth) to the imam for public expenditures and four-fifths to the fighters; fay’, on the other hand, comes from a peace settlement and is entirely at the discretion of the imam to spend on the public interest. The Qur'anic verse (al-Hashr:7) is cited as the primary basis, indicating that such property is for Allah, the Messenger, relatives, orphans, needy, and travelers—effectively the public treasury. The hadith from Abu Hurayrah reinforces that towns taken by peace (opened by Allah and His messenger) are not distributed like ghanimah. The hadith from Ibn 'Abbas provides a practical example: the peace treaty with Najran specified a fixed annual payment (jizyah), which is fay’. The Urdu principle summarizes: fay’ is collected in the bayt al-mal and spent on the welfare of the Muslim community.

Key Terms
فيء (fay’): Property acquired from non-Muslims without military action, such as through peace treaties, abandonment, or jizyah.
غنيمة (ghanimah): Spoils taken from the enemy by force during battle.
خراج (kharaj): Land tax imposed on conquered lands that remain in the hands of the original owners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how is fay’ (property acquired without fighting) to be used?
A) Divided among the fighters who participated in the campaign.
B) Given entirely to the imam for his personal use.
C) Spent on the welfare of Muslims, similar to kharaj.
D) Returned to the original owners.

Key Takeaway
Fay’ is property from the enemy without fighting; the Hanafi school rules it wajib to spend on public welfare, distinguishing it from ghanimah which is distributed to fighters.

Ruling on the Male Apostate's Property and Transactions
Rules for the property and transactions of a male apostate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the distribution of a male apostate's property and explain the concept of suspended (mawquf) transactions.

Core Idea
Apostate's property is suspended, not lost: earnings during Islam go to heirs, apostasy earnings become fay'.

This passage from al-Quduri’s Kitab al-Siyar addresses a critical area of the law of apostasy (riddah) in the Hanafi school. Understanding what happens to an apostate’s property—whether earned during Islam or during apostasy—and the status of his transactions is essential for applying the correct legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the different scenarios
The passage covers four outcomes: death in apostasy, killing in apostasy, joining dar al-harb, and return to Islam. Each triggers different property and transaction rulings.
2
Analyze the division of property
Property earned during Islam goes to Muslim heirs. Property earned during apostasy becomes fay' (public treasury). Debts are paid from the corresponding earnings.
3
Examine the concept of suspended transactions (mawquf)
Sales, purchases, and other dealings during apostasy are neither valid nor void directly; they are suspended (mawquf). Their final status depends on the apostate's fate.
4
Trace the dalil
The ruling is based on hadith commanding execution of apostates and companion rulings on inheritance. The hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him' (Bukhari 6922) establishes the separation from property.
5
Note the mufta bihi and cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi position as stated in the matn is the mufta bihi. Other schools may differ on whether transactions are void ab initio rather than suspended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ قُتِلَ أَوْ مَاتَ عَلَى رِدَّتِهِ انْتَقَلَ مَا اكْتَسَبَهُ فِي حَالِ إِسْلَامِهِ إِلَى وَرَثَتِهِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَكَانَ مَا اكْتَسَبَهُ فِي حَالِ رِدَّتِهِ فَيْئًا وَإِنْ لَحِقَ بِدَارِ الْحَرْبِ مُرْتَدًّا وَحَكَمَ الْحَاكِمُ بِلَحَاقِهِ عَتَقَ مُدَبَّرُهُ وَأُمَّهَاتُ أَوْلَادِهِ وَنُقِلَ مَا اكْتَسَبَهُ في حَالِ الْإِسْلَامِ إِلَى وَرَثَتِهِ مِنْ الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَتُقْضَى الدُّيُونُ الَّتِي لَزِمَتْهُ فِي حَالِ الْإِسْلَامِ مِمَّا اكْتَسَبَهُ فِي حَالِ الْإِسْلَامِ وَمَا لَزِمَهُ مِنْ الدُّيُونِ فِي حَالِ رِدَّتِهِ فَإِنْ أَسْلَمَ عَادَتْ أَمْلَاكُهُ عَلَى حَالِهَا وَمَا بَاعَهُ أَوْ اشْتَرَاهُ أَوْ تَصَرَّفَ فِيهِ مِنْ أَمْوَالِهِ فِي حَالِ رِدَّتِهِ مَوْقُوفٌ فَإِنْ أَسْلَمَ صَحَّتْ عُقُودُهُ وَإِنْ مَاتَ أَوْ قُتِلَ أَوْ لَحِقَ بِدَارِ الْحَرْبِ بَطَلَتْ وَإِذَا عَادَ الْمُرْتَدُّ بَعْدَ الْحُكْمِ بِلَحَاقِهِ إِلَى دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ مُسْلِمًا فَمَا وَجَدَهُ فِي يَدِ وَرَثَتِهِ مِنْ مَالِهِ بِعَيْنِهِ أَخَذَهُ
And if he is killed or dies in his apostasy, what he earned during his Islam transfers to his Muslim heirs. And what he earned during his apostasy is fay'. And if he reaches the abode of war as an apostate and the judge rules on his joining, his mudabbar and umm walads become free. And what he earned during Islam is transferred to his Muslim heirs. And the debts that were incumbent on him during Islam are paid from what he earned during Islam, and what debts were incumbent on him during his apostasy [are paid from what he earned during apostasy?]. Then if he becomes Muslim, his properties return to their state. And what he sold or bought or transacted in from his wealth during his apostasy is suspended. If he becomes Muslim, his contracts are valid. And if he dies or is killed or reaches the abode of war, they become void. And when the apostate returns after the ruling of his joining to the abode of Islam as a Muslim, then whatever he finds in the hands of his heirs of his property in kind, he takes it.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Siyar of al-Quduri states the Hanafi rulings on the property of a male apostate (murtadd). The passage is a ruling statement with supporting proofs (proofs are provided in the original text but omitted here for brevity). The ruling covers several scenarios: First, if the apostate is killed or dies in apostasy, his wealth earned during Islam (as a Muslim) goes to his Muslim heirs, while wealth earned during apostasy becomes fay' (booty) for the Muslim treasury. Second, if the apostate joins dar al-harb and a judge rules that he has effectively joined, his mudabbar (slave promised freedom upon master's death) and umm walad (slave mother of his child) become free (because they are now under enemy jurisdiction). His debts incurred during Islam are paid from his Islamic earnings; debts incurred during apostasy are paid from apostasy earnings. If he later returns to Islam, his ownership of properties reverts. His transactions during apostasy are suspended (mawquf): if he returns to Islam they become valid, but if he dies, is killed, or joins dar al-harb they become void. If after the judge's ruling of lahaq he returns as a Muslim, he may reclaim any of his specific property still in the hands of his heirs. All these rulings are based on the principle that apostasy does not immediately terminate ownership but suspends it pending final outcome.

Key Terms
مُرْتَدّ (murtadd): A person who was Muslim and then rejects Islam, either by speech, action, or belief.
فَيْء (fay'): Booty taken from the enemy without fighting, or property of an apostate that becomes public treasury.
مَوْقُوف (mawquf): Suspended; a legal act that is neither valid nor void immediately, but depends on a future condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the transactions (sales, purchases) of a male apostate during his apostasy if he later returns to Islam?
A) They are void from the beginning.
B) They become valid.
C) They remain suspended indefinitely.
D) They become void only if he dies.

Key Takeaway
The key takeaway is that the Hanafi school treats an apostate's property and transactions as suspended (mawquf), not automatically void, preserving the possibility of validation upon return to Islam.

Female Apostate and Banu Taghlib Taxation
Two rulings: female apostate's transactions valid; Banu Taghlib tax double zakat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a female apostate's transactions and explain the special tax on Banu Taghlib, citing the proof from 'Umar's practice.

Core Idea
Female apostate retains property capacity; Banu Taghlib pay double zakat, not jizyah.

This passage from al-Quduri presents two distinct rulings from Hanafi fiqh: the legal capacity of a female apostate to transact during her apostasy, and the unique tax treatment of the Christian Arab tribe Banu Taghlib. Both rulings are grounded in the practice of the Sahaba, particularly 'Umar ibn al-Khattab. Understanding these rulings clarifies Hanafi positions on apostasy and the treatment of non-Muslim subjects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Locate the two separate legal statements in the text: first, the ruling on the female apostate (murtaddah); second, the ruling on the Christians of Banu Taghlib. Note the language: 'jaza tassarrufha' (her transaction is valid) and 'yu'khadhu min amwalihim di'f ma yu'khadhu min al-muslimin min al-zakat' (double the zakat of Muslims).
These are independent rulings, but connected by the theme of taxation/legal capacity.
2
Analyze the female apostate ruling
The text states that if a female apostate transacts in her wealth during apostasy, the transaction is valid (jaza). Contrast this with a male apostate, whose transactions are suspended (mawquf) according to Hanafi fiqh. Ask: why the difference? The basis: a female apostate is imprisoned, not killed, so her property rights are not suspended.
The proof is not explicitly given here but is derived from the general principle that legal capacity is not stripped from a female apostate.
3
Analyze the Banu Taghlib ruling
The text specifies that from the Christians of Banu Taghlib, double the zakat rate of Muslims is taken (2.5% → 5%). It is also taken from their women, but not from their children. This is a special jizyah-like tax, but called 'zakat' to avoid degrading their Arab status. The proof is the practice of 'Umar, who made a pact with them on these terms.
This is a unique Hanafi ruling; other schools may treat Banu Taghlib like other dhimmis.
4
Contextualize within Hanafi fiqh
Note that the passage also mentions kharaj and gifts from harbis to the imam, which go to the public treasury. The focus is on the imam's authority to collect these funds. The rulings reflect Hanafi reliance on the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs (especially 'Umar) as a source of law.
The dalil here is 'amal al-sahaba (practice of the Companions), considered hujjah in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْمُرْتَدَّةُ إِذَا تَصَرَّفَتْ فِي مَالِهَا فِي حَالِ رِدَّتِهَا جَازَ تَصَرُّفُهَا وَنَصَارَى بَنِي تَغْلِبَ يُؤْخَذُ مِنْ أَمْوَالِهِمْ ضِعْفُ مَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنْ الْمُسْلِمِينَ مِنْ الزَّكَاةِ وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْ نِسَائِهِمْ وَلَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنْ صِبْيَانِهِمْ شَيْءٌ وَمَا جَبَاهُ الْإِمَامُ مِنْ الْحَرَاجِ وَمِنْ أَمْوَالِ نَصَارَى بَنِي تَغْلِبَ وَمَا أَهْدَاهُ أَهْلُ الْحَرْبِ إِلَى الْإِمَامِ
And the female apostate, if she transacts in her wealth during her apostasy, her transaction is valid. And the Christians of Banu Taghlib, there is taken from their wealth double what is taken from the Muslims of zakat, and it is taken from their women, and nothing is taken from their children. And what the imam collects from kharaj and from the properties of the Christians of Banu Taghlib and what the people of war gift to the imam...
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage contains two distinct rulings. First, regarding a female apostate (murtaddah): unlike a male apostate whose transactions are suspended, her transactions during apostasy are immediately valid (jaza). The reason, as explained in Hanafi fiqh, is that a female apostate is not killed but imprisoned, so her property rights are not suspended; she retains full capacity to deal with her wealth. Second, the ruling on the Christians of Banu Taghlib: they are a Christian Arab tribe. By a pact made with 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, they pay double the zakat rate of Muslims (i.e., 5% annually instead of 2.5%). This tax is also taken from their women (adult females) but not from their children. This is a special tax (jizyah-like but called zakat) to avoid treating them as zimmis. The passage also mentions that what the imam collects from kharaj (land tax) and from Banu Taghlib properties, and gifts from harbis (enemy) to the imam, all become part of the public treasury. The text provides proofs from the practice of 'Umar and hadith on kharaj.

Key Terms
مُرْتَدَّة (murtaddah): A female who apostatizes from Islam.
نَصَارَى بَنِي تَغْلِب (Nasara Banī Taghlib): The Christian Arab tribe of Banu Taghlib, who were given special tax terms by 'Umar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the tax rate for wealth of the Christians of Banu Taghlib?
A) Same as the jizyah on other dhimmis.
B) Double the zakat rate of Muslims.
C) Half the zakat rate of Muslims.
D) A fixed amount per person regardless of wealth.

Key Takeaway
A female apostate retains full legal capacity to transact, and Banu Taghlib's unique tax of double zakat is based on 'Umar's pact.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
8 min
The Inviolability of Rebels' Children and Property
Ruling with proofs from hadith and athar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings that rebels' children are not enslaved and their property is not divided, and explain the evidence from hadith and the practice of Ali.

Core Idea
Rebels' children and property are protected to encourage repentance.

This passage from al-Quduri's Kitab al-Siyar presents the unique legal treatment of rebels (bughat) in Hanafi fiqh. Unlike enemy combatants (harbi), rebels are Muslims with grievances; thus their children are not taken as captives, and their property is not distributed as spoils. The Imam holds their wealth until they repent. The proofs include a hadith from Ibn Mas'ud and the actions of Ali at the battles of Basra and Siffin. Understanding these rulings helps distinguish the fiqh of rebellion from the fiqh of war.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key rulings
Read the first part of the text (before the proofs). State the rulings on children, property, and weapons. Note that children are not to be enslaved, property is not to be divided, but weapons may be used if needed.
The text uses 'لا تسب هم ذرية' and 'لا يقسم هم مال'.
2
Examine the hadith proof
Locate the hadith from Ibn Mas'ud. Understand that the Prophet's prohibition on following retreating rebels, killing captives, and finishing off wounded implies the protection of their families and possessions.
This hadith establishes a general principle of restraint.
3
Analyze the practice of Ali
Review the reports of Ali's actions at Basra and Siffin. Note that he specifically refrained from enslaving children and only took weapons and mounts from captives to prevent their return to battle.
Ali's sunna is a key evidence for Hanafi rulings.
4
Differentiate from regular warfare
Contrast these rulings with the treatment of enemy combatants (harbi) where children and property can be taken as spoils. Understand that the difference arises from the intention to encourage rebels to repent and return to the community.
The goal is reintegration, not annihilation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ السّير
وَلَا تُسْبَ هُمْ ذُرِّيَّةٌ ، وَلَا يُقَسَّمُ هُمْ مَالٌ وَلَا بَأْسَ أَنْ يُقَاتَلُوا بِسِلَاحِهِمْ إِنْ احْتَاجَ الْمُسْلِمُونَ إِلَيْهِ . وَيَحْبِسُ الْإِمَامُ أَمْوَالَهُمْ وَلا يَرُدُّهَا عَلَيْهِمْ وَلا يُقَسَمُهَا حَتَّى يَتُوبُوا فَيَرُدُّهَا عَلَيْهِمْ وَأَمَرَهُ أَنْ يَنْزِلَ حَيْثُ يَرْحَلُونَ ، وَلَا يُحَرِّكُهُمْ وَلَا يُهَيِّجُهُمْ ، فَإِنْ قَتَلُوا وَأَفْسَدُوا فِي الْأَرْضِ فَاسْطُ عَلَيْهِمْ وَقَاتِلْهُمْ ، وَإِنْ هُمْ لَم يَقْتُلُوا وَلَمْ يُفْسِدُوا فِي الْأَرْضِ فَدَعْهُمْ يَسِيرُونَ، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه مَا ذُكِرَ فِي الْخَوَارِجِ، نمبر 37908)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ بَدَءُونَا قَاتَلْنَاهُمْ حَتَّى نُفَرِّقَا عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم لِعَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْن مَسْعُودٍ: «يَا ابْنَ مَسْعُودٍ، أَتَدْرِي مَا حُكْمُ اللَّهِ فِيمَنْ بَغَى مِنْ هَذِهِ الْأُمَّةِ؟» قَالَ ابْنُ مَسْعُودٍ اللَّهُ وَرَسُولُهُ أَعْلَمُ، قَالَ: «فَإِنَّ حُكْمَ اللَّهِ فِيهِمْ أَنْ لَا يُتْبَعَ مُدْبِرَهُمْ وَلا يُقْتَلُ أَسِيرُهُمْ، وَلا يُذَفَّفُ عَلَى جَرِيحِهِمْ، (مستدرك للحاكم، كِتَابُ قِتَالِ أَهْلَ الْبَغْيِ وَهُوَ آخِرُ الْجِهَادِ، نمبر 2662 سنن بيهقي، بَابُ أَهْلِ الْبَغْيِ إِذَا فَاءُوا لَمْ يُتْبَعُ مُدْبِرُهُمْ، وَلَمْ يُقْتَلْ أَسِيرُهُمْ، وَلَمْ يُجْهَزْ عَلَى جَرِيحِهِمْ، وَلَمْ يُسْتَمْتَعْ بِشَيْءٍ مِنْ أَمْوَالِهِمْ، نمبر 16747
وجه:(۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلَا تُسْبَيَ فَهُمْ ذُرِّيَّةٌ \ أَمَرَ عَلِيٌّ هِ مُنَادِيَهُ فَنَادَى يَوْمَ الْبَصْرَةِ: لَا يُتْبَعُ مُدْبِرٌ، وَلَا يُذَفَّفُ عَلَى جَرِيحٍ، وَلَا يُقْتَلُ أَسِيرٌ، وَمَنْ أَغْلَقَ بَابَهُ فَهُوَ آمِنٌ، وَمَنْ أَلْقَى سِلَاحَهُ فَهُوَ آمِنْ، وَلَمْ يَأْخُذْ مِنْ مَتَاعِهِمْ شَيْئًا، سَأَلَ عَلِيًّا رضي الله عنهما عَنْ سَبْيِ الذُرِّيَّةِ، فَقَالَ : " لَيْسَ عَلَيْهِمْ سَيِّ، إِنَّمَا قَاتَلْنَا مَنْ قَاتَلَنَا، قَالَ: لَوْ قُلْتَ غَيْرَ ذَلِكَ خَالَفْتُكَ،(سنن بيهقي، بَابُ أَهْلِ الْبَغْيِ إِذَا فَاءُوا لَمْ يُتْبَعْ مُدْبِرُهُمْ وَلَمْ يُقْتَل أَسِيرُهُمْ الخ، نمبر 16749/16747)
وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلَا يُقَسَّمُ فَهُمْ مَالٌ وَلَا بَأْسَ أنْ يُقَاتَلُوا بِسِلَاحِهِمْ \ قَالَ: كَانَ عَلِيٌّ إِذَا أُتِي بِأَسِيرٍ صِفِّينَ أَخَذَ دَابَّتَهُ وَسِلَاحَهُ ، وَأَخَذَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَعُودَ ، وَخَلَّى سَبِيلَهُ، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، بَابُ مَا ذُكِرَ فِي صِفِّينَ، نمبر 37859)
د وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيَحْبِسُ الْإِمَامُ قَالَ: كَانَ عَلِيٌّ إِذَا أُتِيَ بِأَسِيرِ صِفِّينَ أَخَذَ دَابَّتَهُ وَسِلَاحَهُ، وَأَخَذَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَعُودَ ، وَخَلَّى سَبِيلَهُ ، مصنف ابن شيبه، بَابُ مَا ذُكِرَ فِي صِفِّينَ، 37859)
وجه : (٢) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيَحْبِسُ الإِمَامُ أَمْوَاهُمْ الَمَّا جِيءَ عَلِيٌّ بِمَا فِي عَسْكَر أَهْلِ النَّهْر قَالَ: مَنْ عَرَفَ شَيْئًا فَلْيَأْخُذْهُ ، قَالَ : فَأُخِذَتْ إِلَّا قَدْرًا، قَالَ: ثُمَّ رَأَيْتُهَا بَعْدُ قَدْ أُخِذَتْ،(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، ما ذُكِرَ فِي الحَوَارِج، نمبر 37830)
Book of Siyar. Do not take their children as captives, and do not divide their property. There is no harm in fighting them with their weapons if the Muslims need them. The Imam holds their wealth, does not return it to them, nor divide it until they repent, then he returns it to them. He is commanded to encamp where they encamp, not to provoke them nor excite them. If they kill and cause corruption in the land, then attack them and fight them. If they do not kill and do not cause corruption in the land, then let them go. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, section on Khawarij, no. 37908) Aspect (2): The hadith for proof: 'If they start (fighting) we fight them until we separate.' From Ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah said to Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: 'O Ibn Mas'ud, do you know the judgment of Allah concerning those who rebel from this ummah?' Ibn Mas'ud said: 'Allah and His Messenger know best.' He said: 'The judgment of Allah concerning them is that their retreating should not be followed, their captive should not be killed, and their wounded should not be finished off.' (Mustadrak al-Hakim, Book of Fighting the People of Transgression, no. 2662; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on People of Transgression when they desist... no. 16747) Aspect (1): Statement of the Companion for proof: 'Do not take their children as captives' – Ali commanded his herald to proclaim on the Day of Basra: 'Do not follow anyone who retreats, do not finish off the wounded, do not kill a captive, whoever closes his door is safe, whoever lays down his arms is safe.' And he did not take anything from their goods. He was asked about taking the children as captives, and he said: 'There is no enslavement for them; we only fought those who fought us.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on People of Transgression when they desist... no. 16749/16747) Aspect (1): Statement of the Companion for proof: 'Their property is not divided, and there is no harm in fighting them with their weapons' – He said: When Ali was brought a captive from Siffin, he took his mount and weapon, made him promise not to return, and let him go. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, chapter on what was mentioned concerning Siffin, no. 37859) Aspect (1): Statement of the Companion for proof: 'The Imam holds (their wealth)' – He said: When Ali was brought a captive from Siffin, he took his mount and weapon, made him promise not to return, and let him go. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, chapter on what was mentioned concerning Siffin, 37859) Aspect (2): Statement of the Companion for proof: 'The Imam holds their wealth' – When Ali was brought what was in the camp of the people of Nahr, he said: 'Whoever recognizes something, let him take it.' He said: 'Then it was taken except a measure.' He said: 'Then I saw it later that it had been taken.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, section on what was mentioned concerning the Khawarij, no. 37830)
Source pages p. 402

Commentary
This passage from the Kitab al-Siyar of al-Quduri presents the Hanafi rulings regarding rebels (khawarij/bughat) and provides hadith and athar proofs. The passage type is a ruling with proof. The author first states the rulings: rebels' children are not to be enslaved, their property is not to be distributed as spoils, but their weapons may be used if needed. The Imam is to hold their wealth until they repent. The passage then instructs the Muslim commander not to provoke rebels unless they initiate violence. The proofs follow: a hadith from Ibn Mas'ud (marfu'an) stating that rebels' retreating should not be followed, their captives not killed, and wounded not finished off. This is supported by the practice of Ali at the Battle of Basra and Siffin, where he did not enslave children or take property, only took weapons and mounts to prevent immediate return. The rulings emphasize that rebels are not treated as outright enemies of war (harbi); their children are protected, and their property is considered as subject to restitution upon repentance.

Key Terms
ذُرِّيَّةٌ (dhurriyyah): Children of rebels who are not to be taken as captives or enslaved.
مَالٌ (mal): Property of rebels that is not to be divided as spoils but held by the Imam.
سِلَاحٌ (silah): Weapons of rebels that may be used by Muslims if needed in battle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on taking the children of rebels (khawarij) as captives?
A) Permissible
B) Prohibited
C) Recommended
D) Obligatory

Key Takeaway
Rebels' children and property are not to be treated as spoils; they are protected to promote repentance and reintegration into the Muslim community.
